2007</p>
<p>A TEXT BOOK FOR THE COMMUNITY HEALTH NURSING -1 INCLUDING NUTRITION &amp; HYGIENE PSYCHOLOGY &amp; SOCIOLOGY.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="foreword">FOREWORD<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#foreword" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Despite great achievements in health and technology, the world is facing considerable health challenges. These include the growing population of poor who do not have access to basic health and social care, the rapid environmental changes and degradation of the environment, the economic recession and crises in parts of the world that affects the financing of health care, and the inability of technology to face the epidemics and deadly threats from malnutrition and diseases such as HIV/AIDS, malaria and tuberculosis. Over the years, hygiene has been considered to be responsible for more deaths than the bullets.</p>
<p>The concern of nurses is for people's health - its promotion, maintenance, and restoration. Together with midwives and health workers, constituting the majority of the qualified health workforce in most health systems, they play vital role in bringing about health awareness and the necessary changes to address these challenges.</p>
<p>Health promotion encompasses physical, mental and social well-being. Public health practitioners need to enhance their current professional work in health and social care, including counseling and therapy, preparedness for emergencies and crisis situations, and facilitating community involvement. Focus must be on the changing needs of the local communities that are each of them unique.</p>
<p>Neglect of public health also contributes to spiraling health costs. And not all people have access to medical care. Many tribal community people are in need of health and welfare service, but are not currently being served. More funds are needed for patient care, dental services, elderly services, health treatment, and community awareness programs regarding primary health care concepts and the contribution of nutrition to promoting health.</p>
<p>To address these issues, there is a need of political will and commitment of all the stakeholders including the local government, public health practitioners, professional groups, and the private sector.</p>
<p>However, all things considered, it is each individual who has to care for his physical, mental, and social health.</p>
<p>SWAMY BALANANDA,
GUNTUR.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preface">PREFACE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preface" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is accepted that studying of community health Nursing is essential for all vocational MPHW students. I pleased to bring out this book framed according to the syllabus of state intermediate vocational education.</p>
<p>The special features of this book are for the knowledge and understanding based on the chapters of Introduction to community health nursing; Nutrition, Hygiene, Psychology and sociology are extensively explained.</p>
<p>Matter is brief and in simple manner. This will definitely boost the confidence of the students in writing the end examinations. Here the topics are explained based upon scientific principles have changed rapidly in both medicine and science. At the end of each chapter, there are important questions, which are useful for the student. Glossary and reference books are to be mostly useful for both students.</p>
<p>I am confident that this book will definitely help to the students as well as teachers.</p>
<p>I wish to thanks to the Board Of Intermediate education vocational, Hyderabad for giving opportunity to write this book.</p>
<p>CH. SLEEVAMMA
JL IN MPHW(F)
GJC FOR GIRLS,
KHAMMAM.</p>

<li>Immunization</li>
<li>Detection and correction of defects</li>
<li>Prevention and early treatment of common ailments - common cold, indigestion, constipation, headache.</li>
<li>Health in the home</li>
<li>Home as a center for healthful living</li>
<li>Household measures for disposal of refuse, waste.</li>
<li>Latrines, sanitation, ventilation.</li>
<li>Safety in the home, common home hazards</li>
<li>Sanitation to animal sheds, insects and pets.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-a">SECTION - A<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-a" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-health-nursing">COMMUNITY HEALTH NURSING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-health-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-i">UNIT - I<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-i" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>"Health is Not mainly an issue of doctors, social services and hospitals. Health is an issue of social Justice.</p>
<p>There is no time to lose. We have the goal of "Health for all by 2000 AD". This is the call of the world health organisation. and India has taken up the challenge. Formerly, Health care has been for those living near enough to a hospital or a doctor in times of need and for those who could spend money for medicines and treatment. The great majority of people stayed in the village when sick and even today many suffer and die without proper help. Attempts have been made to meet the health needs of the people of India by means of primary health centres and the training of Auxiliary Nurse Midwives to go out from these centres to the homes of the people. The number of ANMS trained were never sufficient and more than half of them after training went to work in hospitals. In fact, their training was given mainly in the hospitals environment, with title experience and understanding of health needs of people, families and communities in rural areas</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="history-and-development-of-community-health-nursing">History and development of community Health Nursing:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-and-development-of-community-health-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Early history (Vedic period) Indus valley civilizations 3000 BC there were planned cities, houses built with public baths with drainage. People practiced proper environmental Sanitation 1400 BC Ayurveda and Siddha Systems of medicine come into existence which suggested development of comprehensive concept of health.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="post-vedic-period-600-bc-600-ad">Post Vedic Period - (600 BC - 600 AD)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#post-vedic-period-600-bc-600-ad" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Medical education was introduced in the ancient Universities of Taxila and Nalanda. During Budha period hospital system was developed for men and women and for animals. This was expanded during king Ashoka, Moghal Period (1000 AD) Unani Medicine which (Arabic system) was introduced through Greek medicine which has become a part of Indian medicine. Nursing and medicine are closely linked together. Nursing is regarded on the "Science of Care" and medicine as the "Science of Cure". As the science of cure, medicine</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing</p>
<p>is concerned with the diagnosis and treatment of illness. As the science of care, nursing is concerned with the care of people who are ill. The care and cure functions are complimentary; both are necessary and important aspects of health care for the people. Nurses were recruited in India for the first time in 1914, being attached to the Queen Alexandra's military nursing Service, which was founded by Florence Nightingale. In 1927, after the first world war, it was named as "Indian military Nursing Service". In 1871 the Govt of Madras started the training for nurses. During 1874 - 80. The Christian Mission Hospitals in India started training courses for nurses.</p>
<p>The Roman Catholic Nuns served as nurses in many Govt., Hospitals in India as well as in Hospitals run by religious orders.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="auxiliary-nurse-midwives">Auxiliary Nurse Midwives:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#auxiliary-nurse-midwives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The use of auxiliary Nursing Personal to ease the shortage of professional nurses put into practices in India. A 2 Yrs., course for the training of ANMS was first started in 1951 at St. Mary's Hospitals, Punjab. By 1962 there were 263 courses being offered in India. The ANM is trained in midwifery with same Nursing skills and orientation to public health and Family Planning. In 1977 the ANM Course was completely revised by the Indian Nursing Council and expanded to include Sociology, Health education and communication skills and decided to change ANMS to multipurpose workers and designate them as multipurpose health workers (Female). By 1978 there were 329 ANM Schools Functioning in the country. The existing ANMS are given an orientation course for a period of 10 weeks to give them additional knowledge and skills required by the multipurpose workers, and this programme is scheduled to be completed by 1983. In most states, the name of ANMS has been changed to Health Work (Female). It is envisaged that by the end of the VI five year plan. There will be one Health worker (F) for every 5,000 population in the country and they supervise the duties of ANMS. The ANMS are responsible for MCH and family planning work in an area of 5,000 population. She is most important person plays a role in rural health services are taken care of by specially trained multipurpose Health workers, male and female.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community">Community :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>Community means a group of people living in a certain locality such as a village, who have common interests. They meet and react with one another. They may have different interests also and not get on well with one another. Some are rich, others poor, some eat too much. Other may go hungry, some have power and influence and may like to give orders. Others have no power and suffer injusions.</p>
<p>The best kind of community is one in which every one cares about all the other members of the community. As a health worker you will be working with the community to help them in solving their problems especially to be more healthy in every way.</p>
<p><strong>Community Health:</strong></p>
<p>Community health includes the state of health of the members of the community, the problems effecting their health and the health care provided for the community. In community health work we help people to find out and think about their health problems and what can be done to improve the health of the whole community. Then we work together with the people and others in the health team to plan and carry out the problems of health care.</p>
<p><strong>B) QUALITIES AND FUNCTIONS OF COMMUNITY HEALTH NURSE: Qualities of Community Health (Worker) Nurse:</strong></p>
<p>As a health worker living and working in a community, you may at first feel a stranger. You will realise that people are watching what you do, what you say and how you react to them. If your appearance, words and behaviour displease or shock people, if you seem to be proud and different or have a habit of gossiping, then you will not be accepted by the community and can do no effective work there.</p>
<p>Student health worker need guidance and help in how to behave acceptably. There is a code of ethics for nurses published by the International Council of Nurses which May also guide the Health worker. In brief it is as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Have respect for life, dignity and rights of people, and serve them all without regard to race, religion, Colour, age, Sex, Politics or Social Status.</li>
<li>Have respect for the values, customs and spiritual beliefs</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing
4</p>
<p>of people.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Do not pass on personal information except to the right person.</li>
<li>Keep up a high standard of work and personal conduct.</li>
<li>Maintain a good relationship and Co-Operation with Co-workers in the health team, and community.</li>
</ol>
<p>Other points which are important for the health Workers to remember and practice are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Always be neat and clean in appearance, and walk with purpose and good posture. This will make you feel good and make a good impression on others.</li>
<li>Take special care of your own health of body and mind, and set a good example in your personal life and habits practice what you teach.</li>
<li>Be Cheerful and enthusiastic in your work, and keep a sense of humour.</li>
<li>Be disciplined in your use of time keep up punctuality cleanlines and order. Have respect for property other than your own.</li>
<li>Be obedient to your superior officers (with intelligence) and uphold their authority. Show them proper respect, and use correct channels of communication. Keep to service rules.</li>
<li>Try to understand other people and the reasons for what they do and say. Be tactful, patient, sympathetic and kind in your attitude to them.</li>
<li>Always be ready to help people with concern and care, but refuse to receive bribes.</li>
<li>Develop good friendships and interests apart from your work. Try to have a hobby and healthy relaxation.</li>
<li>Use every chance to go on learning, by reading books and journals and news papers. Also learn from people who can be helpful to you personally and to improve your work.</li>
<li>Be disciplined in your spiritual life, in order to have resources to help others in distress of spirit.</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions-of-community-health-nurse-worker">FUNCTIONS OF COMMUNITY HEALTH NURSE (WORKER) :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-community-health-nurse-worker" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The Community Health Nurse must be prepared to play a much wider role than is offered by her work in hospitals. There is much greater element of decision, making. Management skills, administration of programmes, teaching and acting as a team leader, as well as a member of the health team are all important perhaps the most crucial requirement is that the nurse must be prepared to learn from the people, and share leadership with them when it is necessary and to plan with them.</p>
<p>The functions of a community health nurse have been classified broadly under the following heads:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Administration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Communication.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nursing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teaching.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Research.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Administration  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⊬</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\nvdash</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6889em;"></span><span class="mrel amsrm">⊬</span></span></span></span></span>  The nurse is responsible for the day-to-day assignment of the nursing staff and supervision of these personnel. She provides direction and leadership to those whom she supervises. She is responsible for planning, implementation and evaluation of a practical plan of nursing administration with in the primary health centre and its associated sub centres.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Communication  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⊬</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\nvdash</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6889em;"></span><span class="mrel amsrm">⊬</span></span></span></span></span>  This involves ability to maintain good working relationship with members of the health team, related agencies and the community. She is a link between the patient, The family and the doctor. She participates in the staff and community meetings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nursing  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⊬</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\nvdash</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6889em;"></span><span class="mrel amsrm">⊬</span></span></span></span></span>  She provides comprehensive nursing care to individuals and families. This includes family care of the pregnant women, before, at the time of and after delivery, care of the new born, the premature, the infant, toddler, the school child, nutrition and family planning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Teaching  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>⊬</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\nvdash</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6889em;"></span><span class="mrel amsrm">⊬</span></span></span></span></span>  Knowledge and skills of methods of individuals and group teaching, preparation and use of simple teaching aids; training of dais and health workers; participation in student training programmes, if any.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Research :- These is probably far more research relevant to nursing than nurses realise. A good deal of knowledge derived from sociology and physiology is relevant to public health nursing, Viz., infant feeding and weaning, mother and child relation ship nursing needs and practices in the community, utilization of the existing nursing services, job analysis of nursing personnel in the team.</li>
</ol>
<p>C. FAMILY HEALTH SERVICES:</p>
<p>The term "Family Health" Covers a broad filed. It is one of the major activities of the world health organisation. It is devided into the following sub-areas:</p>
<p>a. Maternal child health services.
b. Family planning services.
c. Nutrition.
d. Health education.</p>
<p>The broad objectives of the family Health services are:</p>
<p>a. To reduce maternal and child mortality and morbidity rates.
b. Spacing of children.
c. To solve the problems of malnutrition at the family level and
d. To educate all members of the family in the basic requirements of healthy living.</p>
<p>(a) Maternal and Child Health.</p>
<p>The Need for MCH Services :-</p>
<p>There are 4 main reasons why mother and child health care must be given top priority in terms of providing health services:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Mothers &amp; Children below the age of 15 yrs., make up the majority of the population.</li>
<li>Mother and children constitute a "Special risk" or vulnerable group.</li>
<li>By improving the health of mothers and children we improve the health of the family &amp; community.</li>
<li>Ensuring child survival is a future investment for the family &amp; Community.</li>
</ol>
<p>Definition: According to who is "The promotive, preventure, Curative and rehabilitative care for mothers and childrens.</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives-of-mch-care">Objectives of MCH care:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives-of-mch-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Objectives of MCH care have been defined as below:</p>
<p>a). Reduction of Material, perinatal, infant and child mortality &amp; Morbidity.
b). Promotion of reproductive health.
c). Promotion of physical and Psychological development of the child and adolescent within the family. The ultimate objective of MCH care is life long health.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-role-of-nurses-in-mch-care">The Role of Nurses in MCH Care:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-role-of-nurses-in-mch-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The functions are explained under 4 headings as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Direct Care Provides:-
a) Antenatal Care i.e, Care of the women during Pregnancy.
b) Intranatal Care i.e, care of women at the time of delivery.
c) Post Natal care i.e, care of the women after delivery.
d) Child care: i.e., child survival activities i.e.,</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Immunization.</li>
<li>Promotion of breast feeding.</li>
<li>Growth monitoring.</li>
<li>Weaning.</li>
<li>Oral rehydration, when necessary</li>
<li>Birth spacing.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Health Communication and Education:</li>
</ol>
<p>The groups that require priority attention are.</p>
<ul>
<li>Dais.</li>
<li>Mothers.</li>
<li>Family.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Supervision and management :- The Community health Nurse will have to supervise the work of dais, ANMS&amp; Female workers.</li>
</ol>
<p>That means supervision of records, individual conference and counselling.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Research &amp; Evaluation influence the Welfare of mothers and Childrens:-</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-family-planning-services">(b) Family planning Services<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-family-planning-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Family planning being a national programme. The main role of a health worker in family planning services are:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Education and Counselling.</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing
8</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>To assist the Physician.</li>
<li>To promote the concept of small family and child spacing.</li>
<li>To spread information to all eligible couples about family planning methods.</li>
<li>To arrange for clinical and surgical services.</li>
<li>To ensure an adequate supply of Contraceptives.</li>
</ol>
<p>(D) SCHOOL HEALTH PROGRAMMES.</p>
<p>The school health services are important dimension of community. the reasons are large number in the total population, due to rapid growth and development, for early detection of nutritional and communicable diseases, due to group living.</p>
<p>Objectives are as follows:-</p>
<ol>
<li>The promotion of positive health.</li>
<li>The prevention of disease.</li>
<li>Early diagnosis, treatment and follow up of defects.</li>
<li>Awakening health conscious ness in children.</li>
<li>The provision of health full living.</li>
</ol>
<p>Aspects of school health services:-</p>
<p>Some aspects of school health services are as follows:-</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Health Appraisal of school children &amp; School personnel.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Remidial measures and follow up.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Prevention of communicable diseases.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health ful school environment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutritional Services.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>First aid and emergency care.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mental Health.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dental Health..</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eye health.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health Education.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Education of Handicapped children.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Proper maintenance and use of school health records.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health Appraisals:-</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Health Appraisal consists of periodic medical examination of school children and also teachers &amp; other school personal.</p>
<p>a) Periodic Medical Examination :- The School Health committee (1961) in India recommended medical examination for</p>
<p>9 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>the children who are newly entered in the school and there after every 4 years. The physical examination include - test for Vision, hearing, speech, blood, Urine, and faces.</p>
<p>b) Dental Examination :- Children are frequently suffer from dental diseases i.e., dental Carries. So at least once a year dental examination should be provided.</p>
<p>c) School Personal :- Teachers &amp; School personals are some of inspection like pulmonary tuberculosis. So they should also be examined.</p>
<p>c) Daily Morning Inspection :- Some of the Childs helps the teachers in detecting those children who need medical attention they are unusually flushed face.</p>
<ul>
<li>Any rash or spots.</li>
<li>Sore throat, rigid neck, nausea, vomiting, Red or water eyes.</li>
<li>Head ache, symptoms of acute cold, chills or fever, diarrhoea, body pain.</li>
<li>Head lice, skin infections like scabies etc.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Remedial Measures and Follow up:-</li>
</ol>
<p>After medical examination they should be given appropriate treatment and follow up. Special clinics should be conducted.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Prevention of Communicable Diseases:-</li>
</ol>
<p>This can be done by National Immunization programme. A record of all immunization should be maintained as part of school health records when the child leaves the school, the health record should be accompanied with him.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Healthful School Environment :-</li>
</ol>
<p>A healthful school environment is necessary for the child to grow best as emotionally, socially &amp; Personal healthy. The school authority should follow same standards towards location, site structure, classroom, furniture doors and windows, lighting, water supply, eating facilities and lavatory for the school.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Nutritional Services</li>
</ol>
<p>If the child is physically weak, he may be mentally weak also. So the child can't take full advantage of schooling. In India the nutritional disorders are malnutrition, Vitamin, Iron and Calcium</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing
10</p>
<p>dificencies. To prevent these disorders the midday school meal, applied nutrition programme, Vitamin A pro Phylaxis (Against blindness) programmes are implimentary.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>
<p>First aid and emergency care:-
The School teachers should be well trained during teacher training programme or in service training programmes in order to give first aid and emergency care for the pupils in school premises.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mental health:-
The School is the right place for shaping the child's behaviour and promoting mental health. The mental health of the child affects the physical health and learning process. Some of the school children problems are drug addiction, Juvenile sdeliquency and maladjustment. The school teacher plays an important role helping the child to attain positive mental health.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dental Health Service:-
A school health programmes for dental examination at least once in a year should be provided for the children to prevent dental diseases &amp; maintain dental hygiene.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Eye health Services :- The eye health services are to be provided in school to detect the refractive errors, treatment of squint, eye infections such as trachoma.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health Education :- In school Health services the most important element is health education towards environmental health, personal hygiene and family life.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Education of Handicapped children :- The ultimate goal is to assist the handicapped child and his family members and the child will be able to reach his maximum energy to lead a normal life as possible.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>School health Records :- In school, there should be a cumulative record for every student. Such record contain identifying data, i.e., date of birth, parent's name &amp; Address, past health history &amp; findings of physical examination &amp; Screening tests and record of services provided. These records are useful to analyse and evaluate the school health programmes &amp; provide a useful link between the school, home &amp; the community.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="role-of-the-community-health-nurse-in-the-school-health-programmes">Role of the Community Health Nurse in the school Health Programmes:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#role-of-the-community-health-nurse-in-the-school-health-programmes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>She is a counsellor and educator of health.</li>
<li>She plans the health talks to be given in school.</li>
<li>She provides guidance to the teachers and parents in matter of health.</li>
<li>She is the Co-ordinator and organiser of the school health programmes.</li>
<li>She helps and bridge the gap between what the child learns at school and practices at home.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="summary">SUMMARY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>The health worker in her role as a community health nurse needs to :
To know the history and development of community health Nursing in India.</li>
<li>Recognise her own self worth and that of others in the community.</li>
<li>Recognise the concept of health and community.</li>
<li>She should know the qualities and functions of community health nurse.</li>
<li>She plays a vital role in rendering MCH services.</li>
<li>Recognise the importance of school health programmes.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="questions">QUESTIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-ii">UNIT II<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-ii" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="planning-of-community-health-services">PLANNING OF COMMUNITY HEALTH SERVICES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#planning-of-community-health-services" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="the-process-of-nursing">The Process of Nursing:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-process-of-nursing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Nursing is seen as a process, which is described as including.</p>
<ol>
<li>Recognition :- This process is initiated by the recognition of a need. This is based on nursing observation, perception and judgement.</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Assessment :- Having recognized that a need exists, an assessment of the possible courses of action is made. The nurse must decide what action should be taken and whether she is capable of taking such action.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Intervention :- The nurse carries out activities decided upon as being most effective, in order to fulfill the recognised need. This phase contains all the tasks, procedures and practices which are performed by nurses. This is also the phase which has received the greatest attention both in the teaching and practice of nursing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evaluation :- The Nurse should know the effectiveness of the nursing intervention. It demands a similar range of perceptual and judgment skills as the recognition phase.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Organization :- It is the ability on the part of the nurse to organise nursing activity and to recognise the place of that activity in relation to others also involved in caring for the patient or client.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-basic-principles-which-include-in-community-health">THE BASIC PRINCIPLES WHICH INCLUDE IN COMMUNITY HEALTH<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-basic-principles-which-include-in-community-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Meet the Community:-</li>
</ol>
<p>It is first necessary to meet the community, in order to establish contact with community leaders, existing institutions.</p>
<p>Obtain consent of the local leaders for a base line survey of the health situation.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Identification (or Recognition) of health problems and needs various approaches may be used to identify community health problems and health needs they include:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Base - line survey.</li>
<li>Scrutinising the records of PHC and subcentre.</li>
</ul>
<p>13
Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ul>
<li>Specific questions regarding diseases common in the area.</li>
<li>Questions regarding births, deaths, disability, failure to work etc.,</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Setting Priorities among health problems:-
Four criteria are used for setting priorities among health problems.
a) Frequency with which the problems occurs (prevalance)
b) Seriousness of the problem for individuals and society.
c) Urgency of the problem.
d) Feasibility or susceptibility to control the problem within the financial resource limitations.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Planning and problem solving:-
Having recognized that a problem or need exists, the community health nurse must decide what action should be taken by the health team. Planning involves questions of setting objectives, and defining solutions to the problem.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Intervention of Implementation:-
The community health nurse carries out activities decided upon as being most effective in order to fulfil the recognized need.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evaluation:-
Evaluation will measure the extent to which the problem has been solved or the need met. Evaluation provides "Feed back" that can lead to programme modification, which will make the programme more effective.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>EQUIPMENT AND THEIR CARE
No home visit should be made without bag or kit. There are two separate kits.</p>
<p>One for deliveries (Delivery kit) and the other for general nursing and for prenatal and postnatal visits.</p>
<ol>
<li>Delivery Kit:-
The UNICEF kit is widely used for deliveries and is most suitable. The equipment is contained in an aluminum box or leather bag.</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing
14</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community-health-nursing-bag">COMMUNITY HEALTH NURSING BAG<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-health-nursing-bag" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="contents-of-nursing-bag">Contents of Nursing bag :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contents-of-nursing-bag" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<p>CARE OF THE EQUIPMENT</p>
<p>Regular care equipment is most important:</p>
<p>a) To prevent any possibility of errors infection by carrying contained articles form house to house.
b) To preserve the equipment for use as long as possible, and
c) To put it to the best possible use.</p>
<p>It should be remembered that the contents of the kit clean and in good condition but not necessarily Sterile. The following practices are recommended for different types of equipment.</p>
<ol>
<li>Bag :- If the bag is metal, it may be well washed with soap and water or boiled. If it is leather, it can be dried in the sun. The cotton lining must be clean and boiled &amp; replaced. As outer pocket can be made for keeping soap, towel and news paper.
b) Rubber goods :- All should be well washed in soap and water and rinsed. Tubes and catheters must be hung to drain. Plastic</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing
16</p>
<p>apron and sheeting should be hung in the shade to dry. Gloves should be dried with clean cloth both inside and outside and aired for a few hours. Rubber goods sterilized, put them in building water and boil them for 10 minutes.</p>
<p>c) Thermometer :- It should be soaked in an antiseptic solution, after washing with soap and water.</p>
<p>d) Bottles :- All bottles should emptied once a month, after the corks are removed. The bottles &amp; the corks should be boiled. clean, well marked labels should be affixed on the bottles giving the contents and dosage before filling them up.</p>
<p>e) Enamelware and Stainless Steel:-</p>
<p>Boil such ware for 20 mts., dry with a clean towel while the ware is still hot. In an emergency, it may be flamed (for this, rinse the bowl with a little spitit, then set fire to it with a match, being careful to do this only where there is no danger of setting fire to anything else).</p>
<p>f) Cord Ligatures:-</p>
<p>Remove the screw from the bottles and boil the bottles, the top and the threads for 20 mts. Then place threads into (Spirit) bottle &amp; use sterile forceps. Replace the cork and screw it fight.</p>
<p>g) Eye Antiseptic :-</p>
<p>If a silver Nitrate preparation is used. It must be renewed every week. It is very important that this bottle be well labelled. Now a days, freshly prepared lotion of pencillin 1/100 is generally used.</p>
<p>h) Instruments :- All instruments should be washed well with cold water after use, boiled for 20 mts., and dried with a clean towel before being replaced. Do not boil the scissors. These can be thoroughly washed with soap &amp; water, flamed or put in an antiseptic solution before use. A little oil can be added at the joints and blades after several uses to keep scissors sharpened unrusted.</p>
<p>i) Dry Dressing and swabs :- There are several methods of sterilizing dressing and swabs:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Arrangements can be made with the local hospitals or primary health centres to sterilize dressing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The swabs and dressings can be packed in small cotton bags</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>17 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>and then be placed in lined tins and auto claved in the usual way.</p>
<ul>
<li>Swabs can be baked in the tins. The bottom and top of the this must be perforated &amp; the lid let open during baking.
j) Blood - Pressure Machine :- The Cotton arm band should be seperated from the rubber bag and then washed &amp; Ironed in the usual way.
k) Stethoscope :- The chest piece may be immersed in soapy water or an antiseptic solution.</li>
</ul>
<p>The kit must be placed in a safe and clean place and not locked away, as it must be available at all times.</p>
<p>The delivery bag should be completely disinfected after each use. If the same bag is also used for nursing care, empty the bag completely and boil all boilable articles. Soak other equipment in antiseptic or soapy water. Wash the bag after completion, wash your hands well.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="records-and-reports">RECORDS AND REPORTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#records-and-reports" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Record and Reports are necessary to collect information useful for :</p>
<ol>
<li>Assessing the health of the community.</li>
<li>Collecting statistics, which are very important to health authorities.</li>
<li>Attention of the doctor or other members of the health team to specific needs of individuals or families, and for follow up services.</li>
<li>Information of Supervisors in assessing work done.</li>
<li>Assessing need for various drugs, transport etc., based on numbers and types of patients.</li>
<li>A tool for health education of individuals, families and communities.</li>
<li>Evaluating progress of the health programmes for replacing.</li>
</ol>
<p>Records to be maintained in the sub-centre include:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Village Records, with general information about each village.</li>
<li>family folders, and individuals health cards.</li>
<li>Eligible couple register and record of contraceptives distributed.</li>
<li>Maternal and child health records (Including antenatal care, child care, Nutrition and immunizations).</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing
18</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Records of distribution of iron and folic acid, also Vitamin A solution.</li>
<li>Vital events Register (Births and deaths).</li>
<li>Stock register for receipt, issue and balance of drugs, contraceptives, stationery etc.</li>
<li>Records of medical care and referrals.</li>
<li>Inventory of furniture, linen and equipment.</li>
<li>Records of meetings with Village Health Guides and dais, coworkers and supervisors.</li>
<li>Monthly reports and other periodic reports as and when required.</li>
<li>Daily dairy.</li>
<li>Maps, Charts, Graphs.</li>
</ol>
<p>HOW TO MAINTAIN RECORDS:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Record most be kept carefully and in clean conditions, safe from rats and insects.</li>
<li>It is important that records are not lost or mislaid. They are confidential and should be shown only to authorized persons.</li>
<li>Have a good system of filing, family folders, including records of individuals. Should be divided into localities and filed in order of house numbers. It is useful and also to have a register or index cards filed in alphabetical order of the heads of the families.</li>
<li>Records must be readily available and keep up to date.</li>
</ol>
<p>HOW TO WRITE RECORDS AND REPORTS:-</p>
<p>Remember that the delivery of health services is not complete until details are written up in the correct register or record. The last half an hour of each day's work should be reserved for completing the records.</p>
<p>In Writing records and Reports.:</p>
<ol>
<li>Write them promptly, and keep them up to date.</li>
<li>Write legibly, to be understood by others.</li>
<li>Keep sentences short and clear.</li>
<li>Be accurate and complete in important details.</li>
<li>Replace records in their proper place.</li>
<li>Consult your supervisor in case of difficulty in completing records and writing reports.</li>
</ol>
<p>19
Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="daily-dairy">Daily Dairy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#daily-dairy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is not practicable for the health worker to take registers and large record books while carrying out village visits, yet memory is unreliable. There fore a notebook called dairy isto be carried and used constantly and the information writen up in the proper record on return to the sub-centre.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-purpose-of-dairy-is">The purpose of dairy is :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-purpose-of-dairy-is" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>For immediate record of day's activities by the health worker.
Eg: Home Visits, Immunizations, Vitamin A administration, health teaching. given etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To record the name and address of persons to whom preliminary help has been given, and follow up to be done or referral if needed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>To record observations during village visits and matters needing to be reported to the supervisors or PHC authorities.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The information shoudl be neatly, correctly, and honestly written</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="monthly-report">Monthly Report<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#monthly-report" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At the beginning of each month the health worker has to complete the report forms and submit one copy to her supervisor keeping one copy in her file at the sub - centre.</p>
<p>The report includes detailed information of work carried out by herself, Villages Health Guides and Dais during the previous month, under the following readings.</p>
<ol>
<li>Immunization.</li>
<li>Communicalbe diseases.</li>
<li>Vital Events.</li>
<li>Family planning.</li>
<li>Maternal and chidl health (Including deliveries, care of the under five and nutrition supplmenets supplied)</li>
<li>Environmental Sanitation.</li>
<li>Treatment of minor elements (patient numbers, and referrals)</li>
<li>Health education activities</li>
<li>Home visits.</li>
<li>Other activities.</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing
20</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-ailmens-and-treatment">Common Ailmens and Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-ailmens-and-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Some of the common minor ailments which can be treated at home are listed below:</p>
<ol>
<li>Eye Infections:-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Eye infections cause burning pain in the eyes, waking of the eyes,</li>
<li>Light makes the pain work.</li>
<li>Sticky pus &amp; cause eye lids stick.</li>
<li>Eyes become red.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Find out the cause.</li>
<li>If the conditions acute clean the eyes carefully and put antibiotic eye drops or ointment,.</li>
<li>Close the eyes with soft bandage.</li>
<li>Refer the Patient without delay.</li>
<li>Give aspirin to relieve pain.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Ear Ache:-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>It is a common problem in children.</li>
<li>Trouble may be in the external ear or middle ear.</li>
<li>Middle ear infection is common and serious.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment :-</p>
<ul>
<li>Observe the ear for any discharge like watery or serious or pus.</li>
<li>Observe for any throat infections.</li>
<li>Examine for the pain.</li>
<li>Observe for other complaints like cold, too much wax.</li>
<li>Chronic condition may cause deafness.</li>
<li>So immediate appropriate care should be necessary.</li>
<li>Clean the Ear gently.</li>
<li>Instil antibiotic ear drops 4 times a day.</li>
<li>Give aspirin tablets for 3 days.</li>
<li>For children below 3 yrs., with middle ear infection can start pencillin injections and paracetamol tablets.</li>
<li>If any Foreign body or wax, should not try to treat the condition. This may worst the condition further.</li>
<li>Refer the case immediately to the hospital.</li>
</ul>
<p>21 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>COMMON COLD: -</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The patient has a watery discharge from the nose, with sneezing and itchig.</li>
<li>Symptoms come on suddenly and frequently.</li>
<li>The person may be allergic to dust, feathers, pollen or same food item..</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Give antihistamine tablets.</li>
<li>Tell the pateitn to try to observe what causes the allergic reaction and try to avoid contact with that item.</li>
<li>If there is no improvement, refer the patient.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Sinusitis:-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>This is a common Complaint of cold.</li>
<li>The patient is suffered severely with pain and tenderness in the bones just above or below the eyes.</li>
<li>Severe head ache.</li>
<li>Pain increase when the patient bends forward.</li>
<li>There may be thick mucus or pus in the nose.</li>
<li>Discharge smells badly.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment :-</p>
<ul>
<li>Tell the patient to take steam inhalations with Jandubam.</li>
<li>Decongestant tablets or nose drops for relief.</li>
<li>Aspirin or paracetamol to relieve pain.</li>
<li>If there is no improvement after 3 days, refer the patient.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Sore throat :-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Due to tonsilities throat may be red, and tonsils are swollen and pus discharge.</li>
<li>The patient feel difficult to swallow.</li>
<li>Fever and cough present.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment :-</p>
<ul>
<li>Give aspirin for 3 days to relieve pain and fever.</li>
<li>The voice should be rested and no smoking allowed.</li>
<li>If no improvement after 3 days, refer the patient.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="6">
<li>Cough :-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Cough is the most common symptom of respiratory disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>Community Health Nursing
22</p>
<p>Treatment</p>
<ul>
<li>If the cough is dry, steam inhalations and taking extra fluids will help to loosen mucus.</li>
<li>Expectorants may be given.</li>
<li>Advice the patient not to smoke, if he is smoker.</li>
<li>If suspect TB refer the patient.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="7">
<li>Chest pain :-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>May be occur for pneumonia, pleurisy, TB, and Fibrosis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment :-</p>
<ul>
<li>Give aspirin for 4 days, if no improvement refer patient for hospitals.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="8">
<li>Asthma :-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The patient feels dyspnea (Difficulty in breathing).</li>
<li>Wheezing.</li>
<li>Cough and Cyanosis.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment :-</p>
<ul>
<li>If not severe give ephedrine or theophylline.</li>
<li>Give a lot of liquids and steam inhalations.</li>
<li>Patient needs calm and quite environment.</li>
<li>Refer the case to the hospital.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="9">
<li>High blood Pressure :-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The blood pressure may raise due to several reasons.</li>
<li>If the patient is suffering continuously with high B.P.</li>
<li>The following symptoms should be observed.</li>
<li>Head ache.</li>
<li>Fatigue and dizziness.</li>
<li>Palpitations.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment :-</p>
<ul>
<li>The patient should take pills regularly in order to keep well.</li>
<li>Health teaching regarding same conditions.</li>
<li>If patient is over weight, he should lose weight by avoiding sweets, and fatty foods and eatingless staple foods.</li>
<li>Use Sunflower oil for cooking.</li>
<li>Use little or no salt in cooking or do not add salt to meals.</li>
<li>Don't take strong coffee.</li>
<li>Avoid smoking and alcohol.</li>
</ul>
<p>23 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ul>
<li>Learn to relax more and take moderate exercise.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="10">
<li>Anaemia :-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Causes includes hookwarm, malaria and malnutrition.</li>
<li>Patient may looks pale.</li>
<li>Patient Complaints of feeling tired and weak.</li>
<li>Giddy or faint.</li>
<li>Swelling of feet.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment :-</p>
<ul>
<li>Treat the patient according to the condition.</li>
<li>Health education regarding food i.e., green leafer vegetables, fresh vegetables, meat eggs, pulses, jaggery honey etc.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="11">
<li>Tooth Ache:-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Tooth ache may occur due to bad oral hygiene, infections, or in dental caries.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment :-</p>
<ul>
<li>If there is no cavity, no swelling or fever give saline or Potassium Permongate (Kmno₄) mouth wash and health teaching about oral hygiene.</li>
<li>If there is fever give aspirin and mouth washes 3 times a day. after 3 days if no improvement, refer to a doctor.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="12">
<li>Diarrhoea :-
It is a common complaint.</li>
</ol>
<p>The Causes are poisoning.</p>
<ul>
<li>Malnutrition.</li>
<li>Intestinal infections.</li>
<li>Intestinal furors.</li>
<li>Emotional disturbances.</li>
</ul>
<p>Treatment :-</p>
<ul>
<li>Treat for the dehydration without delay.</li>
<li>Give rehydration drinks frequently.</li>
<li>Plenty of liquids, which should be boiled and served warm.</li>
<li>Rehydration drinks are weak tea, rice water, soups, coconut water etc..</li>
</ul>
<ol start="13">
<li>Indigestions:-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>In this patient may feel stomach pain, heart - burn, flatulance,</li>
</ul>
<p>Community Health Nursing
24</p>
<p>regurgitation of fluid and constipation.</p>
<p><strong>Treatment</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Health teach should be given to patient regarding avoidance taking improper food.</li>
<li>Avoid eating quickly or swallowing without chewing the foods.</li>
<li>Avoid taking too spicy or fatly foods or too much alcohol.</li>
<li>Maintain to take balance diet according proper timings.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>14. Head ache :</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Pain may be present on forehead at temples, or back of the head or on sides. It is due to lack of sleep food, nervous tension worry, eye strain, indigestion, constipation, and menstruation.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Treatment :</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Rest in a quit, darkened room without food or drink for 2 hours.</li>
<li>Paracetamol or Aspirin with strong coffee or tea should be taken.</li>
<li>Massaging the back of neck, forehead and shoulders may release tension.</li>
<li>If other reasons treat for appropriate cause.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>15. Backache:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>You should not the sex, age, general health and occupation of the person.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Treatment :</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The patient should take complete rest on a firm bed. Local heat and aspirin may relieve pain for 4 days.</li>
<li>After 4 days if no improvement refer to doctor.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>16. Retension of Urine:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>This may occur due to fall from high place or urinary infections.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Treatment :</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Patient may listen the running tap sound or you can pour water on the lower abdomen showly by one feet height.</li>
<li>Refer the patient to doctor if no progress.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>17. Fever:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Fever may arise due to many reasons. It may be due to malaria, filaria, Polio, Typhoid or any other infections etc., signs and symptoms are body pains, Raise of temperature, Headache, Fatigue.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Treatment :</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Give paracetamol 500 Mg. 3 times a day for 4 days.</li>
</ul>
<p>25 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ul>
<li>Take rest.</li>
<li>Take plenty of fluids and fruit juices.</li>
<li>Soft diet should be taken fatigue.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">SUMMARY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Planning of Community Health Nursing Services are recognitions, assessment, intervention, evaluation, and organization.</li>
<li>The basic principles that are to be practiced are meet the Community, Identification of health problems, setting priorities, planning and implementation and evaluation.</li>
<li>The Community health Nurse should have delivery kit and home visiting kit along with her.</li>
<li>She should know the care of each equipment and maintain them properly.</li>
<li>She has to maintain the records and reports properly and promptly.</li>
<li>The health worker has to complete the monthly report forms &amp; submit one copy to her supervisor keeping one copy with her.</li>
<li>The health worker should know various minor disorder and their treatment. The various minor disorders are eye infections, earache, fever, cold, cough, back pain, retention of urine, etc.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-i">UNIT - I<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-i" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nutrition">NUTRITION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Man kind eats to satisfy the feeling of hunger. Nutrition plays an important role in the promotion and maintenance of health and in the prevention of disease in order to keep well our bodies, need nourishment.</p>
<p>Just as a plant will not grow without water sun shine and proper manure, human beings also need food stuffs of different kinds of nourish to the body. Malnutrition and under nutrition are the greatest international health problems of the present day. A sound knowledge of nutrition is therefore essential for all community health workers. Nutrition deals with the way in which the human body receives and uses all the substances or materials necessary for its growth and development and for keeping it is good condition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="definition">DEFINITION:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nutrition may be defined as the Science of food and its relation ship to health. It is concerned primarily with the part played by nutrients in body growth and development and maintenance.</p>
<p>The word nutrient or "food factor" is used for specific dietary constituents such as protiens, Vitamins and minerals. Dietics is the practical application of the principles of nutrition, it includes the planning of meals for the well and sick.</p>
<p>Good nutrition means "maintaining a nutritional status that enables us to grow well and enjoy good health.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="relation-of-nutrition-to-health">Relation of Nutrition to Health:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#relation-of-nutrition-to-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A person who does not eats the right foods or does not eat enough is malnourished and we call this a malnutrition also means that a child is less clever than he should be. The trouble may start even before birth if his mother does not have the right foods when she is pregnant. The malnourished child does not play but sits doing nothing. He is slow in learning to walk and talk. At school he is hungry, sleepy, dull and very slow to learn. The children are slow in passing mile stones.</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>Good nutrition is a basic component of health. The relation of nutrition to health may be seen from the following view points.:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Growth and development :-
Good nutrition is essential for the attainment of normal growth and development. Not only physical growth and development, but also the intellectual development, learning and behaviour are affected by malnutrition. Mal nutrition during pregnancy may affect the foetus resulting in still birth, premature birth and small for the dates babies. He is under weight because of not having enough of the kind of foods needed for growth. Good nutritions is also essential in adult life for the maintenance of optimum health &amp; efficiency. So nutrition affects the individuals health from birth to death.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Specific deficiency :-
Malnutrition is directly responsible for certain specific nutritional deficiency diseases. The commonly reported ones in India are Kwashiorkar, marasmus, blindness due to Vitamine A deficiency anaemia, beri-beri, goitre etc., Good nutrition therefore is essential for the prevention of specific nutritional deficiency diseases and promotion of health.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Resistance to infection ↑
Malnutrition predisposes to infections like tuberculosis. It also influences the course and out come of many clinical disorders. Infection, in turn, may aggravate malnutrition by affecting the food intake.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mortality and Morbidity ↑
The Indirect effects of Malnutrition on the community are even more striking a high general death rate, high infant mortality rate, high sickness rate and a lower expectation of life. Over nutrition, which is another form of malnutrition is responsible for obesity, diabetes, hypertension, cardiovascular and renal diseases, disorders of liver and gall bladder.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>More recent reports suggests that diet perhaps plays an important role in certain types of gasto intestinal cancers. It is now quite well acceptable that diet and certain diseases are interrelated.</p>
<p>Nutrition
28</p>
<p>Here is a comparison of the effects on people of good nutrition and malnutrition:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Good Nutrition</th><th>Mal Nutrition</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1. Correct weight for height and age</td><td>Weight too much or too little</td></tr><tr><td>2. Strong Muscles</td><td>Weak muscles.</td></tr><tr><td>3. Limbs straight.</td><td>Bow - legs or knock, knees.</td></tr><tr><td>4. Smooth, clear skin, mucous</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>membrances a good colour</td><td>Skin dry and rough, mucous</td></tr><tr><td>membranes pale</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>5. Healthy, bright eyes; clear sight</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>sight or loss of sight.</td><td>Eyes dull; night blindness; poor</td></tr><tr><td>6. Hearing good.</td><td>Hearing poor.</td></tr><tr><td>7. Breathing unobstructed.</td><td>Mouth breathing; adenoids.</td></tr><tr><td>8. Teeth well formed, and free from dental caries.</td><td>Uneven teeth; dental caries; spongy gums.</td></tr><tr><td>9. Tonsil clean and small</td><td>Tonsils enlarged, often sore.</td></tr><tr><td>10. Erect posture in sitting, standing and walking.</td><td>Round shouldered; twisted spine; protruding</td></tr><tr><td>abdomen.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>11. Nerves steady; expression calm and</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>cheerful, quick to learn.</td><td>Nervous, anxious, irritable,</td></tr><tr><td>slow to learn.</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>12. Plenty of energy</td><td>Tired and listless.</td></tr><tr><td>13. Good resistance to infections</td><td>Poor resistance to infections.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Relation of other factors of importance for nutritional status and health.</p>
<p>There are many other factors which affect the nutritional status of the health of the individual. The most important of which are:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Surface area of the body :-
The larger the surface area of the body in relation to bulk, the greater the use of (Nutrition) diet.</li>
</ol>
<p>Eg.:- A tall man lost his energy more when compare to short man with same weight. So the tall need and should eat more compare to short fat man of the same weight.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Sex:-
Energy using by the body surface area in men is more compare to the women. So the calorie requirement is also more in men than women.</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>40 calories per Sq. Metre per hour for men.
37 calories per sq. metre per hour for women.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Age:-
Growing children and adolescents need more diet than adults.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diseases
Some diseases, especially thyroid gland, may increase or decrease the basal metabolic rate. So the intake of food also increases or decreases in thyroid problem cases.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Under Prolonged or Chronic under nutrition the diet intake is decreased.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Psychological or emotional tension caused by worries or stress will increase the intake of diet.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>FUNCTION OF FOOD :-</p>
<ol>
<li>For growth or body building, and for repair of tissues protein foods mainly used.</li>
<li>To provide energy for doing work staple foods and fats.</li>
<li>To help the body to function properly and to protect from disease Vitamins and minerals.</li>
</ol>
<p>On the basis of the above funtions foods have been classified as:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Energy Yielding foods:- These are rich in carbohydrates and fat. Eg. Rice, wheat, potatoes, cereals, roots and tubers sugar, fats and oils.</li>
<li>Body building foods:- These are foods rich in protein, eg:- Milk, eggs, meat, liver, fish, pulses, oilseed cakes.</li>
<li>Protective Foods:- These are foods rich in Vitamins and minerals and proteins, eg:- Milk, green leafy vegetables. Protective foods are so called because they protect the body against infection, disease and ill health. It may be mentioned that diets in India are generally poor in protective foods.</li>
</ol>
<p>A balanced diet must contain foods from the above three groups:-</p>
<p>Constituents of Food:-
The dietary constituents of food are shown below:-</p>
<p>Nutrition
30</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-8592193f.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="dietary-constituents-of-food">Dietary Constituents of Food:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#dietary-constituents-of-food" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Proteins, fats and carbohydrates are called "Proximate Principles" or energy yielding foods. Together with water. They form the bulk of food. The human body has the following approximate.</p>
<p>Table-I
Composition of Human Body.</p>
