<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-foods">Classification of foods:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-foods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are many ways of classifying foods:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Classification by Origin
a) Foods of animal origin.
b) Foods of vegetable origin.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Classification by Chemical composition:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ol>
<li>Proteins</li>
<li>Fats</li>
<li>Carbohydrates</li>
<li>Vitamins</li>
<li>Minerals.</li>
</ol>
<ol start="3">
<li>Classification by predominant function:</li>
<li>Body building foods Eg. Milk, meat, poultry, fish eggs, pulses, groundnuts, etc.,</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Energy giving foods Eg. Cereals, Sugars, Roots, and tubers, fats and oils.</li>
<li>Protective foods:- Eg.: Vegetables, fruits, milk.</li>
</ol>
<p>4 Classification by nutritive value:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Cereals and millets.</li>
<li>Pulses (Legumes)</li>
<li>Vegetables.</li>
<li>Nuts and oilseeds.</li>
<li>Fruits.</li>
<li>Animal foods.</li>
<li>Fats and oils.</li>
<li>Sugar and jaggery.</li>
<li>Condiments and spices.</li>
<li>Miscellaneous foods.</li>

<p>Nutrients</p>
<p>Nutrients are organic and inorganic complexes contained in food. There are about 50 different nutrients which are normally supplied through the foods we eat. Each nutrient has specific functions in the body. Most natural foods contain more than one nutrient. These may be divided into</p>
<ol>
<li>Macronutrients:- These are proteins, fats and carbohydrates which are often called "Proximate Principles" because they form the main bulk of food. In the Indian dietary, they contribute to the total energy intake in the following proportions.</li>
</ol>
<table><thead><tr><th>Carbohydrates</th><th>65-80 %</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Fats</td><td>10 - 30 %</td></tr><tr><td>Proteins</td><td>7-15 %</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ol start="2">
<li>Micro Nutrients</li>
</ol>
<p>These are vitamins and minerals they are called "Micro Nutrients because they are required in small amounts which may vary from a fraction of a milligram to several grams.</p>
<p>Carbo hydrates</p>
<p>Energy foods and calories:-</p>
<p>Carbohydrates are composed of carbon, hydrogen, and</p>
<p>Nutrition
32</p>
<p>oxygen. A continued need of the body is for energy foods are fuel for the body to work rather like diesel is fuel for a bus to run. The harder you work, the more energy food you need, but even at rest. The bodystill uses fuel for breathing and for the heart beating. By burning fuel foods for energy, heat is also produced. In cold weather you can keep warm by exercise and eating more energy foods.</p>
<p>They are cheapest sources of energy and are the basis of our diet. Indian diets are characterised by excessive amounts of carbohydrates, providing as much as 90% of the required calories. In balanced diet, carbohydrates provide 50-60% of total calories taken in excess, the carbohydrates are converted into body fat.</p>
<p>The kind of staple food we eat depends on our habits and what is available, staple foods includes.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Cereals and grains:-
Wheat, made into bread, Chappati etc., Rice, jowar, maize, and ragi (The millets)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Starchy Vegetables, Potatoes, Sweet potato, and tapioca.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Starch fruits, banana, bread fruit,</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-2fcdb0c9.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<p>Sugars, honey and jaggery provide extra energy. These too are carbohydrates foods.</p>
<p>Body requirement :-
Carbo hydrates requirement for children 60-250 grams.</p>
<p>Adolescents 400 grms.
Men 300 - 700 grms.
Womens 240 - 540 grms.</p>
<p>Proteins</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>The word "Protein" means that which are essential for growth; for making different kinds of cells, tissues and organs of the human body. Proteins are composed of carbon, hydrogen, oxygen, nitrogen and sulphur in varying amounts. From this we can understand why pregnant women, nourishing mothers, babies and children all needs to have a lot of proteins in their diet. Those who are injured or have same disease which attacks body cells, need extra protein for repair of tissues that have been harmed. Every one needs protein because our bodies are made up of living cells whcih wear out and need replacing.</p>
<p>For Eg.:- The life of red blood cells is only about 120 days. New red blood cells need to be produced constantly.</p>
<p>Proteins differ from carbohydrates and fat in the respect that they contain nitrogen. Proteins are made up of simple substances called amino acids. These are building blocks of proteins.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="amino-acids">AMINO ACIDS:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#amino-acids" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are many different proteins and each one is made up of a group of about 100 amino acids. There are about 20 different kinds of aminoacids. we can think of them as beads of different colours joined together to make a chain or necklace (a protein). A protein is like a necklace rolled into a ball, but so small we cannot see it.</p>
<p>When we swallow a protein food, first the proteins separate, then the protein chain is broken and amino acids seperated. Inside the body the new proteins are formed by joining up the aminoacids in a different order, according to needs of the body.</p>
<p>The body can make some amoniacids out of others, and these are called "non essential" amino acids. About 8 aminoacids cannot be made by the body and must be taken in our food. These 8 are the essential aminoacids.</p>
<ol>
<li>Isoleucine</li>
<li>Leucine.</li>
<li>Lysine</li>
<li>Methionine</li>
<li>Phenylalanine.</li>
<li>Threonine</li>
<li>Trypto phane</li>
<li>Valine.</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
34</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-b0afb16b.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions">Functions:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>For growth and development :- They furnish the building material</li>
<li>For repair of body tissues and their maintenance:- It has been shown that the body proteins are constantly being broken down. They have to be replaced for which fresh protein make is required.</li>
<li>For synthesis of antibodies, enzymes and hormones: Antibodies, Enzymes and hormones contain protein. The body requires protein to produce them..</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources">Sources :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are 2 main sources of protein.</p>
<ol>
<li>Animal sources :- Milk, eggs, meat, fish, etc.,</li>
<li>Plant sources :- Pulses, cereals, nuts, etc., other chana, soyabean etc.,</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="proteins-content-of-some-foods">Proteins content of some foods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#proteins-content-of-some-foods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

Protein (G. per 100 gms. of food)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="animal-foods">Animal Foods:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#animal-foods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="others">Others:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#others" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="protein-requirements">Protein requirements:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protein-requirements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The requirements of proteins as per body weight. The
Indain Council of Medical Research in 1981, recommended 1.0 g
protien 1 kg. body weight for an Indian adult.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="fats">Fats:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fats" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fats are composed of Carbon, hydrogen and oxygen.
They are composed of smaller units called fatty acids. Some fats
such as ground nut oil, gingerly oil are liquid at room
temperature.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification-of-fats">Classification of Fats<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-fats" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Saturated fats. Eg. Animal Fats.</li>
<li>Un saturated fats. Eg. Vegetable oils and fats.
Current research indicate that excessive intake of satu-
rated fat is harmful to the body.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions">Functions:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fats Serve the following functions.</p>
<ol>
<li>Fats provide energy. A grame of fat provide 9 calories of
energy i.e., twice the number of calories from carbohydrates and
proteins.</li>
<li>Fats are carries of fat soluble vitamins. Eg.: Vitamine A,D,E,
and K.</li>
<li>Dietary fats supplies essential fatty acids are needed for
growth and maintenance of the integrity of the skin.</li>
<li>They maintain our body temperature.</li>
<li>Fats provide support for many organs in our body such as
heart, kidneys, intestine etc.</li>
<li>Foods containing fats are tasty.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources">Sources<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dietary fats are derived from 2 main sources.</p>
<ol>
<li>Animal sources :- These are Ghee, butter, fat of meat, fish
oils etc.</li>
<li>Vegetable sources :- Various vegetable oils such as ground
nut oil, ginger oil, mustard oil, cotton seed oil and coconut oil.</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
36</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fat-requirements">Fat requirements:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fat-requirements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Adult requires 20-60 grams 1 day.</p>
<p>Calories are used to measure energy. We use calories to measure how much energy is there in certain foods. We use calories also to measure how much energy a person needs (energy requirements)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nutrients-that-provide-calories-and-the-amounts-are-as-follows">Nutrients that provide calories, and the amounts are as follows:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrients-that-provide-calories-and-the-amounts-are-as-follows" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>One Gram of Carbohydrate provides 4 calories.
One Gram of proteins provides 4 calories.
One Gram of fats provides 9 calories.</p>
<p>Note that proteins are not including in "energy foods" because their main use is for body - building; what is left over from requirements for body building and repair can be used as fuel for energy.</p>
<p>Here are some foods, and the calorieis provided per 100 gms.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Cow's milk</th><th>65</th><th>potato</th><th>99</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Buffalo's milk</td><td>117</td><td>Wheat Bread</td><td>238</td></tr><tr><td>Jaggery</td><td>383</td><td>Wheat Flour</td><td>348</td></tr><tr><td>Honey</td><td>320</td><td>1 Chappati</td><td>124</td></tr><tr><td>Sesame seeds</td><td>564</td><td>Rice</td><td>345</td></tr><tr><td>Groundnuts</td><td>549</td><td>Ragi</td><td>331</td></tr><tr><td>Banana</td><td>153</td><td>Maize</td><td>342</td></tr><tr><td>Tapico</td><td>159</td><td>Bajra</td><td>360</td></tr><tr><td>Sweet Potato</td><td>132</td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Calorie Requirements (energy requirements)</p>
<p>A baby below 6 months needs 120 Calories per kg. of body weight per day.</p>
<p>A baby from 7 to 12 months needs 100 calories / Kg.</p>
<p>A Child 1-3 years old needs about 1200 calories per day.</p>
<p>A child 4-6 years old need about 1600 calories per day.</p>
<p>A child 7-9 years old needs about 1800 calories per day.</p>
<p>A child 10-12 year old needs about 2100 calories per day.</p>
<p>An Adolescent girl 13-19 and boy 13-15 - 2300 calories per day.</p>
<p>An adolescent boy 16-19 years need 3000 calories per day.</p>
<p>A man moderately active needs 2800 calories per day.</p>
<p>A woman an moderately active need 2200 calories per day.</p>
<p>A women who is pregnant need extra 300 calories per day.</p>
<p>A women who is lactating needs extra 500 calories per day.</p>

<p>39 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vitamins">Vitamins:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vitamins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vitamins are complex chemical substances they are required by the body in very small amounts. They donot yield energy like fats and carbohydrates. They are vital for the very survival of man. They protect the body against ill health, infection and disease. Since the body can not manufacture vitamins, they must be supplied through the diet. A well balanced diet almost meets the daily requirement of vitamins needed by the body.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="classification">Classification:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vitamins are classified into two broad groups as below:-</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Fat soluble vitamins.
a) Vitamin A or retinol.
b) Vitamin D
c) Vitamin E
d) Vitamin K</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Water soluble Vitamins.
a) Thiamine (Vitamin B1)
b) Ribo Flavin (Vitamin B2)
c) Nicotinic Acid (Niacin)
d) Pyridoxine (Vitamin B6)
e) Pentothenic Acid
f) Folic acid
g) Vitamin B12
h) Ascorbic acid (Vitamin C)</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vitamine-a-retinol">Vitamine A (Retinol)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vitamine-a-retinol" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a fat soluble vitamin. Its chemical name is "retinol" 8% of children between the ages 6 months and 6 years had vitamin A deficiency signs. In some countries, including India vitamin A is a major cause of preventable blindness.</p>
<p>If a person does not have enough vitamine A1 he gets night blindness, then dry eye, and may become blind.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions">Functions:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>It is needed for normal vision. and health of the eyes.</li>
<li>It is needed for health of the epithelial tissues (skin, mouth) of the</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition</p>
<p>body.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>It is connected with growth, especially skeletal growth.</li>
<li>It is anti - infective i.e, it protects the body against microbial infection.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-aefb9606.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources">Sources:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Animal Sources :- Butter, ghee, egg, milk, liver and fish are good sources of vitamin A.</li>
<li>Vegetables and fruits:- The cheapest sources of Vitamin A is green leafy vegetables such as spinach, amaranth, coriander, drum-stick-leaves.</li>
</ol>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources">Sources:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Liver, eggs, fish and milk.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="daily-requirement">Daily requirement:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#daily-requirement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>One microgram for adult.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="minerals">MINERALS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#minerals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At first minerals are in the rocks and are washed away from rocks into the soil. Minerals in the soil and water are absorbed by plants. Plants are eaten animals and human beings. There fore we get minerals from 3 sources water, plants and animals.</p>
<p>In our body contains 24 minerals, all of which must be obtained from foods we eat:</p>
<ol>
<li>Calcium:-</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>This mineral is present in large amount in our bones and teeth. It forms 1.5 -2 % of the body weight.</p>
<p>Daily requirement :-</p>
<ul>
<li>An adult requires 0.5 mg per day.</li>
<li>During pregnancy and lactation one gram per day is leaded.</li>
</ul>
<p>Functions:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Formation and maintenance of bones and teeth.</li>
<li>For coagulation of blood.</li>
<li>For regulation of Neuromuscular irritability and functioning of nerves.</li>
<li>Strengthen of capillary walls.</li>
<li>Contraction of heart muscles and skeletal muscles.</li>
</ol>
<p>Calcium needs to be in correct proportion with phosphorous. Vitamin D &amp; C are also needed for calcium to be fully used.</p>
<p>Sources:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Best source is milk.</li>
<li>Fish, eggs, green leafy vegetables and fruits.</li>
<li>Ragi, bajra, sesame seeds and wheat.</li>
<li>Small dried fish is good source.</li>
</ol>
<p>PHOSPHOROUS</p>
<ol>
<li>with calcium to form bones and teeth.</li>
<li>For brain and nerve formation.</li>
<li>For Carbohydrate and fat metabolism</li>
<li>For all cells in the body.</li>
</ol>
<p>Daily Requirements:-</p>
<p>300 - 1200 mg. per day.</p>
<p>Sources:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Most foods contain phosphorous especially milk, meat, fish, eggs, nuts, grains and green leaves.</li>
</ul>
<p>IRON</p>
<p>The total amount of iron present in the body is between 3-4 gms 75% is found in blood.</p>
<p>Function:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Iron is required for the formation of hemoglobin.</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
47</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>The central function of iron in the body is "Oxygen Transport". Daily Requirement:-
The Values are recommended in India are as follows:-
Adult man - 25 mg daily.
Adult women - 35 mg daily
Prgnancy - 40 mg daily
Lactation - 32 mg daily.</li>
</ol>
<p>Deficiency of Iron cause anaemia. Vitamin C helps in the absorption of iron.</p>
<p><strong>Sources:-</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>Animal Sources are :- liver, kidney, meat, egg, yolk.</li>
<li>Plant : Vegetables, cereals, pulses, dark green leafy vegetables, ragi, bajra, jaggary etc.,</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>SODIUM CHLORIDE</strong></p>
<p>We need salt for the fluids in the body and to help to regulate the fluid balance. People add salt to food to make it taste better, but there is enough salt already in most foods for the needs of the body. However, in hot weather a great deal of salt is lost from the body in sweat and extra salt should be taken to prevent muscle cramps and heat exhaustion. In the case of dehydration the salt as well as fluid lost must be replaced.</p>
<p><strong>POTASSIUM</strong></p>
<p>It is needed for</p>
<ol>
<li>Regulation of PH (Reaction) of tissue cell content.</li>
<li>Regulation of osmotic pressure of cell contains.</li>
<li>Relaxation of the heart muscle.</li>
</ol>
<p>Potassium is lost from the body in vomit and diarrhoea and so this mineral is often included in rehydration fluid. Potassium requirement is 1000 -2000 mg. daily.</p>
<p><strong>Sources:-</strong>
It is present in most foods including cereals and millets, pulses, nuts, oil seeds, vegetables and fruits, milk, meat, fish and</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>liver.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="iodine">IODINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#iodine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Iodine is needed for the functions of the Thyroid gland which is situated in the neck to form thyroxine hormone.</p>
<p>Sources:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Richest source of Iodine is crude common salt (prepared from sea water), sea fish and cold liver oil, smaller amounts occur in other food stuffs.</li>
</ul>
<p>Daily Requirement :- 150 mg. per day.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="fluoride">FLUORIDE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fluoride" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>It is found mostly in bones and teeth.</p>
<p>Sources:-</p>
<ul>
<li>Drinking water, sea fish, Cheese, tea.</li>
</ul>
<p>Daily Requirement :-</p>
<ul>
<li>The optimum level of fluoride in drinking water is 0.5 - 8 mg per ltr.</li>
</ul>
<p>WATER</p>
<p>Water basic human requirement. Water makes up two thirds of the body weight or 60% of the human body weight is due to water. Water is distributed in 3 compartments.</p>
<ol>
<li>inter cellular fluid - 50% of body weight.</li>
<li>Interstitial fluid - 15% of the body weight.</li>
<li>Blood this account for about 5% of the body weight.</li>
</ol>
<p>Sources:-</p>
<ul>
<li>The human body derives water from 2 main sources as</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Drinking water.</li>
<li>Food.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="functions">Functions:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Water is an essential constituent of many vital body fluids eg. blood, lymph, CSF.</li>
<li>It assists in the regulation of body temperature.</li>
<li>It helps in the transport of nutrients with in the body.</li>
<li>It is important in building and repair of body tissues.</li>
<li>Maintain the fluid balance in the body.</li>
<li>It is utilized in many body process eg.: Digestion, absorption and</li>
</ol>
<p>49</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nutrition">Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>elimination of body wastes.</p>
<p>Besides these water is needed for bathing washing and various other activities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="water-loss-from-our-body-is">Water loss from our body is :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water-loss-from-our-body-is" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>From kidneys - by means of urine.</li>
<li>By the skin - as sweat and perspiration.</li>
<li>By the lungs in the expired air.</li>
<li>Minor Degree by the faces from intestine.</li>
<li>Lactating women in the milk.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="requirement">Requirement :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#requirement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A normal healthy person needs to drink on an average about 6 glasses of water per day.</li>
<li>We can take fluids in the form of water, milk, soups and sambar, juices and other liquids.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="extra-fluids-need-to-be-taken">Extra fluids need to be taken :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#extra-fluids-need-to-be-taken" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>In summer time, and in the case of fever, to make up the loss in sweating.</li>
<li>In the case of vomiting or diarrhoea. Infants may die of dehydration if the loss is not made up by giving enough fluids.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cellulose">CELLULOSE : -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cellulose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This means the indigestible parts of foods. It includes the outer husk of whole cereals and pulses, also the skins, seeds and fibrous parts of fruits and vegetables.</p>
<p>It is good to include some cellulose in the diet. It increases the bulk of faces in the bowel and helps to prevent constipation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">SUMMARY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>To know the relation fo nutrition to health.</li>
<li>The health worker knows the functions of nutrition.</li>
<li>The classification of foods are Carbohydrates, fats, proteins, vitamins and minerals..</li>
<li>Carbohydrates are energy giving foods.</li>
<li>Fats are body building foods.</li>
<li>Proteins are body protecting foods.</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nutritive-value-of-food-stuffs">NUTRITIVE VALUE OF FOOD STUFFS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutritive-value-of-food-stuffs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the previous lessons, we learned about various nutrients required by the body. We have obtained these nutrients from the foods we eat.</p>
<p>On the basis of their nutritive value, food stuffs, have been classified into the following groups:</p>
<ol>
<li>Cereals and millets</li>
<li>Pulses</li>
<li>vegetables</li>
<li>Fruits</li>
<li>Milk and milk products</li>
<li>Meat, fish and eggs</li>
<li>Fats and oils</li>
<li>Sugar and jaggery</li>
<li>Condiments and spices</li>
<li>Beverages</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-cereals-and-millets">1) Cereals and Millets:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-cereals-and-millets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The cereals form the bulk of the daily diet of people. The cereals &amp; millets available in India are:</p>
<p><strong>Cereal:</strong> Rice, Wheat</p>
<p><strong>Millets:</strong> Maize, Jowar, Ragi, Bajra.</p>
<p>The Rice and wheat are most important cereals. They contain vitamins, mainly Vitamin B, Minerals, proteins and fat. Too much of washing may loose some vitamins. Millets are rich in Charbohydrades, Ragi is a rich source of calcium and yellow maize contain carotene.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-pulses">2) PULSES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-pulses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The next important to cereals in India are pulses. The various grams, dhals, peas and beans, Redgram, greengram, black gram, Bengal gram pulses are rich in proteins. They also called as "Poor man's meat". Pulses are also good sources of B-group vitamins &amp; minerals.</p>
<ul>
<li>Sprouted grams are good source of Vitamin - C.</li>
</ul>
<p>nutrition
52</p>
<ul>
<li>Soyabean has contain 40% of protein. Khesari Dhal - consumption of
Kesari dhal over prolonged period causes paralysis of lower limbs.</li>
<li>Ground nut: Ground nuts are more grown in India. They are rich fat and protein and also rich in nicotinic acid, thiamine &amp; riboflavin. Seeds are used for oil extraction and the residue for animal food.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-vegetables">3) VEGETABLES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-vegetables" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Vegetables are classified into 3 groups:</p>
<ol>
<li>Dark green leafy vegetables:</li>
</ol>
<p>These are the cheapest nutritious diet among protective foods. They are very valuable for the human nutrition. There is a variety of green leafy vegetables available in the market. They are palak (Spinach), amaranth, sourgreen, cabbage, methi etc.</p>
<p>These are rich in source of carotene, calcium, riboflavin, folic acid and vitamin - C. They contain cellulose which acts as roughage and prevent constipation.</p>
<p>A daily intake of 100 grams of leafy vegetables are recommended.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Roots and Tubers: They are tapioca, carrot, potato, radish, beetroot and onions.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Potato &amp; tapioka contain plenty of starch and fairly rich in proteins. They are used as staple foods to provide energy.</li>
<li>Carrots are rich in carotene.</li>
<li>The young leaves of root vegetables are very nutritious and should be eaten also. They are rich in calcium, potassium and some vitamins. A daily intake of 75 grams of root vegetables are recommended.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Other Vegetables:</li>
</ol>
<p>All the other vegetables such as brinjals, tomatoes, cauliflowers, drumstics, gourds, ladies fingers, pumpkin are rich source of vitamin - C and minerals. Daily 75 grams. of vegetable should be taken.</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-10a65a67.jpeg" alt="img-7.jpeg"></p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Fruits :</li>
</ol>
<p>They are protective foods. All kinds of fruits are rich source of vitamin-C, carotene and Minerals. So they can be eaten fresh and raw. The Indian goose berry (amla) and guava are very rich source of Vitamin - C. Some fruits such as mango and papaya are rich in carotene. Sitaphal are rich in calcium. There is not much vitamin - C in apples, grapes, pears and bananas. Daily intake of 85 grams of fresh fruits are recommended.</p>
<p>Nutrition
54</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-5cddf965.jpeg" alt="img-8.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-6488b741.jpeg" alt="img-9.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-b94c2564.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Milk and Milk products:</li>
</ol>
<p>Milk is the most complete or wholesome food among all foods. It contains the different nutrients in proper proportions. It is rich in calcium which is used for growth and development and maintenance of health. But it contains very little iron and only</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>small quantities of vitamin-C and B Infact, milk is only food for infants up to the age of 6 - 10 months.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>Human Milk</th><th></th><th>Cows &amp; Goat Milk</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Buffalo Milk</td><td></td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>1) Protein</td><td>2 %</td><td></td><td>4 %</td><td>5 %</td></tr><tr><td>2) Carbohydrates</td><td>6 %</td><td></td><td>4 %</td><td>5 %</td></tr><tr><td>3) Fat</td><td>4 %</td><td></td><td>4 %</td><td>8 %</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><strong>Nutritive value:</strong></p>
<p>Milk contain all the food factors:</p>
<ol>
<li>Proteins: Baffalos milk is rich in proteins than cows and human milk.</li>
<li>Fat: Buffalo's milk is rich in fat compare to cows and human milk.</li>
<li>Carbohydrates: Human milk contain more carbohydrates than cows, goat and buffalo milk.</li>
<li>Minerals: Milk is rich in calcium and almost all minerals needed by the body.</li>
<li>Vitamins: Milk is a good source of all vitamin except vitamin - C</li>
</ol>
<p>A minimum in take of 200 grms of milk by vegetarians and 100 grams by non vegetarians is recommended.</p>
<p>Pre school children, pregnant &amp; lactating mothers also need greater amounts of milk in their diet.</p>
<p><strong>Milk products:</strong> The common milk products consumed in this country are:</p>
<p>a) Curds (Dahi): Nutritive value of curd in similar to that of milk. It is prepared from milk.
b) Ghee: is 100% milk fat &amp; contain 1,000 to 2,000 IU of vitamin-A per 100 grams &amp; also vitamin - D it is much used in Indian homes.
c) Butter: Contains 82% of milk fat, a trace of proteins and rest of water it contain vitamin A &amp; D.
d) Cheese: composition depends upon the type of milk used. It contain high percent of milk fat &amp; protein.
e) Koa: It contains all milk solids.
f) Buttermilk: It is good for health due to less fat.
g) Whole milk power: It contain all nutrients except vitamin - C which is destroyed during drying. When 7 parts of water are added to the milk power, the milk has almost the same nutritious value as fresh milk and can be used in infant nutrition.</p>
<p>Nutrition
56</p>
<p>h) Skimmed milk power: In this fat is removed. However good source of protein, calcium and water soluble vitamins like B-complex and minerals. It is not suitable for babies due to lack of fat and vit. A &amp; D. UNICEF &amp; CARE have distributed more tons of milk powder to children and expected mothers in this country. Vegetable milk: Milk from soya beans, groundnuts, coconut are called vegetable milk.</p>
<p><strong>Animal Foods:-</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Meat: It is very nutritious. It is good source of vitamin B and protein. It is rich in iron and phosphorous, riboflavin and niacin.</li>
<li>Fish: It is rich in proteins. It is a fair source of B vitamins. Fatty fish contain vitamin A and D. Large fish contain phosphorus. Small fish eaten with bones are good source of calcium. Sae fish contain Iodine.</li>
<li>Egg: It contain all food factors except Carbohydrate.</li>
</ol>
<p>The egg yolk contains protein fat, vitamin A and D and B vitamins.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Liver: It is rich in proteins. Vitamin A and B vitamins including B12 which is necessary to prevent pernicious anaemia.</li>
<li>Fats and Oils: These are source of energy and essential fatty acids. It makes food tasty and palatalbe.</li>
</ol>
<p>Vanashpati (from ground nut oil) Ghee and butter are rich sources of vitamin A. All vegetable oils are good sources of vitamin E.
8. Sugars and jaggery: It includes cane sugars, glucose and honey. These are rich in carbohydrates and provide energy. Honey and jaggery contain iron and some minerals and vitamins. So these are more nutritious than white sugar and glucose.
9. condiments and spices: These include pepper, candamn, ginger, turmeric, temanind, chillies, cloves, suffron, corinder, curry leaves, cinnamonz, garlic, asafoesies etc. spices are used to make the food tasty, stimulating the appetite and helping in digestion. Spices have antibacterianal properties same are used in preserving foods and making pickles.
10. Beverages: These are classified as follows.</p>
<ol>
<li>Alcoholic: Whisky, rum, brandy, toddy.</li>
<li>Non-Alcoholic beverages: Coffee, tea, cocoa.</li>
<li>Soft drinks: Aerated water, coco - cola sugar cane, fruit juices, lemonade, coconut water.</li>
</ol>
<p>57 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Alcoholic Beverages:</strong>- The Constituent present in alcoholic beverages is ethyl alcohol. Beer and toddy contains about 5 %, spirit such as Brandy, wine about 10-25 % and spirits such as whisky, gin and rum contain 45 % of alcohol. Beer contain a life quantity quantity of B-vitamins.</li>
</ol>
<p>Alcohol contains 7 calories per gm, but it is very harmful to health in the following ways.</p>
<p>a. Alcohol irritates the mucosa and cause stomach and duodenum ulcers and leading to various complications.</p>
<p>b. It also affect the functioning of the liver and causes cirrhosis of liver in chronic cases.</p>
<p>c. In chronic cases, nervous system affected and cause a form of paralysis.</p>
<p>People should also realise about the bad affects of alcohol on their behaviour. Alcohol is a habit forming and chronic alcoholics result great harm to their total life and their family.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li><strong>Non alcoholic Beverages:</strong>-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Coffee contain caffein which stimulate the nervous system.</li>
<li>Tea when sugar, milk is added to tea, it is harmless compared and provide energy also.</li>
<li>Cocoa is mixed with coffee or tea which is rich in fat.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li><strong>Soft Drink:</strong>-</li>
</ol>
<p>Fruit juices, coconut water, sugar cane juice, lemon juice, carbohydrates, drinks are containing fair quantity of vitamin C and small quantities of B vitamins and minerals and provide energy also. They contain small quantities of minerals and vitamins.</p>
<p><strong>Improving diets with locally available stuffs. :-</strong></p>
<p>First the health worker should investigate, analyse and make plans in co-operation local handlers in order to help the community to improve their nutrition.</p>
<p><strong>The Health worker investigates the following things:-</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>How much malnutrition present in the community and the causative factors.</li>
<li>What type of foods are included in the diet of the family, preparation and serving also.</li>
<li>Is there cattle or poultry are kept and whether foods are sold or only keeping for family to eat.</li>
<li>Which families have fields, kitchen gardens and what type of</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
58</p>
<p>foods grow well in the area.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Local customs and habits related to the selection, preparation, cooking and serving of food, also customs related to infant feeding and weaning.</li>
<li>The appearance and names of locally available food stuffs both cultivated and growing wild.</li>
<li>The cost and seasonal availability of food stuffs.</li>
</ol>
<p>This investigation may carried out:-</p>
<ol>
<li>By means of simple dietary servay.</li>
<li>By observing the foods which are sold in the market.</li>
</ol>
<p>Then prepare a sample groups balanced diet according to the group i.e., is infants, pre school children, pregnant woman, and lactating mother.. The plan of meal should be based on locally available low cost food stuffs.</p>
<p>At first people may reject any suggested change in their dietary habits. With patient and preservance of your health education you may expect a gradual improvement and can see better results in family health.</p>
<p>Applied nutrition programme:-</p>
<p>The nutrition of the individuals, families and the community can be improved by many possible ways.</p>
<p>Kitchen Gardens, and poultry, keeping are the important areas in applied nutrition programme.</p>
<p>Some of the suggestion given below are :-</p>
<p>Better use of land to produce and grow more food:-</p>
<p>In India each crops like coffee, cotton, or tobacco are grown in much land to earn more money. Those crops had no nutritious value.</p>
<p>Lands which could be used for food crops may also be used in some places to grow for fire wood trees.</p>
<p>There is a need to cultivate more land and grow food crops of better quality of means of :-</p>
<ol>
<li>More land should be irrigated.</li>
<li>Hilly places should be terraced.</li>
<li>Crops should be rotated.</li>
<li>By using good quality of seeds.</li>
</ol>

Community Health Nursing - I</p>

<ol start="5">
<li>Produce the composition of manure.</li>
</ol>
<p>In some places other cultivations like fish breeding, or bee keeping for producing honey which are valuable foods.</p>
<p>In order to maintain good health, people are encouraged to grow more of the foods which are rich in nutrients, such as ragi, bajra, pulses, ground nut, soyabean, and dark green leafy vegetables.</p>
<p><strong>Kitchen Gardents:-</strong></p>
<p>The Health worker encourage the families in the community to plant kitchen gardents and eat the vegetables and fruits they grow.</p>
<p><strong>Educate them the value of kitchen gardens as follows:-</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Fresh fruits and vegetables taste better and are more nutritious.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It costs less to feed the family.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sullage water from the house can be used for irrigation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A compost fit can also be made to supply manure kitchen and other waste can be put into it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Gardening is good exercise and helps to remove worries and tensions.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The kitchen garden should be arranged near the house and to the water source, on land that slopes gently for drainage. If the soil is sandy, tank soil should be added, loam soil, which is in between sandy and clay soil, is the best.</p>
<p>According to the space availability the size of the garden may be plan. If there is plenty of space, the size will be depend on time available for working in the garden and the family size and needs.</p>
<p><strong>Kitchen Garden preparation:-</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Make a compost pit in a corner.</li>
<li>Make a fence around the gardens, so that no animal can comes into it.</li>
<li>Arrange a drain to carry sullage water from the house. This must be kept clean, so that the water must be flow freely.</li>
<li>Form a plan, devide the area into plots for different kinds of vegetables with paths between. Plan also for fruit trees such as papaya, guava and amla.</li>
<li>Dig the ground for some extent, remove all the stones.</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Add plenty of manure, leave it for 2 days, and dig again.</li>
<li>Sow good seeds, with plenty of variety. Some plants are best sown in boxes (nurseries) and the seedlings transplanted. When transplanting be careful not to harm the root, and to fix the plant firmly in the soil.</li>
<li>Pour water well after sowing and every day or as needed. Waste water which are coming from bathrooms or kitchen may be used. It can be directed in channels between rows of plants raised on ridges.</li>
<li>Stir up the soil often by hoeing to keep it loose plants do not like hard earth.</li>
<li>When there is a lot of sunshine, make a temporary shade with news paper or a box.</li>
<li>Be ware of insects and pests. Use insect killers with care, either as a spray or dusting power. Eg: DDT powder, or Kerosine oil.</li>
<li>Make a support with sticks for the plants to climb.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Poultry keeping:-</strong></p>
<p>By keeping poultry the family can have home produced eggs and chicken to help in better nutrition. If the fowls are cared well for and fed well; you can expect to get 150 -180 eggs per hen per year. White leghorns are the best egg-layers. More eggs will be laid if they are fed with a diet such as.</p>
<ol>
<li>Grains such as paddy, bajra, maize and ragi, 60 gm per fowl per day.</li>
<li>Mash, a mixture such as the following.</li>
</ol>
<table><thead><tr><th>Rice and wheat bran</th><th>-</th><th>5 parts</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Ragi flour</td><td>-</td><td>3 parts.</td></tr><tr><td>Fish meal</td><td>-</td><td>2 parts All 60 gms.</td></tr><tr><td>per fowl per day.</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Ground nut cake</td><td>-</td><td>1 part</td></tr><tr><td>Bone Meat</td><td>-</td><td>2 parts</td></tr><tr><td>Salt</td><td>-</td><td>alittle</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ol start="3">
<li>Fresh clean water always should be available.</li>
<li>Shell grit or limens and always available.</li>
<li>Greens or vegetables tops chopped 30 gms.</li>
</ol>
<p>Poultry should be let out all day, scratching for worms, insects and greens. A good place is a coconut or fruit tree top, where they have shade also. The ground should be kept clean, and the</p>
<p>Nutrition
62</p>
<p>area fenced for protection.</p>
<p>Poultry should be made conveniently near to the house. It should be airy, easy to clean, and raised on supports above the ground. Perhaps about 25 cm apart should be provided a separate place should be provided for roostig. (hatching of eggs)</p>
<p>For breeding have a good quality make bird. (A male bird is not necessary for egg production alone.</p>
<p>Baby chicken grow well if given white ants, chopped boiled eggs milk or curds, chopped greens, anions and garlic. Grains and mash should also be available. Get the help of the BDO, Extension Officer or veterinary for vaccination of chickens to prevent diseases, and in the case of sickness among the fowls.</p>
<p>Chickens should be eaten or sold while end.</p>

<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>UNIT - III</p>
<ol>
<li>Factors to be considered in planning meals:-
The advantages in planning meals are :-</li>
<li>It helps in the selection of a wider variety of foods.</li>
<li>It helps to meet the nutritional requirements of all family members.</li>
<li>It is easy to prepare and serve according to menu.
To be effective, meals should be planned for several days at one time.</li>
</ol>
<p>Factors that influence planning of meals are:-</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Income</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Family size</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Religion,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cultural habits.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occupation</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Level of knowledge.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Income :- What are the requirements, habits or customs of the group. The most important factor for selection of food is a amount of money available to purchase the food. The family depends upon the family income level and in a hostel or institution, upon the total contribution to the food budget.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Family Size:- The meals should be plan according to the size of the family. The nutrition of the infants and young children needs special consideration and adjustment according to their needs of growth and development activities and abilities to digest.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Relegation :- In different religions there are different loss regarding foods which may be for bidden, Eg: Hindus do not eat beef, muslim and Jesus do not eat pork. According to their religious laws, the meal should be planned.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cultural Habits:- Choice of food varies with the custom of different groups. The meal should be planned to meet the needs of vegetarians, non vegetarians, vegetarians who eat egg, and vegetarians who does not eat eggs.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Occupation:- The Special adjustment in the nutritional requirement of the older adult according to the degree of their activities. So the meals should be plan according to the occupation of the individuals.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Level of knowledge:- According to the level of knowledge of the family, the meal should be planned. So that all the family members can be accepted to take the food.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
64</p>
<p>Ignorance and poverty are the main problems at the root of malnutrition and under nutrition and adequate nutrition is linked with education, social and economic status of a nation.</p>
<p><strong>Selection of Foods:</strong>- When selecting foods to give a balanced diet it is essential that the body’s need for growth and repair and for regulation and protection should be satisfied first. The total calories may can be made up from other foods. McCollum has said “Eat what you want after you have eaten what you should”.</p>
<p>Some foods help to satisfy the body’s needs for more than one nutrient. Foods can therefore be divided into groups so that selection of one or more foods from each group will result in a balanced diet. These food groups are:-</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Protein Foods:</strong>-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Milk and milk products (i.e., curds, butter milk)</li>
<li>Pulses- Dhal, gram, lentils, dried beans and peas.</li>
<li>Nuts and oil seeds.</li>
<li>Eggs.</li>
<li>Fish.</li>
<li>Meat:- Mutton, poultry, pork, beef.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li><strong>Protective vegetables and fruits:</strong>-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>(One or more from each of the following three groups)</li>
<li>Green leafy vegetables, amaranth, radish tops, spinach, fenugreek, drum stick leaves etc.,</li>
<li>Yellow or orange fruits and vegetables :- Carrot, pumkin, papaya, mango.</li>
<li>Vitamin C rich fruits and vegetables are amla, Guava, orange, grape fruit, sweet lime, pineapple and tomato.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li><strong>Other Vegetables:</strong>-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Flowers, fruit and stems of plants.</li>
<li>i.e, brinjal, ladies' figner, beans and peas, cucumber, gourds and onions.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li><strong>Cereals, Roots and Tubers:</strong>-</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Rice, Wheat, Maize, jowar, Bajra, Ragi and others.</li>
<li>tapioca, potato, yam, sweet potato, colocasia (cereals are more nutritious if atleast two different kinds are eaten at the same time)</li>
</ul>
<ol start="5">
<li>Fats, oils, sugars and jaggery vegetable oils, vanaspathy, ghee, butter, sugar, jaggery, honey, fats and sugars are good sources of calories.</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>Condiments and spices contain same nutrients but are used mostly to give flavour.</p>
<p>It should be remembered that one cereals particularly rice, should not used alone by omitting other cereals. This is of particular importance in south India.</p>
<p>For vegetarians who do not take flesh foods, more pulses and dhal should be taken and an increased amount of milk must be used to make total protein which is obtained by the animal sources. The dietary value fo butter milk which is often very dilute, depends upon the quality of milk or curds from which it is prepared.</p>
<p><strong>Nutritional Requirements for vulnerable groups:-</strong></p>
<p>some groups in our communities are more likely to lack a balance diet and to suffer from malnutrition. These are called the ulnerable groups. Vulnerable groups who need special attention with regard to nutrition are as to follows:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Infants : Birth to one Year.</li>
<li>Children : 1-3 yrs.</li>
<li>Children : 4-6 yrs.</li>
<li>School children and adolescents.</li>
<li>Pregnant and lactating mothers.</li>
<li>Old people.</li>
<li>The sick, who need a modified diet.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>1. Infants:-</strong> Breast milk is the best food for infants - but is not enough after six months. From 4 months onwards child can start having porrigidge (Conjee) made with milk. When he is taking this well, from about 6 months he can be give parrdige with extra proteins.</p>
<p>Daily 600 ml. of breast milk secreated by the mother. This milk contain 65 calories per 100 gms of milk.</p>
<p>After 6 months output of breast milk decreases while the nutritional requirements increases to the child.</p>
<p>The best indicator of infant nutrition is its body weight weaning means not sudden with-drawal of child from the breast. It is a gradual process starting around the age of 4 months.</p>
<p>"These weaning foods can be made from the floor of a good staple food, i.e, rice, wheat, maize, ragi, bajra, add some milk and sugar for taste. At 4th month give 1 or 2 to parridge once in a day when he is hungry before going breast milk later gradually increase the amount of food. This may be boiled egg. mashed and mixed in, ground nut, gram or dhal ground to a</p>
<p>66</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nutrition">Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>poweder, sieved and added to cereal flour before cooked. Dark green leafy vegetables to the porridge also added.</p>
<p><strong>Vegetables</strong>: Such as carrots, pumpkin, green leaves, cooked and mashed. Fruits like ripe tomatoes, papaya, mangoes, juices with sugar and jaggery cane give.</p>
<p>At the age of 1 year the child should eat all the foods the family eat but the food must be soft with out spices i.e., cereals, pulses, vegetables, and fruits. The child needs 3 good meals a day. His weight curve will show if he is getting enough food for him to grow.</p>
<p>Children 1-3 years :- (Toddles) need about 120 calories per day.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-day-requirement">A Day requirement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-day-requirement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Item</th><th>Remarks</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>150 gm staple foods (at last two kinds including ragi or Bajra)</td><td>Serve 3 times a day.</td></tr><tr><td>200 ml.milk</td><td>Instead of this vegetarians</td></tr><tr><td>30 gm. egg, fish or meat</td><td>need extra 100 ml. milk and</td></tr><tr><td>40 gm Dark Green leafy vegetable..</td><td>10 gm pulses.</td></tr><tr><td>30 gm sugar of jaggery</td><td>preferably carrot, pumpkin, or</td></tr><tr><td>20 gm oil</td><td>other supplying carotene,</td></tr><tr><td>30 gm of other vegetables</td><td>jaggery provides extra iron</td></tr><tr><td>50 gm of Fruits.</td><td>and Costs loss.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aday-menu">Aday menu:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aday-menu" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>6 AM : Fresh fruit such as banana, guava, tomato, papaya or mango.</li>
<li>12 noon: 75 100 gm well cooked rice or other staple.</li>
<li>1 Boiled and mashed egg or fish or meat or</li>
<li>2 spoons well cooked or mashed dhal.</li>
<li>3-4 spoons boiled dark green leafy vegetables.</li>
<li>1 spoon ghee or oil, added and well mixed in the food while hot.</li>
<li>3 PM : Pulses such as Bengal gram 1 handful, milk with sugar or jaggery.</li>
<li>7-30 PM Meals similar to 12 noon meal.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="children-4-6-years-or-pre-school-child">Children 4-6 years or Pre School child)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#children-4-6-years-or-pre-school-child" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Children in this age group need special attention they show a good deal of physical activity and growth. So they need extra protein vitamins and minerals. They need about 1500 calories per day, with requirements of following.</p>
<ul>
<li>200 gm staple foods (two)</li>
<li>200 ml. milk For vegetarians give extra</li>
<li>30 gm egg, fish or meat milk and pusles.</li>
<li>50 gm pulses.</li>
</ul>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ul>
<li>75 gm Dark Green leafy vegetables. Give same waw vegetables salad about 3 times per week.</li>
<li>50 gm fruit.</li>
<li>40 gm sugar and jaggery.</li>
<li>25 gm oil.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-day-menu">A Day menu<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-day-menu" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>6 AM : Milk with sugar and jaggery.
8 AM : Ragi porridge or other staple, with milk and jaggery or pulses
10 Am Banana or other fruit.
12 noon Staple food (Two mixed), dark green leafy vegetables and other vegetables, one egg, dhal and curds, oi.
3 PM Pulse or nuts and milk.
7-30 PM Staple food (with family) and vegetable, fish or beans.</p>
<p>In many poor families, young children are breast-fed not given other foods to eat which result in high incidence of kwashiorkar and maramus. The best guide to assess child's growth is his body weight.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="adolcent-6-15-years">Adolcent: (6-15 years)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adolcent-6-15-years" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this age protein caloric deficiency and vitamins are frequent. They need to have a good breakfast and to have a balanced midday meal at school. In the evening they again need to have a well balanced meal with the family. They need one or two snacks during the day. If a mid day meal is not provided at school, the child should be given packed meal to take to school.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-invovled-in-organizing-a-school-meal-programme">Principles invovled in organizing a school meal programme:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-invovled-in-organizing-a-school-meal-programme" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>The meal should be supplement and not a substitute to the home diet.</li>
<li>The meal should supply at least 1/3 of total daily calorie and 1/2 of the protein requirement.</li>
<li>Cost of meal should be reasonably low.</li>
<li>The meal should be prepared easily in school.</li>
<li>Locally available foods should be used.</li>
<li>The menu should be frequently changed to avoid monotomy.</li>
</ol>
<p>A child who is hungry will not be able to learn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-balanced-midday-meal">A Balanced midday meal:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-balanced-midday-meal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Cereals such as rice or wheat - 75 gm per day per child.</li>
<li>Pulses such as dhal or beans - 30 gm per day per child.</li>
<li>Dark Green leafy vegetables - 30 gm per day per child.</li>
<li>Other vegetables - 30 gm per day per child.</li>
<li>Oil - 8 gm per day per child.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nutrition
68</p>
<p>A packed meal from home could include chappaties with thick dhal, boiled beans or ground nut, butter, and one fresh fruit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="5-selection-of-foods-during-pregnancy">5. Selection of foods during pregnancy :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#5-selection-of-foods-during-pregnancy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During first 3 months of normal pregnancy the diet need not be different from the average normal diet for women. After the 3 months the foods should be selected in such a way that all essential nutrients are supplied in proper amounts.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-following-foods-are-include-daily-in-the-meal-plan">The following foods are include daily in the meal plan:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-following-foods-are-include-daily-in-the-meal-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>30 gm - sugar or jaggery.</li>
<li>600 gm milk</li>
<li>120 gm meat, fish or 2 serving dhal.</li>
<li>4 serving vegetables and ghees</li>
<li>3 serving whole grain cereals. 2 fruits, nuts.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="meal-plan">Meal Plan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#meal-plan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
