<p>A minimum of 25 gms of oil should be used in cooking per day. Liver should be taken once or twice a week. For vegetarian dhal and grains can be used in place of meat and an increased amount of milk should be used. If the family can't effort large amount of milk, ground can be recommended. These can be used as chutny. Green leafy vegetables, Yellow vegetables, raw tomatoes, citrus fruits like lemon, oranges and gooseberry can be used papaya, guava also used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="selection-of-food-during-lactation">Selection of food during Lactation:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#selection-of-food-during-lactation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>Immediately after delivery mother requires adequate rest. She can develop a good appetite during this period. She can give normal regular meal or light meal.</p>
<p>Later the selection of foods during the lactation is basically same as that during pregnancy except for the daily addition of: 500 ml. of milk.</p>
<p>30 gm mutton or 15 gm dhal.</p>
<p>-fruit (citrus one).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pregnant-and-lactating-women-need-a-diet-as-follows">Pregnant and Lactating Women need a diet as follows:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pregnant-and-lactating-women-need-a-diet-as-follows" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Staple Food:-</th><th>Lactating Veg. Gm/day.</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Woman Non-veg.gm/day.</td><td>Cereals-in 3 meals</td><td></td></tr><tr><td>(include ragi or bajra).</td><td>500</td><td>75</td></tr><tr><td>Extra Proteins</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Pules - 2 servings</td><td>100</td><td>50</td></tr><tr><td>Nuts or sesame seeds</td><td>100</td><td>80</td></tr><tr><td>Meat, fish or egg</td><td>—</td><td>100</td></tr><tr><td>Milk or curds</td><td>800</td><td>650</td></tr><tr><td>Protective foods</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Dark Green leafy Vegetables</td><td>100</td><td>100</td></tr><tr><td>Other vegetables</td><td>75</td><td>75</td></tr><tr><td>Fruits</td><td>60</td><td>60</td></tr><tr><td>Extra Energy FoodsFats and oils</td><td>75</td><td>45</td></tr><tr><td>Sugar and jaggery</td><td>30</td><td>30</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>If a pregnant or lactating woman is pure vegetarian or cannot afford to have milk, she should be encouraged to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Increase the pulses in her diet.</li>
<li>Eat a handful of groundnuts daily.</li>
<li>Drink milk made from ragi malt, groundnuts or soyabeans.</li>
<li>Old People:- Old people need less calories than, and can eat only a small amount at a time, the diet should include some protein and protective foods every day.</li>
</ol>
<table><thead><tr><th></th><th>Vegetarian gm/ day</th><th>non - veg. gm.day</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Cereals in meals (Including ragior bajra)</td><td>300</td><td>300</td></tr><tr><td>Pulses</td><td>70</td><td>70</td></tr><tr><td>Ground nuts and sesame seeds</td><td>50</td><td>30</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Nutrition
70</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Milk</th><th>500</th><th>200</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Meat, fish and eggs</td><td>-</td><td>30</td></tr><tr><td>Dark green leafy vegetables</td><td>100</td><td>100</td></tr><tr><td>Other vegetables</td><td>30</td><td>30</td></tr><tr><td>Fats and oils</td><td>20</td><td>20</td></tr><tr><td>Sugar and jagger.</td><td>20</td><td>20</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Points for education of the community about good nutrition for vulnerable group (mothers and children) are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>If children under 5 year do not have a balanced diet they easily get sick and may die or grow up weak in body and mind.</li>
<li>If a pregnant woman woman does not have a balanced diet (enough of the right kinds of foods every day) her baby when born is likely to be small and weak. Also she will not have sufficient breast milk.</li>
<li>Pregnant and nursing women need to eat more than they eat normally, with extra protein and protective foods for health of themselves and the babies they are nourishing.</li>
<li>The nursing mother should continue to have extra nutritious food, and include green and yellow vegetables daily. She also needs to drink more including milk substitutes.</li>
<li>Breast milk is the ideal food for babies, and should be continued as long as possible. Other foods need to be given in addition from the 4th month.</li>
<li>Make sure that all infants receive a balanced diet with something from each of the food group. At one year a child should be having all kinds of solid food plus breast feeding or about 4 cups of milk.</li>
<li>Children need to have regular balanced meals, and should not be made to wait long or to miss meals. They need 3 good meals a day and extra snacks. For snacks, give fruits, pulses and nuts.</li>
<li>Foods given to children should be:-
a) Well prepared in clean conditions.
b) Not highly spiced, nor with a lot of sugar.
c) well - cooked and served fresh.</li>
<li>Rapidly growing school children need a good balance diet with extra body building and protective foods.</li>
<li>Adolescents need plenty of energy foods in addition to</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>foods containing other nutrients. Mature girls need extra dark green leafy vegetables for iron to make hemoglobin, because they lose blood when mestruating.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-modified-diets">7. Modified diets:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-modified-diets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are 4 types of diets.</p>
<ol>
<li>Full or regular diet.</li>
<li>Liquid diet or fluid diet.</li>
<li>Soft diet.</li>
<li>Bland diet.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-regular-or-full-diet">1. Regular or Full diet:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-regular-or-full-diet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For patients who are allowed it, a well balanced full diet should be served, either vegetarian or non vegetarian as desired. Patients with tuberculosis should be encouraged to take a full diet to put on weight.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-liquid-diet">2. Liquid Diet:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-liquid-diet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Liquid diets are used for patients who are unable to tolerate solid food and patients with high fever. This is modification of the consistency of a regular diet. If the patient receives liquid diet for along time, it is important to see that the diet should be adequate in all respects.</p>
<p>A liquid diet may be either a clear liquid or a full liquid diet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-clear-liquid-diet">1. Clear Liquid diet:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-clear-liquid-diet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is used when an acute illness or surgical patient who are intolerated to food and other nutrients. The only foods permitted on this diet are clear tea, weak black coffee, fat free broth, clear soup, meat and yeast extracts, soda water and other airrated beverages, clear fruit juice, barley water, gelatine, sugar and glucose. Such fluids are practically no food value other than calories. Calories may increase due to the use of glucose. This diet is continued for only one or two days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="2-the-full-liquid-diet">2. The full liquid diet:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-the-full-liquid-diet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is given for the patients must be maintained by fluids for a long period of time. This is necessary for the patient who is unable to swallow solid food or gastrostomy tubes. This diet includes all foods at room or body temperature.</p>
<p>Milk to the basis of good liquid diet and it can be enriched by adding egg, raji, skimmed milk powder or cream. Different flavors may be added to milk such as cocoa, coffee or fruits etc., strained dhal water, or soups made with meat or vegetables may be given, starches such as arrowroot, sago and cornflower can be</p>
<p>Nutrition
72</p>
<p>used to increase the calories.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-soft-semi-solid-and-light-diets">3. Soft, semi Solid and light diets:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-soft-semi-solid-and-light-diets" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are between liquid and full diets. The patient is unable to masticate. So the chief difference between this diet and the regular diet is the method of preparation.</p>
<p>The foods are cooked more simply with less spices and are more easily digestable and lower in roughage. A patient with moderate fever and one who is recovering from an illness or surgery, should be given light diet. When planned on the basis of the regular diet this diet should be equally nutritious and balanced. Avoid oilly, fried foods, and greasy sweets. Foods may be mined or mashed to make them soft.</p>
<p>Make sure that highly nutritious foods are included such as green leafy vegetables, dhal, curds, also eggs, meat and fish for non vegetarian light diet.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="4-bland-diet">4. Bland Diet:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-bland-diet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a soft and easily digestable diet with no spices or condiments and no strong coffee not other stimulants. It is often ordered in gastro intestinal conditions like ulcers.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="therapeutic-diet">Therapeutic Diet.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#therapeutic-diet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The diet may be planned according to the disease condition of the patient.</p>
<p><strong>Anaemia:</strong>- It is a condition in which deficiency of hemoglobin or RBC content and which result is decrease of blood to carry <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msub><mi>O</mi><mn>2</mn></msub></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">O_2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8333em; vertical-align: -0.15em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">O</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t vlist-t2"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.3011em;"><span style="top: -2.55em; margin-left: -0.0278em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight">2</span></span></span></span><span class="vlist-s">​</span></span><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.15em;"><span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to tissues.</p>
<p><strong>Cause:</strong>-</p>
<ul>
<li>Loss of blood</li>
<li>Mal nutrition.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Treatment:</strong>-</p>
<ul>
<li>Remove the cause.</li>
<li>Provide necessary nutrients.</li>
</ul>
<p>The following plan will provide the essential nutrients for blood building.</p>
<ol>
<li>1 serving of dried fruit like raisins, dates.</li>
<li>Use whole grain cereals and not finely milled.</li>
<li>Weekly 1-2 servings liver, kidneys, Heart and 2 or more servings of pulses light dhal.</li>
<li>Use plenty of jaggery and green leafy vegetable daily.</li>
<li>Provide high protein diet, i.e., milk, egg, meat, fish.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Hypertension (or) High Blood Pressure:</strong>-</p>
<p>73 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>This is a common condition in middle age, especially in fat people. This may be temporary as a result of exercise, emotion, pregnancy, or menopause. It may be permanent, associated with atherosclerosis, cardiac failure or chronic kidney disease and stroke.</p>
<p>To prevent and treatment of Hypertension:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Over weight people should loose weight. (low calorie diet).</li>
<li>Low fat, salt-free diet is needed.</li>
<li>Strong coffee other stimulants should be avoided.</li>
<li>Get the person to relax and not to worry.</li>
</ol>
<p>A sample day man for Hypertension is as follows:-</p>
<p>Morning:-</p>
<p>Break fast : Weak tea 1 cup.
Bread or idli with sugar or jam and butter, serving.
Fruits 1 serving, and weak tea 1 cup.
Roasted nuts 1 table spoon.</p>
<p>Midmorning : Fruit juice 1 glass.</p>
<p>Lunch : Rice or chappati 1 serving.
Dhal or meat or fish curry 1/2 cup.
Vegetables and potato 1 serving.
Curds 1 cup.
Fruits 1 serving.
Skim milk pudding 1 cup.</p>
<p>Evening : Biscuits 2 and fruit juice 1 glass, and roasted nuts 2 table spoons.</p>
<p>Dinner : Similar to lunch.</p>
<p>In this diet the food value should be :-</p>
<p>Calories not less than 2,000.</p>
<p>Protein - 20 gm / day.
Fat - not more than 5 gm.
Carbohydrates 470 gm or more.
Sodium - not more than 200 gms.
Chlorin - not more than 200 mg.
Fruit juice - 700 - 1,000 ml / day.</p>
<p>Diabetes:-</p>
<p>In this disease. There is too much sugar in the blood, and some sugar is passed in the urine. It is due to deficiency of insulin production, a hormone released from the pancreas. It is common among rice - eaters and usually starts at about 40 years of age.</p>
<p>Diet should be strictly regulated according to the amount of sugar found in specimens urine and the amount of insulin ordered</p>
<p>Nutrition
74</p>
<p>by the doctor. When the injection of insulin has been given, food also has to be given and the doctor's instructions must be strictly followed.</p>
<p>The patient must be helped to understand the importance of diet in his disease and about the danger of coma.</p>
<p>The health worker must be observant and prevent the patient from taking forbidden food such as seeds and sweetend coffee.</p>
<p>Low calorie diet should be recommended. The diet should be according to the need of the individual patient. Total calories are divided into equally into 3 or 4 meals. In many patients sugar is higher during morning time, so smaller breakpast is given. Depend upon the type of insulin meals is taken.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Peptic ulcer:-</li>
</ol>
<p>Discontinue in the lining of stomach and duodenum which is a chronic is called as peptic or gastric ulcer.</p>
<p>The Gastric juice contains acid and this prevents healing of the ulcer. A person who has a peptic ulcer will complain of pain in the upper abdomen which gets worse two or three hours after meals. The pain is increased at night when meals is missed.</p>
<p>At first there may be only indigestion and heart burn. Later, besides pain, there may be vomiting with blood, motion is black in colour called malena due to internal bleeding. The ulcer get deeper and cause a hole in the wall of the stomach or duodenum leading to peritonitis.</p>
<ul>
<li>Bleeding and peritonites cause death if the condition is not treated urgency.</li>
<li>Peptic ulcer can be prevented by taking regular diet and eating habits.</li>
<li>For those with ulcer, health education is as follows;</li>
<li>The patient should take meals regular times.</li>
<li>A bland diet is needed.</li>
<li>Avoid too much greasy spicy and heavy meals.</li>
<li>Avoid smoking and alcoholic drinks.</li>
<li>Relax, keep calm, and avoid tension, nervousness and anger.</li>
</ul>
<p>Menu for Peptic Ulcer:-</p>
<p>6 AM - Milk 2 cups or 150 ml.
8 AM - Bread 2 slices, and butter 2 tea spoon,
boiled egg, or cheese 2 slices, or</p>
<p>75 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>ground nuts 2 table spoons an milk 2 cups.
10 AM - Milk 2 cups or 150ml.
12 Noon - Rice or bread, mashed dhal 1 cup.</p>
<ul>
<li>minced meat or fish, or cheese or ground nut as above. Boiled potoato, and mashed leafy vegtables 1 cup.</li>
<li>Curds 1 cup.
2 PM - Milk 1 cup.
4 PM - Milk with sugar 1 cup, and biscuits 2.
6 PM - Milk with sugar 2 cups.
8 PM - Similar to 12 noon meal</li>
<li>or soft cooled egg.
10 PM - Milk 1 cup.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Tuberculosis:-</strong></p>
<p>In this the fever is prolonged unless the food intake decreases, the patient will lose weight.</p>
<p>Food should be bland, easily digested, varies and served attractivity.</p>
<p>High Caloric : High Carbohydrate, High protien diet.
Break fast : - Coffee with milk 200ml.</p>

Lunch : - Cooked rice - 2 cups.</p>

<ul>

<p>Latenight milk 200 ml.</p>
<p>Sugar oil, and butter can taken as desired. For vegetarians</p>
<p>Nutrition
76</p>
<p>flesh foods must be omitted and add more milk, curds and skimmed milk powder and more butter and ghee.</p>
<p><strong>Dietary therapy:</strong>-
Adequate nutrition plays an important part along with fresh air, rest, change of environment and various drugs in the treatment of Tuberculosis.</p>
<p>One of the aim is prevent emaciation and promote weight gain. The weight gain is occur due to intake of adequate diet.</p>
<p><strong>Principles of Diet therapy :-</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Diet should be high in protein to promote healing and high caloric to regain weight lost.
Proteins - 75 - 100 gm / day.
Calories 2500 - 3000 cal / day.</li>
<li>The diet should be rich in minerals and vitamins.
Calories:-Calories is important for classification of Tuberculosis nodes.</li>
</ol>
<p>Iron is necessary for hemoptysis. Vitamin C is need for early healing.
3. fluids :- Up to 3000 ml / day is needed.
6. <strong>Renal diseases</strong>
Renal refers to the kidneys and urinary tract. The special diet in kidney disease has already been mentioned. For infections of the urinary tract and renal stones, give plenty of fluids. If there is no fever, a bland, well balanced diet may be given.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li><strong>Heart Disease:</strong>
Heart troubles are more common in older people, especially those who are fat, those who smoke, and those with hypertension. The trouble is most often Coronary heart disease.</li>
</ol>
<p>Diet is important in the treatment and care of those with heart problems. The diet should be low in cholesterol and rich in essential fatty acids. Those who are overweight should have less calories. They should have little or no salt.</p>
<p><strong>A sample day's menu for Coronary Heart disease is as follows:</strong>
Morning Weak tea or milk.
Breakfast Bread or idli 1 serving, cheese 2 slices, or groundnut 2 teaspoons.
Fruits 1 serving, weak tea or milk 1 cup.
Lunch Rice or chappati 1 serving,
Dhal or meat or fish curry 1 serving,
Vegetables 1 serving,
curds 1 or 2 cups,</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>Fruits 1 serving,
Skim milk pudding 1/2 cup.</p>
<p>Tea
Biscuits 2, nuts 2 table spoons,
Fruit 1 serving and Weak tea 1 cup.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>There are various factors influence the planning of meals. They are income, family size, religion, culture and occupation.</li>
<li>Food should be selected according to the nutritive value i.e., protein foods, protective vegetables and fuits, cereals and fats and oils etc.</li>
<li>Nutritional requirement for special groups are infants, toddler, preschool, school age or adolescents, pregnant and lactating mother and oldage people.. These are vulnerable groups need special diet.</li>
<li>These other types of diets i.e., liquid diet, full diet, bland diet and soft or semi solid diet.</li>
<li>Other diseased persons need therapeutic diet those are anemia, hypertension, diabetes, peptic ulcer and tuberculosis.</li>
<li>Health worker know the preparation of special diets to the patients.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-iv">UNIT IV<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-iv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preparation-of-foods">PREPARATION OF FOODS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-foods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Fruit juice, barley water, tea, egg flip, boiled egg, pouched egg, albumin water, whey.</p>
<ol>
<li>Fruit juice:-
It is prepared from fresh fruit. Remove the juice from citrus fruit by means of squeezeer, strain, dilute, with water and add sugar or glucose to taste.</li>
</ol>
<p>Fruits which stew well, eg: apples and tomatoes may be stewed with a little water until pulpy, then strained through muslin. Add water and sugar or glucose to taste.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Barley Water:-
1 table spoon of barley flour.
2 table spoon of cold water.
500 ml of boiling water - salt.</li>
</ol>
<p>Mix the flour to a smooth paste with cold water and gradually add the building water, stirring all the time, boil about 30 mts add salt and 1 table spoon of lime juice, and strain before use.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Tea :-
Boil clean water, pour a little amount of water into the tea pot to warm it, and pour this way. Put some tea leaves into tea pot (about 1 tea spoon) ful and pour on boiling water. Cover the teapot and leave it to stand for about 2 mts before seerving. Add a little milk and sugar or lime juice.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Egg flip :-
Break an egg thoroughly (yolks not used, in albumin water may be used) and add 250 ml of milk. Stir well and strain before serving. This may be flavoured with sugar, cinnamon or lemon juice. If desired, it may be added to coffee, tea or cocoa.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Boiled Egg:-
A lightly boiled egg, cooked but still soft, is easily degested and suitable for the sick and for infants. The egg in its shall is placed into a pan of boiling water and kept boiling for 3 to 4 mts.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pouched Egg:-
This is suitable for those who are on light diet. Break the shell, taking care not to break the egg yolk and pour the egg into a shallow pan of boiling water. Cook gently until the white part is opaque. Take it out with a fish slice or flat spoon. It is usually</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>served on a slice of toast with or without butter, and a little salt.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Albumin water: - 1. Press the whites of two eggs through gauze into a glass, and without beating add lime juice, water and sugar,.</li>
</ol>
<p>For some persons without sugar added beef juice or to any beverage to the albumin water.</p>
<p>Albumin water: - 2. Take the whites of two fresh egg. Add one cup of water put into a wide neck bottle. Cork it and shake thoroughly. Add a little lime juice and sugar. If preferred orange juice may be substituted for the lime juice.</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>Whey: -</li>
</ol>
<p>To 500 ml. of fresh milk warmed to blood heat (37°C) add 1-2 teaspoons of rennet. Set it aside in a warm place for a water of an hour. Then break up the curd thoroughly by stirring with a fork. Let it stand for 15 mts, then strain the whey through muslin and bring it to the boiling point. Curds may be used in place of renner.</p>
<p>SELECTION AND STORAGE AND PREPARATION OF FOODS</p>
<ol>
<li>SELECTION: -</li>
</ol>
<p>The health worker should help family to plan the diet selecting foods for a mixed, well balanced diet:</p>
<ol>
<li>Select more than one kind of cereal grain. Raw milled rice and white flour should be avoided. Select paraboiled milled rice and whole wheat flour which are much more nutritious.</li>
<li>Select different kinds of pulses and nuts.</li>
<li>Buy grains and pulses in fairly large quantities if possible, if necessary going to some place where they are cheaper.</li>
<li>Select foods that are in season, plentiful and cheap.</li>
<li>Select a different kind of vegetables for each day as far as possible.</li>
</ol>
<p>Buy fresh and make sure they are of good quality. Include some vegetables or fruit that can be eaten raw.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Try to produce foods at home: Vegetables, fruits, milk, eggs etc.</li>
</ol>
<p>STORAGE: -</p>
<p>Teaching points are :</p>
<ol>
<li>All foods should be kept in clean conditions safe from rats</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
80</p>
<p>and other pests.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Vegetables and fruits lose their nutrient value if kept too long. Try to buy frequently. Keep them cool, away from sunlight and where there is plenty of fresh air. Use while fresh.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-purpose-of-cooking">THE PURPOSE OF COOKING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-purpose-of-cooking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cooking is an art. It is linked with dietary habits and cultural pattern of people.</p>
<p>Different methods are used in different types of diets.</p>
<ol>
<li>To soften and break down the cellulose of plant foods and the connective tissue and fibres of animal foods, to make them more digestable.</li>
<li>To develop new flavours in food, either by the method of cooking or by adding spices other flavouring substances.</li>
<li>To destroy the harmful bacteria, worm eggs and parasites. So that the food is safe for human use.</li>
<li>It stimulates the digestive juices.</li>
<li>It introduces variety, i.e., many different types of dishes can be prepared with the same ingredients.</li>
<li>Good cooking increases the acceptability of food, whereas bad cooking may lead to rejection of foods.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-cooking">METHODS OF COOKING:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-cooking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During the process of cooking, heat is applied to food in some way or other. The amount of heat and the form of heat depends upon the food to be cooked.</p>
<p>Methods which may be used are boiling, simmering, stewing, steaming, frying, grilling, baking and roasting.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-boiling">1. Boiling:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-boiling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Cooking in water at 100°C (212°F) is called boiling. For this the water must be bubbling freely, but steadily, all over the surface. Rice, dhal, pulses, roots, tubers and other vegetables are cooked in this way. Boiling in excess of water may result in loss of vitamins and minerals. So minimum water should be used.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-simmering">2. Simmering:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-simmering" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>It is a modification of boiling. Being to cook food in water just under boiling point. The temperature should be about 84°C. Meat and fish are best cooked by simmering because at high temperature, the fibres of meat are hardend.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-steaming">3. Steaming:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-steaming" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>It is cooking food in the vapour which rises from boiling water. This may be done by placing the food container in a staemer above a pan of boiling water or pressure cookers. Because of increased pressure of steam, the temperature attained is higher than 100°C. This process is best to save nutrients, food and time.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Stewing:</li>
</ol>
<p>This is method differs from boiling, in that</p>
<p>(a) comparatively smaller amounts of liquid is used.
(b) prolonged low degrees of heat is applied, usually about 200°F</p>
<p>i.e., simmer food slowly with only a little liquid in a covered pan on top of the stove. The addition of onions, tomatoes or small cutted vegetables and some condiments and herbs can make a meat stew appetising. In this method the nutrients are not lost. Stewing is used for cooking meat.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Frying:</li>
</ol>
<p>It is cooking food in very hot fat or oil. This is one of the quickest methods of cooking and should be done in an open pan.</p>
<p>These are 2 types (1) Shallow frying (2) Deep frying</p>
<p>(1) Shallow Frying: Shallow frying is suitable for cooking foods like eggs, sausages, dosai and pre-cooked foods.
(2) Deep frying; Food is completely immersed in large quantity of hot oil.</p>
<p>Eg.: Puri, pakoda, Vadai, cutlets etc. In deep frying oil should be sufficiently hot, otherwise food will absorb lot of oil and oil is free from moisture.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Roasting:</li>
</ol>
<p>Food is smeared with a little fat and exposed directly to heat or flame.</p>
<p>Chicken or tender mutton may be cooked by this method and also large joints of meat and for root vegetables dry roasting. Eg. Ground nuts.</p>
<p>This causes only slight loss of nutrients.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Baking:</li>
</ol>
<p>It is cooking food by dry heat. It is done in a hot air oven. Food is enclosed by hot air, so that it gets heat from all sides. The</p>
<p>82</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nutrition">Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>cooking temperature may be vary from 250°F to 500°F.</p>
<p>Baking is an expensive and slow method of cooking. In this Biscuits, Cakes, Bread are usually cooked.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-puffing">8. Puffing:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-puffing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is applying heat for a few seconds. It causes slight loss of thiamine only. Puffed rice, . Bengal gram and peas are commonly used for snacks.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-grilling">9. Grilling:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-grilling" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is cooking food by exposing it directly to very great heat either infront of a bright, hot fire or a special grilling plate.</p>
<p>It is very quick method of cookig. Only tender foods can be cycilled eg: Meat and fish, kabab, cheese, tomatoes,, brinjal etc. Stoves heated by gas and electricity are usually fitted with plates which can be heated for grilling.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-principles-of-cooking">General Principles of cooking:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-principles-of-cooking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Vitamin C is mostly lost in any kind of cooking especially by cooking for a long time. So you should not cook for a long time.</li>
<li>Adding cooking soda to dhal to hasten or to greens cause heavy loss of vitamin C. Therefore soda should not be used.</li>
<li>Greenleafy vegetables should be cooked in covered, quickly in a little boiled and salted water.</li>
</ol>
<p>Other vegetables should be covered.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Vegetables should be eat after thorough wash with salt water and clean water. Cut in to large pieces to prevent loss of vitamins.</li>
<li>Add tamarind or other acids only at the end of cooking or vegetables become hard.</li>
<li>Should not open the coveings while cooking food. Too much of opening may cause loss of vitamins.</li>
<li>Should not wash the rice somany times before cooking, this may cause loss of vitamin B which is theouer layer of rice.</li>
<li>Should not pour too much water and remove conjee, it may cause loss of nutrients.</li>
<li>Use fresh vegetables for cooking to save nutrients.</li>
<li>Using too much of oil also dangerous to health. Oil should be heated well before using.</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preservation-of-foods">Preservation of foods:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preservation-of-foods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>While fresh foods usually have a better taste, appearance and colour, it is useful to be able to preserve foods and keep them longer. By preservation methods, growth of bacteria is showed down.</p>
<p>(-Freezing is the best way to pressure foods at home but a refrigerator is costly)</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="house-hold-methods">House hold methods:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#house-hold-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is the best way but it is costly to preserve foods at a low temperature if possible.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Cold storage: The home refrigerator has now made to store and preserve a variety of foods. Fruits and vegetables should be kept just above the freezing point i.e., 0°C or 31 - 33°F, meat and butter are kept at much lower temperature. There is no growth of food poisoning organs at this low temperature.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drying or Dehydration:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Drying removes water and with out moisture micro-organisms can not grow. Vitamin C is destroyed but other nutrients are preserved. Milk, fruits, vegetables fish and meat may be preserved by drying. Preserved fruits and vegetables can be used when out of season to supply nutrients such as iron and carotene.</p>
<p>A simple dryer has been invented which could provide the basis for a cottage industry for preserved food.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Smoking:</li>
</ol>
<p>Meat may be preserved with smoke. Smoke contains phenols which help in preservation.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Salting and pickling:</li>
</ol>
<p>Salt is a preservative. By adding certain condiments, mangoes, vegetables, meat and fish may be preserved.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Making Jam:</li>
</ol>
<p>By boiling fruits and adding equivalent of sugar, jam is made which the housewife can keep for some time.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="commercial-methods">Commercial Methods:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#commercial-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Canning:</li>
</ol>
<p>Various foods (E.g. fruit juices, milk, baby foods, soups, fish) are preserved by canning. The food is first sterilized at high temperature i.e., 275 - 350°F for a short time i.e., a matter of a few seconds, then cooled and filled in presterilized containers in a</p>
<p>Nutrition
84</p>
<p>sterile atmosphere. There is some loss of meat labile vitamins drying the process of canning.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Freezing :-
A number of foods (fruits, vegetables, meat, fish) are preserved by the freezing techniques. At 0°F vegetables can be preserved for 8-10 months and meat for about 3 months.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chemicals :-
Certain chemicals (eg: benzoic acid, sodium benzoate) may be used for preservation but their use is strictly limited by government regulations and prohibit the use of chemicals for preserving food.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Irradiation :- Micro Organisms. are destroyed by gamma rays.
Wheat, potatoes and onions may be preserved by irradiation.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Milk preparations :-
Milk is high in nutrients, but quickly spoils. It keeps longer in the following preparations which can be made at home:
Curds: Add about 1/4 teaspoonful of 'starter' for each cup of barely warm milk, and let it stand at room temperature for twelve hours or more undisturbed. Lime juice can be used for starter if old curds from the pay before is not available.</p>
<p>Cottage cheese: Set the curds. After it has well set, drain off the whey by straining through a clean cotton cloth. When dry, remove the cheese from the cloth, add salt, and cream also if possible.</p>
<p>Ghee: Set of curds. After it has set, beat it up until butter forms. Then mix in cold drinking water and separate off the butter. Drop the ball of butter into a pan, and boil gently till all the white disappears and a good smell comes from the boiling butter. Then store in a covered pot.</p>
<p>Khoya which can be used to make milk-sweets, is made by boiling milk on a slow fire for some hours.</p>
<p>OTHER METHODS OF ENRICHING THE FAMILY DIET:
Sprouting gram, increases the vitamin B and C content of the gram. Green gram is best. Soak it in water for 24 hours, then spread it out on a damp cloth and keep the cloth damp for one or two days, until there is a half inch sprout. It may be eaten raw or</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>after cooking for a shorter.</p>
<p>Fermenting Cereals and dhals increases the Vitamin B content. This is done in making the popular S. Indian idli and dosa.</p>
<p><strong>Cereal-millet mixture</strong>: Using a millet such as ragi or bajra or jowar together will the staple cereal, adds extra nutrients to the dosa.</p>
<p><strong>Cereal-Pulse mixture</strong>: The protein value of a meal is increased by adding dhal or groundnuts to rice, roti, or chappati.</p>
<p>Milk Porridge: If instead of using water, milk is used to make the porridge out of any cereal flour, an infant gets more protein and calories in his diet.</p>
<p>Powdered protein foods can be prepared at home or in a mill. Foods rich in plant proteins such as groundnuts, grams and dhals, beans, are pounded or ground into prowder. Dried fish can also be powdered. The protein rich powders can be kept in tins. They need to be cooked and should therefore be added to the cereal flour before cooking. This makes a very nutritious meal for a child.</p>
<p>Pounded Dark Green Leaves: The leaves may be pounded either fresh or dried. Dried leaves make a green powder which can also be used to enrich a child's porridge. It can also be added to the dough for making roti or chappati, to enrich the family diet. It is rich in protein and iron.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-cooking">EFFECTS OF COOKING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-cooking" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-digestability">(1) Digestability:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-digestability" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The first and most important purposes of cooking food is to increase digestability. The starch granules absorb water, swell up and burst; the connective tissue of meat and fish is softened which helps in digestion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-distraction-of-microorganisms-and-parasites">(2) Distraction of microorganisms and parasites:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-distraction-of-microorganisms-and-parasites" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Cooking renders the food safe for human consumption by destroying microorganism like the typhoid bacilli and also the eggs and ova of intestinal parasites. Special mention must be made of the cysticerci of tapeworms which are destroyed.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-vitamins">(3) Vitamins:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-vitamins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Nutrition
86</p>
<p>The vitamins that are effected by cooking are vitamin B and vitamin C. The other vitamins are not destroyed.</p>
<p><strong>(4) Protiens:</strong>
Protiens are coagulated by heat. This helps in digestion.</p>
<p><strong>(5) Colour and texture changes:</strong>
Foods undergo colour and texture changes during cooking. The palatability of food is increased.</p>
<p><strong>Effects of cooking on food constituents:</strong></p>
<p><strong>(1) Carbohydrates:</strong>
As a result of heating in water, the starch granules absorb water, swell up and eventually burst. This is known as "gelatinization" of starch. Maximum gelatinization occurs at boiling point temperature. There is also a large increase in volume as for example, rice when it is cooked increases greatly in bulk.</p>
<p><strong>(2) Protiens:</strong>
Protiens coagulate at 60°C, boiling hardens albumin and globulin. This can best seen in the case of egg, if the egg is boiled for a long time, the albumin becomes very tough.</p>
<p><strong>(3) Fats:</strong> These are not effected much by heat.</p>
<p><strong>(4) Vitamins;</strong>
There is some unavoidable loss of vitamins during cooking. The loss is considerable in respect of thiamine and vitamin C. The use of baking soda in cooking causes further destruction of vitamins.</p>
<p><strong>(5) Minerals:</strong> These are not effected by cooking.</p>
<p><strong>Effects of cooking on different types of food:</strong></p>
<p><strong>(1) Cereals:</strong>
Rice is washed before cooking. Excessive washing removes the water soluble vitamins and minerals. The practice of cooking rice in large quantities of water and draining away the excess of water at the end of cooking leads to further loss of B group vitamins and minerals. Rice, Therefore must be cooked with just enough water so that all the water is absorbed at the end of cooking. This is usually 2 or 2 1/2 times the volume of rice. All cereals (Eg. wheat flour) absorb water and during cooking starch granules swell up and burst. This renders the digestion of starch rapid and complete.</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>(2) Pulses:</p>
<p>Pulses are rich in proteins (20% to 25%). They also contain small quantities of starch. It is very important to boil pulses very thoroughly, this destroys antitrypsin substance present in them.</p>
<p>(3) Greenleafy vegetables:</p>
<p>Greenleafy vegetables are prized for vitamins and minerals. The vitamin A which occurs in the form of carotene is not affected by cooking, but other vitamins thiamine and vitamin C are partially destroyed by cooking. If the cooking water is drained away, there will be loss of not only vitamins but also minerals. It is therefore recommended that greenleafy vegetables should be cooked in a small amount of water and for the proper length of time. Baking soda should not be used to hasten cooking.</p>
<p>(4) Other vegetables:</p>
<p>Other vegetables like potatoes should be cooked with their own intact. This retains all the vitamins and minerals contained in them. As a rule, vegetables should be cooked in a small amount of water to prevent loss of vitamins and minerals. They can also be cooked by steaming.</p>
<p>(5) Fruits:</p>
<p>Most fruits are eaten fresh and raw. This makes the vitamins present in the fruits easily available. Fruits can also be cooked by stewing; this will result in loss of some vitamins, particularly vitamin C.</p>
<p>(6) Meat:</p>
<p>Meat is cooked in a number of ways i.e., boiling, roasting, stewing, frying.</p>
<p>The following changes take place in meat during cooking:</p>
<p>(a) Coagulation of protein at 60°C.
(b) There is reduction in water content.
(c) Collagen which is a protein of the connective tissue is changed into gelatin.
(d) Elastin, which is also component of connective tissue is not affected.
(e) The fate of meat melts.
(f) There is loss of mineral salts in cooking water but this water can be used as a soup or gravy.
(g) The loss of B group vitamins especially thiamine.</p>
<p>Nutrition
88</p>
<p>(7) Fish:
Fish contains so little connective tissue, so the cooking time is very short. The protiens coagulate at 60°C in fish.</p>
<p>(8) Milk:
When the milk is heated, scum consisting of fat, forms on the surface. This makes it difficult for steam to escape, hence milk boils over easily. Some of the lactalbumin sticks to the sides and bottom. Prolonged boiling may altered the taste of milk. The cooked flavour is due to burning or caramelization of milk sugar. There is distraction of thiamine and vitamin C during boiling. Milk, which is already a poor source of vitamin C becomes poorest at the end of the boiling. Boiling destroys enzymes and the useful lactic acid bacteria present in milk.</p>
<p>(9) Egg:
The albumin of the egg begins to coagulate at 60°C, and solidifies at 64°C to 65°C. At boiling point i.e., 100°C the albumin becomes tough. However there is little change in the nutrients present in the egg.</p>
<p>FOOD HYGIENE
Food is a potential source of infection. It can be contaminated by backteria and other microorganisms and parasites at any point during its journey from the producer to the consumer.</p>
<p>Food hygiene implies hygiene in the production, handling distribution and sewing of all types of food. Food hygiene is an important aspect of community health.</p>
<p>MILK HYGIENE
Source of infection:-
Milk is an important "vehicle" or medium for the transmission of disease agents eg: tuberculosis bacilli, typhoid bacilli. The contamination of milk may arise from 3 sources.</p>
<ol>
<li>The dairy animal, eg: Tubercle bacilli.</li>
<li>The human handler: eg: Typhoid bacilli.</li>
<li>The environment; Eg: Through contaminated vessels, polluted water, dust and flies.</li>
</ol>
<p>Milk Born Disease:-
The important milk born diseases are:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Directly from the milk of animal.</li>
</ol>
<p>89 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>a. Bovine Tuberculosis.</p>
<p>b. Brucellosis.</p>
<p>c. Streptococci infections.</p>
<p>d. Q. Fever.</p>
<p>e. cow pox.</p>
<p>f. Foot and mouth diseases.</p>
<p>g. Anthrax</p>
<p>h. Tick - born encephalitis.</p>
<p><strong>Indirectly from the human handler or environment:</strong></p>
<p>a. Typhoid and paratyphoid fever.</p>
<p>b. Dysentery.</p>
<p>c. Cholera.</p>
<p>d. Viral hepatitis.</p>
<p>e. Diptheria.</p>
<p><strong>Boiling of Milk:</strong></p>
<p>Boiling is an ancient method of rendering the milk safe for human consumption. In fact much of the milk produced in India is treated by boiling.</p>
<p><strong>The Disadvantages of boiling the milk are:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Boiling kills all organisms present in the milk, including the useful lactic acid bacteria.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It destroys vitamin C and B mostly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Boiling gives a "cooked" taste to the milk, due to the burning of lactose during boiling.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Proteins in the milk are coagulated.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The enzymes are destroyed.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Pasteurization:</strong></p>
<p>Posteurization has been defined by an expert committee of WHO (1970) as "The heating of milk to such temperatures and for such periods of time as are required to destroy any pathogens that may be present while causing minimal changes in the composition, flavour and nutritive value".</p>
<p>Pasteurization differ from boiling in the following respects:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Pasteurization destroys only the harmful pathogenic bacteria, but not the useful lactic acid bacteria.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The vitamins are not destroyed by pasteurization.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
90</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Pasteurization causes only minimal changes in protein and sugar.</li>
<li>Pasteurization is the simplest, safest and the cheapest method of rendering milk safe.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Methods of pasteurization:</strong>-
Three methods of pasteurization are widely used:</p>
<ol>
<li>Holder or vat method.</li>
<li>HTST or high temperature and short time method.</li>
<li>UHT or ultra high temperature method.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>1. Holder (Vat) method:</strong>-
In this method milk is heated and kept at 63 – 66°C for 30 mts and the quickly cooled to below 5 degree Centigrade.</p>
<p><strong>2. HTST method:</strong>-
Milk is heated rapidly to a temperature of 72°C and then quickly cooled to below 5°C.</p>
<p><strong>3. UHT method:</strong>-
The temperature of milk is raised to 125 – 150°C for a few seconds only and then rapidly cooled.</p>
<p><strong>Phosphatase Test:</strong>-
This test is employed to final out if the milk has been properly pasteurized or not. The test is based on the principle that the enzyme phosphatase which is present in raw milk is destroyed during pasteurization. If the phosphotase enzyme is present after pasteurization, it indicates that the milk has not been properly pasteurized.</p>
<p><strong>Meat Hygiene.</strong>
The term "meat" includes various tissues of animal origin. Meat can be a source of infection if it is bad or unwholesome. The meat-borne diseases are :-</p>
<ol>
<li>Tape Worms :-
Tinea solium.
Tinea Saginata.
Trichinella spiralis.
Fasciola hepatica.</li>
<li>Bacterial - Anthrax.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Actinomycosis.</li>
</ul>
<p>91 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<ul>
<li>Tuberculosis.</li>
<li>Food poisoning.</li>
<li>Antrhrax.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Meat inspection:-</strong></p>
<p>Since meat is consumed by a large number of people, it is a responsibility of the community to ensure that the meat sold in the market is fit for human consumption. This responsibility rests on municipalities, corporations and other local bodies. The animals to be slaughtered and are first examined by a qualified veterinary surgeon. This is called "antemortem examination". The diseased and sick animals are excluded, and only healthy animals are passed for slaughter. The main causes of antemortem rejection are emaciation, tuberculosis, pregnancy, diarrhoea, febrile conditions, sheep - pox, foot rot, blucellosis. A second examination is carried out soon after slaughter: This is called "Postmortem inspection". If any disease condition (Eg: cysticercus boris, liver fluke, hydatidosis, tuberculosis, infections of liver and lungs) is found, the meat is rejected.</p>
<p><strong>Signs of good meat:-</strong></p>
<p>The characteristics of good meat are:-</p>
<ol>
<li>Colour :- This should not be pale pink or deep purple.</li>
<li>Touch :- The meat should be firm and elastic to touch. It should not be greasy or slimy.</li>
<li>Smell :- The odour should be agreable.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Fish</strong></p>
<p>Fish decomposes quickly after death. The signs of fresh fish are:-</p>
<ol>
<li>It must be in a state of stiffness or rigor mortis.</li>
<li>The gills must be bright and</li>
<li>The eyes must be clear and prominent.</li>
</ol>
<p>The following diseases are known to be transmitted by fish :</p>
<ol>
<li>A tape worm known as D-latus and</li>
<li>Fish poisoning. Since fish is not eated raw in this country. D-Latus infection is a rare disease.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Tinned fish</strong></p>
<p>More and more people are eating tinned fish and meat these days than over before. It is necessary to inspect the tin or can before consuming the contents. The following points should</p>
<p>Nutrition
92</p>
<p>be noted when examining tinned fish or meat or any other tinned food.</p>
<ol>
<li>The tin must be from fresh stock i.e it must be new and clean.</li>
<li>There should be no evidence of having been tampered with, as for example, the presence of scaled openings Such tins should be discarded.</li>
<li>On shaking the tin there should be no sound.</li>
<li>On opening the tin, the contents should not be blown out, on the other hand, there should be a hissing noise.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>EGGS</strong></p>
<p>Eggs become stale on prolonged storage, and storage under unsatisfactory conditions. The freshness of the eggs may be tested as follows:-</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Candiling:</strong>- When a strong light is projected, the egg must appear transparent. The eggs are rejected if there are any spots or internal blemishes.</li>
<li><strong>Floating in saline water:</strong>- Fresh eggs sink in 10 /- salt solution; stale eggs will float.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Fruits and vegetables</strong></p>
<p>Fruits and vegetables, especially those which are eaten raw (i.e., tomatoes, radish, carrot) can be a source of infection. Those which are grown in sewage -irrigated land, are particularly dangerous, if eaten raw and unwashed. They can transmit pathogenic bacteria like the typhoid bacilli and worm infestations. Vegetables which are cooked and eaten are free from this danger. Vegetables which are to be eaten raw are best treated in a weak solution of potassium permanganate, and later washed in running water.</p>
<p><strong>Sanitation of eating place:</strong>-</p>
<p>Sanitation of eating places (eg.: hotels, restaurants) is a challenging problem in food sanitation. It is particularly low in India. The following minimum standards have been suggested for restaurants and eating houses in India under the model public health act (1955)</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Location</strong> ↑</li>
</ol>
<p>Shall not be near any accumulation of filth, open drains, stables, manure pits and other sources of nuisance.</p>
<p>93 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Floor
To be higher than the adjoining land, made with impervious material and easy to keep clean.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rooms
a. Rooms where meals are served shall not be less than 100 sq. feet and shall provide accommodation for a maximum of 10 persons.
b. Walls up to 3 feet should be smooth, corners to be rounded should be impervious and easily washable.
c. There should be ample lighting facilities aided by artificial lighting with good circulation of air.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Kitchen
a. Floor space minimum 60 sq. ft.
b. Window opening to be 25% of floor area.
c. Floor to be impervious, smooth, easy to keep clean and non slippery.
d. Doors and windows should be 2% of floor area, in addition to smoke pipes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Storage of cooked food:-
Seperate room should be provided for long storage, control of temperature is needed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Storage of uncooked food stuffs:-
Persihable and non possible articles should be kept separately, in rat proof and vermin-proof space; for storage of perishable articles, temperature control should be adopted.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Furniture
Should be reasonably strong and easy to keep clean and dry.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disposal of Refuse:-
To be collected in covered impervious bins and disposed of twice a day.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Water supply
To be an independent source, adequate, continuous and safe.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Washing facilities:-
To be provided cleaning of utensils and crockery, to be done in hot water and followed by disinfection.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
94</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="food-handlers">Food handlers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-handlers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Food handlers are those persons who are connected with cooking, serving or distribution of food. They can spread disease by their unhygiene habits. The diseases likely to be spread by food handlers are typhoid and paratyphiod fever, diarrhoea, and dysenty, viral hepatitis (Jaundice) and intestinal worms.</p>
<p>Persons with a previous history of typhoid fever, and chronic dysentry should not be employed in eating establishments. Persons suffering from skin diseases ear discharges or only infected wounds on the body should not be permitted to handle food or utensils.</p>
<p>Many of the food handlers have very little educational background. The following aspects of personal hygiene should be emphasized to all food handlers.</p>
<p>a. Hands</p>
<p>The hands should be clean at all times. Hands should be scrubbed and washed with soap and water immediately after visiting a lavatory. Finger nails should be kept trimmed and free from dust.</p>
<p>b. Hair</p>
<p>Head covering should be provided, particularly in the case of females to prevent loose hairs falling into food.</p>
<p>c. Overalls</p>
<p>Clean white overalls or aprons should be worn by all food handlers.</p>
<p>d. Habits</p>
<p>Coughing and sneezing in the vicinity of food, licking the fingers before picking up an article of food, smoking on food premises are to be avoided.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="food-borne-disease">Food Borne Disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-borne-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Food Borne infections and diseases may be classified as below:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Bacterial: Typhoid and paratyphoid.
Diarrhora.
Dysentry.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Viral : Viral Hepatitis (jaundice)
Poliomyelitis.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>95
Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Protozoal : Amoebiasis.</li>
<li>Intestinal worms : Tape worm and round worm.</li>
<li>Others : Food poisoning.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The health worker should help families to plan the diet selecting foods for a mixed, welt balanced diet.</li>
<li>Select different kinds of nutrients.</li>
<li>Select foods that are in season, plentiful and cheap.</li>
<li>Food materials should be stored in proper methods.</li>
<li>The health worker should know the purposes of cooking.</li>
<li>The types of coking are boiling, steaming, pressure cooking, frying, dry roasing, baking, puffing.</li>
<li>Preservation of food materials by house hold methods are drying, salting, pickling, making jam etc.</li>
<li>The food hygiene should be maintained to prevent communicable diseases that are spread from one person to other persons.</li>
<li>The food handlers should be little educable and they have maintain proper hygiene to prevent the spread of disease.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="questions">Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
