<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-v">UNIT - V<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-v" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="balanced-diet">BALANCED DIET: -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#balanced-diet" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A balanced diet is one which contains all the nutrients such as carbohydrates, fats, proteins, vitamins and minerals which meet the requirements of the body to maintain a balance state of health is known as balanced diet.</p>
<p>If any nutrient is deficit the individual suffers with malnutrition of that factor. Usually malnutrition in carbohydrates, proteins are seen in children due to lack of proper nourishment in India.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mal-nutrition">MAL NUTRITION : -<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mal-nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This condition is wide spread in India among children 6 months to 3 years. Malnutrition is a condition which occurs when the body does not get the proper kind of food in the amounts needed for maintaining health or child is getting too little of energy foods (callories) as well as the little of body building (proteins) foods. in fact there is starvation or under nutrition.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-main-factors-causing-pem-are">The main factors causing PEM are:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-main-factors-causing-pem-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Poverty and poor environmental sanitation.</li>
<li>Ignorance, illiteracy, food fads and habits.</li>
<li>Repeated infections such as diarrhoea and respiratory infections.</li>
<li>Large families with not enough foods.</li>
<li>Low birth weight and an aneamic mother.</li>
<li>Infections, worm infections.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="signs-and-symptoms">Signs and symptoms:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#signs-and-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The signs and symptoms of malnutrition in children are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Growth failure or the child loses weight.</li>
<li>Skin changes - skin dry, scaly or rough, loss of subcutaneous fat (elasticity)</li>
<li>Eye changes - dryness, nightblindness.</li>
<li>Hair changes - light colour, brittle.</li>
<li>Oedema.</li>
<li>Anaemia.</li>
<li>Others: apathy, listlessness, soreness of mouth, bowing of legs, frequent episodes of illness etc.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="screening-for-malnutrition">Screening for malnutrition:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#screening-for-malnutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are several methods to identify malnutrition in children:</p>
<ol>
<li>Height and weight :- The best way to identify children who are malnourished is to take their height and weight regularly. The</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>growth chart shows the child's health and nutritional status.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Mid arm circumference :- Another simple and useful methods is to measure the mid arm circumference. Any child between 1-5 years considered to be malnourished, if the measurement is less than 12.8 cms.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clinical and laboratory examination:-</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The examination of child from head to foot for signs of malnutrition (i.e. protein, vitamin and mineral deficiencies) is another approach for detectionary malnouritions. Such examinations may be supplemented by laboratory tests such as estimation of hemoglobin.</p>
<p>Problems of malnutrition:-</p>
<p>The important problems of malnouritions in India are :</p>
<ol>
<li>Kwashiorkor and marasmus:-</li>
</ol>
<p>These are serious diseases of P.EM. which develop in, young children between 1-3 years of age. They are due to (a). An inadequate diet, that is a diet lacking in proteins and calories and</p>
<p>(b) Infections such as diarrhoea, measles, bronchitis which lead the child into malnutrition.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-495bf98c.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg">
KWASHIORKAR</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-4ae36b9a.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg">
MARASMUS</p>
<p>The Signs and symptoms of kwashiorkor are:</p>
<p>Oedema.</p>
<ul>
<li>Growth failure.</li>
<li>Diarrhoea</li>
<li>Hair and skin changes.</li>
</ul>
<p>The signs of marasmus are :-</p>
<ul>
<li>Marked wasting of muscles and</li>
<li>Loss of subcutaneous fat.</li>
<li>The child is reduced to "skin and bones" kwashiorkor and mearasmus affect not only the physical growth but also mental</li>
</ul>
<p>Nutrition
98</p>
<p>development of the child. They can also cause death.</p>
<p>PEM need to be prevented by means of:</p>
<ol>
<li>Proper antenatal care of mothers, because a healthy mother give birth to a healthy baby.</li>
<li>Promotion of breast feeding.</li>
<li>Proper weaning of the child.</li>
</ol>
<p>The child should be given nutrition supplement starting around the age 4-6 months as breast milk alone is not sufficient to sustain the growth of the child. Nutritional supplements can be easily prepared at home using low cost locally available. Foods such as cereals, millets, pulses groundnuts, sugar and jaggery. Proper use of these supplements help in preventing malnutrition during the weaning period.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>
<p>Nutrition education of the mother.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Immunization of the child against child hood diseases.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Food hygiene practices to prevent infections.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Economic development to decrease poverty.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Improved environmental sanitation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutrition and health education.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Family planning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Anaemia:-</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>If the conjunctiva is pale, the persons said to be anaemic.</p>
<ul>
<li>A better method will be to estimate the Haemoglobin level.</li>
<li>If the Haemoglobin level is less than 12 gms. the person needs treatment of iron and folic acid tablets.</li>
</ul>
<p>a. Vitamin A deficiency:-</p>
<p>This is a serious health problem especially among preschool children.</p>
<ol>
<li>Stunted growth i.e., the growth may be decreased.</li>
<li>Unhealthy eyes.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Night blindness or inability of see in dim light.</li>
<li>Bitot's spots : These are brownish, triangular, raised, foamy patches seen on the white portion (conjunctiva) of the eye.</li>
<li>Xeropthalmia : Means dryness of the eyes which leading to eye infections and later keratomalcia (dull, opaque, cornea) and to blindness.</li>
</ul>
<p>The conjunctiva is not included.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-dc510ede.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<p>99 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Dry, scaly skin and epithelial tissues. Germs enter easily leading to infections of respiratory tract. Eye changes leading to blindness can occur rapidly. Screening of small children is needed to detect early signs of the deficiency.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>In the government programme started in 1976, children from 1-5 year are given an oral dose of Vitamin A solution once in 6 months. If too much vitamin A is given toxic symptoms occur such as head ache, loss of appetite and dry itching skin.</li>
</ul>
<p>b. Vitamin D deficiency:-</p>
<p>Vitamin D deficiency leads to following conditions:-</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Rickets:- Rickets in children who donot have enough sunlihgt or who are not eating animal food such as eggs. It is a common disease in children. Rickets causes a child to have poor teeth and a small chin, bulging of the head bones, beading of the ribs, and bow legs or knock knees. The child feels sore in various parts of the body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Osteomalacia :- It means Softening of the bones which may be seen in adults.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>In these two conditions the essential abnormality is that bones contain less calcium than normal. In this condition the softening of the bones occur. It is a disease of pregnant or lactating mothers and old people.</p>
<p>When signs of these disease are found, Multivitamin tablets and advice on diet should be given, and the person referred to a doctor.</p>
<p>c. Vitamin E deficiency:-</p>
<ul>
<li>It Causes habitual abortion, testicular and myocardial degeneration.</li>
</ul>
<p>d. Vitamin K deficiency:-</p>
<p>It is rarely occur in adults who consume normal balanced diets. It causes decreased clotting mechanism.</p>
<p>e. Vitamin C deficiency :-</p>
<p>It is called scurvy disease i.e., bleeding disease. It is mostly seen in infants fed on in adequate artificial feeds. The persons who does not have enough fresh fruits and vegetables containing vitamin C. An infant with early signs of the disease loses his appetite and cries when his arms and legs are moved. Signs and symptoms of scurvy are :-</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Spongy bleeding gums and loose teeth.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bleeding under the skin and into various tissues.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
100</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Pain and swelling of the joint.</li>
<li>Slow healing of wounds or breakdown of old wound scars.</li>
</ol>
<p>Treatment is with ascorbic acid (Vitamin C) tablets or multivitamin tablets and advice about diet. Infants who are not breast fed need vitamin C. and it can be given in the form of fruit juice or greens juice. Those recovering from illness such as diarrhoea, or from wounds, need more of this vitamin.</p>
<p>f. Vitamin B deficiency:-
i) Thiamine deficiency:-
This is common where people eat a lot of raw polished rice as in parts of Andhra Pradesh early symptoms are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Beri Bew indicates by edema or swelling all over the body in wet type. There is paralysis in dry type. Infantile beri beri can result in early sudden death due to enlarged heart.</li>
<li>Loss of appetite.</li>
<li>Tringling hands and feet, or numbness.</li>
<li>Restlessness and general weakness.</li>
<li>Breathlessness due to heart enlargement.</li>
<li>Encephalopathy may be resulted.</li>
</ol>
<p>In this deficiency, riboflavi and nicotinic acid deficiency is also present. So vitamin B complex is necessary.</p>
<p>ii) Ribo flavin deficiency:-
Signs and symptoms of this deficiency:</p>
<ol>
<li>Angular stomatitis - sore white patches at the corners of the mouth.</li>
<li>Glossitis - Swollen, sore tongue.</li>
<li>Redness and burning sensation of the eyes.</li>
<li>Dermatitis - skin lesions.</li>
</ol>
<p>iii) Nicotinic Acid deficiency:- The disease caused by this is called pellagra. But it takes some time to develop. The signs are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Soreness of the tongue with indentations made by the teeth</li>
<li>Pigmented scaly skin and diarrhoea. Skin beeames pigmented and scaly on parts of the body exposed to sunlight that is hands, feet, face and neck.</li>
<li>Pigmentation has a symmetrical distribution.</li>
<li>Insevere cases, mental disturbance. At last cause death.</li>
</ul>
<p>Vitamin B complex should be given.</p>
<p>iv. Folic acid deficiency:
It causes anaemia among poor people and pregnant mothers.</p>
<p>Treatment: Iron and folic acid tablets should be given.</p>
<p>v. Vitamin B₁₂ Deficiency:
It cause pernicious anaemia i.e., market decreased</p>
<p>101 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>number of red blood cells.</p>
<ul>
<li>Affect the nervous system including spinal cord.</li>
</ul>
<p>vi. Mineral deficiency:-
a) Calcium deficiency: This may cause</p>
<ol>
<li>Stunted growth in children.</li>
<li>Rickets (ear and vitamin D deficiency).</li>
<li>Tetany:- Nervousness, muscle, twitchings and spasms.</li>
<li>Osteoporosis :- Brittle bones so that fractures occur with minor accidents.</li>
<li>Interference with blood clotting.</li>
<li>Refer to the doctor is important.</li>
</ol>
<p>b) Iron deficiency:
Insufficient iron in the diet is a common cause of anaemia those who lack iron look pale, easily get out breath and feel tired. Children who are anaemic are often sick.
Normally the iron in our bodies is used over and over again and we need little extra from our diet, but in the following circumstances iron is lost and anaemia is caused unless more iron is taken into the body,</p>
<ol>
<li>Bleeding of any kind, including menstruation, piles trouble and dysentry.</li>
<li>Disease such as malaria and hook worm, when blood is destroyed.</li>
<li>In pregnancy because the foetus takes iron from the mother.
Growing children need extra iron to make blood, and anaemia is common especially after the age of 3 or 4 months when the iron stored in the liver is used up. There is very little iron in milk and other foods must be given to these young children.</li>
</ol>
<p>c. Iodine deficiency:
Lead to swelling of the thyroid gland in the neck, a condition know as goitre.</p>
<ul>
<li>During pregnancy the lack of iodine can cause cretinism in the body and mental retardation may be caused. In India 9 millions of people are estimate to be affected by goitre.
Goitre may be prevented and curved by the regular use of iodized salt in the diet of people who live in areas of iodine deficiency. 1992 National Policy laid to prepare only iodized salt and condom used using common salt. The National Goitre control programme (1962) iodized salt is supplied freely in endemic goitre areas, with the help of UNICEF.</li>
</ul>
<p>Nutrition
102</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="anaemia-in-women">ANAEMIA IN WOMEN:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anaemia-in-women" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Many women are anaemic. The condition is usually connected with pregnancy and childbirth.</p>
<p>Besides menstruation, blood may be lost due to abortions or delivery and not made up. The growing foetus and breast feed child also takes nutrients from the mother.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="to-detect-anaemia-in-women">To detect anaemia in women:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#to-detect-anaemia-in-women" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Notice if she looks pale, gets tired easily and has little energy.</li>
<li>Examine the conjunctiva by pulling down the lower eyelid (with clean hands).</li>
<li>Examine the mucous membrane of the mouth by pulling down the lower lip.</li>
<li>Find out the haemoglobin percentage by using a Talquist colour scale.</li>
</ol>
<p>Iron Deficiency Anaemia is the most common type. Iron and protein are both necessary for the formation of haemoglobin.</p>
<p>Folic Acid is used to vitamin C necessary for the formation of red blood cells. Pregnant women need extra Folic acid as well as iron to meet the needs of the foetus for its blood.</p>
<p>Vitamin B₁₂ deficiency causes the disease called Pernicious anaemia. This vitamin is also important for making red blood cells. The richest source is liver, because vitamin B₁₂ is stored in the liver.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treatment">Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Pregnant and nursing mothers, also family planning acceptors who have below 12 gm (80%) haemoglobin are eligible for free iron and folic acid tablets.</p>
<p>If the haemoglobin is below 10 gm (70%) refer to the health centre or hospital. Those suffering from pernicious anaemia need regular injections of vitamin B₁₂</p>
<p>Health Teaching related to Treatment:</p>
<ol>
<li>Iron and folic acid are both needed to improve the blood and overcome anaemia.</li>
<li>The tablets must be taken daily, and because they may irritate the stomach they should be taken at meal times with food.</li>
<li>The tablets will make the faeces black, but there is no harm in this.</li>
<li>The tablets are harmful to small children and so must be kept out of their reach.</li>
<li>In addition to the tablets, foods rich in iron such as dark green leafy vegetables should be eaten daily.</li>
<li>Continue the treatment for three months, when the blood test</li>
</ol>
<p>103 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>for haemoglobin is to be reapeated.</p>
<p>In addition, teach women the importance of spacing the family, to enable her to regain health and strength.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-workers-role">Health Workers Role<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-workers-role" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Encourage parent to bring all infants and pre-school children to the sub-centre for checking.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Regularly weight and measure infants and pre-school children and record on the ‘Road to Health’ chart.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Measure the arm circumference of children 1-5 years and record.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>From the observations, detect early cases of malnutrition and give the appropriate treatment and health teaching.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>On village and home visits, observe carefully all children, pregnant and nursing women. Identify case of malnutrition and anaemia, and make sure they recieve treatment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Look for malnutrition in children, especially when a child is :</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>a. a twin, low-birth-weight, or has noliving parents.</p>
<p>b. one of four or more children in the family.</p>
<p>c. having a sister or brother who is less than one year younger.</p>
<p>d. having a sister or brother who is malnourished.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Look for malnutrition or anaemia in a pregnant or nursing woman who</li>
</ol>
<p>a. has a history of stillbirths, abortions or haemorrhage.</p>
<p>b. has had four or more pregnancies.</p>
<p>c. had her last delivery less than a year ago.</p>
<p>d. is a widow or seperated from her husband.</p>
<p>e. in pregnancy is not increasing in weight.</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>
<p>Identify cases of nutritional deficiencies, especially signs of Vitamin A deficiency. Refer all severe cases immediately to the health centre or hospitals.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Give vitamin A solution 2 ml. to all children 1-5 years once every six months (but not more often ) and record the details. gove also to all children and adults in whom there are signs of vitamin a deficiency.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Be always prepared to gtive dietary advice to individuals and families with nutritional deficiencies, and where needed, to give multivitamin tables or other treatment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Help mothers who themselves or their children are malnourished, with practical dietary advice and with demostrations whenever possible, of balanced meals.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Be an example in the community for improving nutritional status practise what you teach.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Nutrition
104</p>
<ol start="13">
<li>
<p>Have a good programme of nutrition education, focussing on target groups, mothers, grandmothers, dais, schoo teachers. Take every opportunity for nutrition education in homes, clinics, school and community centres.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Evaluate the health education. Simple methods include checking the weightss of children and when visiting homes see if mothers know and are carrying oyut what has been taught.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cultural-factors-food-fads-and-habits">CULTURAL FACTORS, FOOD FADS AND HABITS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cultural-factors-food-fads-and-habits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The foods eaten by a family depend a great deal on their religion, social customs, traditional beliefs, family habits and food fads. Some traditional food habits are good, but others are not so good and may be harmful. We have to understand the customs and beliefs of families before starting nutrition education. Religion has a great influence on food habits in all parts of India. Hindus do not eat beef, and Muslims have no pork. Fasting at certain times is a practice in some religions. Muslims consider that eating and drinking from a common dish or cup is a sign of brotherhood. Vegetarianism is honoured among Hindus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vegetarian-and-non-vegetarian-deits">Vegetarian and Non-vegetarian Deits:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vegetarian-and-non-vegetarian-deits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Some families are pure vegetarians, taking no milk, eggs, meat, fish, poultry etc. Such families have a balanced diet only if they eat a good mixture of foods containing plant proteins at every meal. If enough pulses and nuts, especially soyabean or groundnuts, are added to the staple food, the deit can be a balanced one.</p>
<p>Vegetarians who include milk, and more so those who include eggs, can more easily have a balanced diet.</p>
<p>Non vegetarians may include as much as they can get of milk, eggs meat, chicken and fish.</p>
<p>In developed countries, non vegetarians sometimes eat too much of the animal protein foods, and may become sick with hypertension, heart disease or gout.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="food-habits-and-customs">Food Habits and Customs:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#food-habits-and-customs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is common in India for the men to eat first, next the children, and last the women. This means that even when pregnant or lactating, many women have a very poor diet.</p>
<p>During pregnancy, it is thought that the women needs to eat less so that the baby will not grow too big and cause a difficult delivery. In some societies foods such as eggs, fish, meat, milk and leafy vegetables are not allowed during pregnancy. Papaya fruit is thought to produce abortion and should not be eaten by pregnant women.</p>
<p>After giving birth, the mother may be given a diet of only</p>
<p>105 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>bread and coffee or chappati with a watery curry.</p>
<p>There are harmful practices also related to the feeding of infants and children. Some families believe that the baby needs nothing more than breast milk for the first year of life. If the mother becomes pregnant breast feeding is stopped suddenly, and the child is expected to eat the same meals as the family.</p>
<p>It is believed that a sick child should not be fed if he refuses food, and that a child with diarrhoea should be given liquids as it will make the diarrhoea worse.</p>
<p><strong>Food Fads:-</strong></p>
<p>In selecting foods, people are influenced by personal likes and dislikes, and fear of eating certain foods. Food fads often prevent people from having a balanced diet.</p>
<p>In some places there is fear that fish and milk taken together will cause leprosy or white patches (leucoderma). Others think that drinking a lot of water makes a person fat. Many people eat only white polished rice as staple food, and refuse other staple foods.</p>
<p>There are different beliefs about 'hot' foods and 'cold' foods. Hot foods may include wheat, meat, eggs., nuts, and oilseeds, and are thought to increase body heat and cause boils and fever. Cold foods include fruits, vegetables and milk, and these are thought to reduce body heat and cause cold, sore throat or cough.</p>
<p>There is not scientific basis for these beliefs and fears, but they add to the problem of malnutrition. They can only be overcome by nutrition education. For example without condemning the belief in 'hot' and 'cold' foods, we can tell people about another way of grouping foods: body building, energy, and protective foods.</p>
<p><strong>Food Adulteration:</strong></p>
<p>Food adulteration means any practice by which the quality of food sold is changed, or is given a false lable so that the person buying the food is decieved.</p>
<p>The prevention of Food Adulteration Act lays down certain minimum standards, and any food that does not meet the standard is said to be adulterated. The persons responsible can be brought to trial and punished severely. The aim of this is to try to ensure that people get proper nutritive value in the value in the foods they buy, and to avoid danger to health.</p>
<p>The Health Worker should be alert to local food adulteration practices. This subject should be included in health educa-</p>
<p>Nutrition
106</p>
<p>tion of the community, with the following points:</p>
<ol>
<li>Type of foods which may be adulterated and in what way?</li>
<li>Simple methods of finding out the adulteration.</li>
<li>The action to be taken:
a. The food may be rejected at the time of purchase.
b. A sample may be shown to the Health worker or village head.
c. The village council members should gather evidence from more families, and make a report to the health inspector.</li>
</ol>
<p>Food adulteration practices vary in different areas. Here are a few examples and hints on detection:</p>
<ol>
<li>Milk is often watered and may have powder of some kind added to it. When it is boiled, it will appear different from pure milk.</li>
<li>Rice or wheat often has stone chips and soil added. This can be found out when washing and cleaning the grain.</li>
<li>Chilly poder may have powdered brick added. When it is mixed in water the brick powder does not dissolve.</li>
<li>Ghee is adulterated by adding pork fat or dalda. On heating, the smell and taste will be different.</li>
<li>Coffee may be moxed with the skins of tamarind seeds, because it causes paralysis if taken for a long period.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nutrition-education">Nutrition Education<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrition-education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Nutrition education is of prime importance in improving the health of families and of the communities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-to-be-considered">FACTORS TO BE CONSIDERED:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-to-be-considered" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The Health Worker will need to keep in mind the following factors in relation to nutrition education.</p>
<ol>
<li>Culture, religion, food habits and fads.</li>
<li>Foods available locally, and water supply.</li>
<li>Educational level of the groups.</li>
<li>Economic status of the families.</li>
<li>Land available for food production.</li>
<li>Housing and environmental sanitation.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-nutrition-education-and-opportunities">PRINCIPLES OF NUTRITION EDUCATION AND OPPORTUNITIES:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-nutrition-education-and-opportunities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="principles-include-the-following">Principles include the following:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-include-the-following" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>First observe and ask questions to learn about the culture and food habits of the people, and what food are available?</li>
<li>Do not expect people to change food habits easily. New ideas should be introduced gradually, and only one thing taught at a time. Any suggested changes should be acceptable, and integrated into the present cultural practices.</li>
<li>Help people to see that good nutrition is important for them, eg.</li>
</ol>
<p>107 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>if they want their children to grow strong and do well at school, enough of the right kinds of foods must given to them.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>
<p>Find out the local food words so that there will be good communication.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In teaching, use actual foods whenever possible, especially home produced foods. Teach also with nutrition posters, flip charts, puppets role play etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Always encourage questions and discussions, to clear doubts. Ask those who have tried out something new to tell others about it.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Link your teaching on nutrition with MCH activities and with other health education.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Do not teach people things it is not possible for them to do, nor about foods they cannot afford to buy or cannot get.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Follow up and find out if families are making the needed changes in food practices. Use the information to modify your teaching.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="opportunities-for-nutrition-education-are-as-follows">Opportunities for nutrition education are as follows:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#opportunities-for-nutrition-education-are-as-follows" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>When visiting families for any reason, the Health Worker may help them in learning better budgeting selection, sorage, preparation and cooking of foods. VHGs and Dias who have been specially trained in nutrition can help the mother in practical ways.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In the antenatal clinic and at the preschool clinic, there will be opportunities for both group and individual nutrition education.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A nutrition education programme for mothers, including cooking demonstrations, can be arranged at the sub centre, Mahila Mandal, or other centre.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutrition education is an important part of the school health programme. It may be linked with a school midday meals programme.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>On village visits, the Health worker should visit any Balwadis or Anganwadis, see what diet is being served, and give teaching as needed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If there is nutrition Rehabilitation Centre, this gives opportunity for intensive teaching and supervision of mothers in feeding her child in a better way.</p>
</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-and-media">METHODS AND MEDIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-and-media" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As we have seen is very difficult to get people to change their dietary habits. Therefore the methods and media used for health education need to be selected and used with great care. As far as possible it is best to get people involved in discussing</p>
<p>Nutrition
108</p>
<p>the issues and in practical activities.</p>
<p>In a class of mothers, most of them will have similar problems, perhaps connected with water supply, or fuel, or high price of foods. Some mothers may have some special problems.</p>
<p>Individual teaching is very useful to help mothers to solve some special problem, such as worry that her child is not growing well. for pregnant and nursing mothers, and those with children who are often sick, and likely to be malnourished, individual nutrition education is most important.</p>
<p>Individual nutrition education is best done in the home, where you may find various factors in the problem such as poor environmental sanitation, or no place to store food.</p>
<p><strong>Cooking demonstrations are very useful for a group of mothers.</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Have the class in a place where mothers can sit comfortably. It may be under a tree in the village.</li>
<li>Cooking utensils and fuel should be familiar to them, perhaps borrowed from a nearby home.</li>
<li>Select a recipe using foods that are locally available, in season and not costly.</li>
<li>Select a preparation the mothers are interested to learn to do, and which will help them to feed a small child or the family in a better way.</li>
<li>On a clean surface place the foods to be used and the utensils so that everyone can see clearly.</li>
<li>Make sure you wash your hands before starting the preparation, so that the mothers learn to practice clean cooking.</li>
<li>Keep foods covered to protect from flies and dust.</li>
<li>When the cooking is over, taste some and invite the mothers also to taste it.</li>
<li>If possible let one or more of the mothers also demonstrate the preparation.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>KIthen Gardens:</strong> Have a model kitchen garden at the sub centre if possible. Encourage village leaders to organise a kitchen Garden competition and give prizes.</p>
<p>Other methods of nutrition education which are useful and interesting for groups such as mothers or school children include puppet shows, role plays and folk dances with songs.</p>
<p><strong>Classess for Fathers:</strong> Fathers also need to know what foods are best for infants, children, pregnant and nursing mothers. They also need to understand the need for mothers to be</p>
<p>109 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>given enough money to buy foods in adequate amounts, for everyone in the family to have a good balanced diet. Perhaps the men will like to come to a special meeting where they can learn these thins. This will go a long way in improving family nutrition.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction-to-hygiene">Introduction to Hygiene:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction-to-hygiene" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Hygiene is the Science of Health and its preservation. The term also refers to practices that are conductive to good health. Good personal Hygiene usually means those measures a person takes to keep his skin and its appendages (his hair, finger nails, and toe nails) and his health &amp; mouth clean and in good condition.</p>
<p>Physical health is an important component of total health. The subject of physical health includes care of the skin, hair, teeth, eyes, ears, hands, feet, rest &amp; sleep, exercise, recreation &amp; posture. The students must know not only the anatomy of the body organs but also known how these can be maintained in a state of optimum health.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="definition">Definition:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The science of preserving and promoting health is known as hygiene,</p>
<p>Hygiene has two aspects</p>
<ol>
<li>Personal Hygiene</li>
<li>Environmental Hygiene</li>
</ol>
<p>The Subject of personal hygiene is physical health and how to maintain it.</p>
<p>Preventive medicine is defined as "The Science and art of preventing decease,</p>
<p>Prolonging life &amp; promoting physical and mental health and efficiency"</p>
<p>Whereas in preventive medicine the focus is on the individual in community health.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="personal-hygiene-helps-in-the-following-manner">Personal Hygiene helps in the following Manner:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-hygiene-helps-in-the-following-manner" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>To maintain a good and clean physique.</li>
<li>To maintain good muscle strength</li>

<li>To maintain a healthy skin</li>

<li>To maintain resistance and prevent infection</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="principles-relevant-to-hygiene">Principles relevant to Hygiene:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-relevant-to-hygiene" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<li>The infect skin is the body first organ to defense against infection and injury.</li>
<li>Individual differences exit in the nature of the skin and its appendages.</li>

</ol>
<p>111 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>(4) The health of the skin and mucus membrane is highly dependant on adequate nourishment, fluid intake and exercise.</p>
<p>(5) A person general health affects both the status of his skin and appendages, teeth and mouth.</p>
<p>(6) Hygiene practices are learnt.</p>
<p>(7) Hygiene practices vary with cultural norms, personal values and ability to maintain good habits of cleanliness and grooming.</p>
