<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-in-the-home">Health in the home:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-in-the-home" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Housing is an important part of man's physical environment where he spends most part of his time. House is meant not nearly the physical structure providing for shelter, but also include necessary facilities, services, equipment and devices needed for the physical and mental health and social well being of the individual and the family.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="functions-of-the-house-are">Functions of the house are :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#functions-of-the-house-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>It satisfy physical needs, it facilitate for rest, recreation and exercise.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Psychological needs: It provides cleanliness and privacy for leading family life and helps for promotion of mental health.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Health Needs:- It consist of safe and adequate water supply, facilities for safe disposal of excreta and other wastes, facilities for washing bathing, facilities for storage, preparation and cooking of food and free from insects, rodents and vermin.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Protective needs: A house is asafe from accidents, fire, gas and other hazards.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Standards of housing :- The following standards of housing have been recommended by the environmental hygiene committee (1949) in India.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Site :- House must be located in healthy locality. Avoid building on clay soil or damp soil. It should not subjected to flooding during rains. It should be away from dust, smoke, smell and noise.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Open Space:- House should be in proper lighting and ventilation. There should be open place all around the house. In rural due to plenty of land the house should be build up not exceed 1/3 rd of total area and in urban area 2/3 rds.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Walls:- Walls should be reasonably strong, and unsuitable for rats and vermin. A 9" birck wall plastered smooth will meet the above requirement.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Floor:- It must have a hard surface Eg: cement or stone floor. So that it can be easily washed and kept clean and dry. It</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Hygiene
134</p>
<p>should be free from dampness.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Roof:- The width of the roof should be not be less than 10 feet.</li>
<li>Rooms:- The number of living rooms should not be less than 2 or not less than 50 sq. feet per person.</li>
<li>Floor space:- It should be 50 sq. feet per person.</li>
<li>Doors and windows:- Doors and windows combine should have 2/5th of the floor area.</li>
<li>Facilities:- These should be separate kitchen, a latrin, a safe water supply and washing and bathing facilities.</li>
<li>Safety from fire and other accidents.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Rural Housing:-</strong></p>
<p>Most people in villages are living in thatched huts which do not meet requirements of health. Huts an dark with low roof and without windows. The size is not enough for family and besides cattle, goat and hens are rearing and also no sanitary facility. Fire hazards are very easy.</p>
<p>Nows huts are replaced by better houses. In rural area the standard expected of houses are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Atleast two living rooms.</li>
<li>A separate kitchen and storage facilities.</li>
<li>A sanitary latrine.</li>
<li>Doors and windows.</li>
<li>Sanitary well or tubew well wih in 1/2 km.</li>
<li>Cattle shed to be at least 25 feet away.</li>
<li>Proper arrangements for disposal of refuse and waste water.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Due to poor Housing:-</strong></p>
<p><strong>The common Home Hazards:-</strong></p>
<p>The adverse effects of poor housing on man's health are explained as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Over crowding causes Spread of :-</li>
</ol>
<p>a. Respiratory infections such as common cold, tuberculosis, diphtheria, bronchitis, influenza.
b. Skin Diseases: Scabies, ring worm, leprosy.</p>
<p>The Health worker needs to educate families on the risks of over crowding and inadequate ventilation.</p>
<p>135
Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Open fire and smoke in the home, cause the following hazards:
a. Children get burns and scalds.
b. Women cooking - sari may catch fire.
c. Fire hazards especially in thatched houses.
d. Smoke is harmful to eyes and respiratory tract.</li>
</ol>
<p>The family should be encourage to build a smokeless chula, advantages of which are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Smoke is gone out through chimney, so that irritation of the eyes, nose and throat can be reduced.</li>
<li>Usage of fuel is decreased.</li>
<li>The walls of the kitchen may not become black due to smoke.</li>
<li>It is simple and cheap to construct and use.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="3">
<li>Badly constructed houses have the following hazards:
a. They may collapse, causing severe injury or death.
b. Leaking roof and dampness cause ill health.
c. Cracks in walls and floor encourage insects and rats carrying disease.</li>
</ol>
<p>House holders should be helped to improve the state of repair be safety of their houses for better health are should construct better house.</p>
<p><strong>Ventilation and lighting:-</strong></p>
<p><strong>Defenitation :-</strong> Ventilation may be defined as exchange of air between outdoors and indoors. By this the stagnated air in the house is replaced by a supply of fresh air from outside.</p>
<p>In a well ventilated room the air is:</p>
<ol>
<li>Constantly circulating.</li>
<li>Of comfortable temperature.</li>
<li>60% of moisture in the air.</li>
<li>Free from smoke and other impurities and unpleasant smells.</li>
</ol>
<p>Poor ventilation has the following effects on the room occupants:</p>
<ol>
<li>Yawning, fatigue, irritability, and lessened efficiency.</li>
<li>Feeling of heat sweating and may be fainting.</li>
<li>Poor appetite.</li>
<li>Insomnia (Sleeplessness)</li>
</ol>
<p>Hygiene
136</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Headaches.</li>
<li>Spread of infections such as colds, and lowered resistance to infections.</li>
<li>Irritation of eyes and air passages if smoke is present.</li>
</ol>
<p>The recommended standards of ventilation on are:</p>
<ol>
<li>Floor space of 50-100 sq. feet per person.</li>
<li>Air change in living rooms two or three changes per hour, in work rooms four to six changes.</li>
</ol>
<p>Types of Ventilation: There are 2 types of ventilation.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Natural Ventilation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Artificial or mechanical ventilation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Natural Ventilation:-
In India this is most by means of doors and windows. This is brought about by means of certain forces are wind, diffusion, temperature.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Wind:- It brings about natural ventilation by its movement.</p>
<p>Diffusion:- or Spreading out, the gases is called diffusion.</p>
<p>Temperature:- Temperature between indoors and outdoors is different. Then the movement of air from hotter region to colder region to become normal temperature.</p>
<p>Doors and windows facing each other provide, what is known as "Cross ventilation".</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Artificial Ventilation:-
This is done by following way.</li>
</ol>
<p>a. Electric fans: Electric Fans are the simplest means. In a closed room electric fans above will not ensure adequate ventilation.
2. Air conditioners:- The principle in that fresh air is drawn into the room by an electric fan or pump the air is filtered and moistened, and cooled or warmed as required. An airconditioned room must have spring doors which are kept shut, and no open windows.
3. In large halls: a bigger water cooler is implanted to proper fresh air to all parts and withdraws the impure air.</p>
<p>LIGHTING</p>
<p>137 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>Good lighting is essential for proper vision and health of eyes. The requirements of good lighting are :</p>
<p>a. Sufficiency – The intensity of light must be sufficient.</p>
<p>b. Destribution :- of light must be uniform.</p>
<p>c. Absence of glare: Glare means excessive brightness. It hurts the eye &amp; decrease critical vision. It is important cause of accidents.</p>
<p>d. Absence of sharp shadows:- It should not present in the field o vision.</p>
<p>e. Steadiness:- The source of light should be constant.</p>
<p>f. Colour : The colour of light is not important as long as the intensity adequate.</p>
<p>Measurement of light: - The light should be measured in foot candles.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Foot candles</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Living room 7</td></tr><tr><td>Reading Room 6-10</td></tr><tr><td>Bed Room 4-6</td></tr><tr><td>Types of lighting are two.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<ol>
<li>Natural Lighting:-</li>
</ol>
<p>It is derived mainly from the sky and party by reflextion. It depends upon the time of day, season, weather and clouds.</p>
<p>It is affected by the facing of building to north or south, size and shape of windows. the colour of walls and ceilings. It should always white.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Artificial lighting:- It may not depends upon day light during all hours. Not only during night time sometimes, we need artificial light during day time. It is from electric bulbs, tube lights etc.,</li>
</ol>
<p>Tube lights are cool and efficient.</p>
<p>Disposal of refuse:</p>
<p>Refuse means any kind of waste material. Solid refuse is applied to, refuse from houses, street sweepings, commercial and industrial and agricultural operations. Exereta means human urine and faces. Improper disposal of these wastes are caused ill health in the community.</p>
<p>Hygiene
138</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-refuse-and-hazard">Types of Refuse and hazard:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-refuse-and-hazard" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Dry refuse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wet refuse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dry refuse or solid refuse contains 1. Garbge, kitchen, waste, left overfood.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Rubbish, waste paper, broken glass, bottles, and tins, bits of metal, plastic and rags.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ashes from burning wood. Charcoal and cow dung fuel.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Animal dung,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Street sweepings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fallen leaves.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dead animals.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-various-hazards">The various Hazards:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-various-hazards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Breeding of flies and other insects and rats.</li>
<li>Encouraging of dogs and cows.</li>
<li>Growth of bacteria, and spread of infection by means of flies, dust and contamination of water supply.</li>
<li>Unpleasant sights and smells.</li>
<li>Danger of falls, Eg: Due to fruit skin on paths.</li>
<li>Piles of refuse may be a fire hazard.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wet-refuse-or-liquid-waste">Wet Refuse or liquid waste:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wet-refuse-or-liquid-waste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>(Sullage water) in a rural community consists of</p>
<ol>
<li>Waste water from houses after washing clothes, utensils, vegetables, bathing etc.</li>
<li>Waste from public wells and washing places.</li>
<li>Waste water from cattle shed and market places.</li>
<li>Waste water from industries.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hazards">Hazards:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hazards" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Liquid wastes from pools and cause.</p>
<ol>
<li>Mosquito breeding.</li>
<li>Risk of polluting water supply.</li>
<li>Dampness of house and danger to foundation of building.</li>
<li>Bad smell.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-disposal-of-dry-refuse">Methods of Disposal of Dry refuse:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-disposal-of-dry-refuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Refuse should never be thrown on the ground nor swept into a corner. If it is not disposal property, it must be put into abin.</p>
<p>139 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>Any thing wet or must should be first wrapped in paper:</p>
<ol>
<li>The refuse bin should have well - fitting lid to protect refuse from flies and others insects, crows, rats and dogs.
b. Be made of plastic or metal which is easy to wash.
c. Be emptied daily and disposed of by a safe method.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods">Methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Burning:- This is the best method of refuse disposal
a. In cineration: By this method bacteria will be killed and refuse reduced to a small amount of ash. It should be carried away from houses to avoid smell and smoke, preferably in an incinerator. In this a chief drawback is that the refuse is a loss to the community in terms of manure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Feeding to animals:-
Left over food and vegetables waste may be fed to animals such as pigs. A separate bin may be kept for this purpose.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Burrying:-
In a pit or trench, 3 ft deep, to prevent dogs or rats from getting at the refuse. Every time when refuse is dumped, it must be covered with some soil. When done in a large, this is called "Controlled tipping method. The refused may be broken down by bacteria into manure which may be used after 3-6 months. and the pits used again for fresh refuse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Composting: In rural areas this is a very useful method. The compost pit is made as follows:
a. Select a site near to the house but away from any water source.
b. Dig a pit 3 metres x 3 metres x a metre deep, or a little larger if needed.
c. The walls of the pit may be lined with bricks.
d. Fill the pit with alternate layers of house refuse and cowdung in proportionf 3:1 and cover each layer with soil to avoid fly breeding.
e. From time to time the compost may be turned and mixed with a long pole.
f. The top layer should be of refuse covered with earth to about 30 cm. above ground lelel. When full, the compost pit is left forr 6 months, after which the contents can be used as manufreand the</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Hygiene
140</p>
<p>pit used again</p>
<p>g. Two such pits will be needed for alternative use.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li><strong>Incineration</strong>: Incineration is a form of burning which is the safest method of refuse disposal, especially for hospital refuse such as dirty dressings, but glass and tin should not be included.</li>
</ol>
<p>Properly constructed incinerators are built and should be well maintained. The resulting ash may be used for road making or repair.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Dumping on Land This is a method which can be used to fill up low-lying land, but is not without health hazards. The dumping ground must be well away from houses because it will attract files and rats, and have a bad smell.</li>
</ol>
<p>To lessen flies, the refuse may be burned. The land may later be used for cultivation.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Disposal of the Dead Depending on custom and religious practice, the following methods are used:</li>
</ol>
<p>a. Burying. Christians and Muslims preper this method. Adequate fresh land is needed. Graves are dut 3-5 feet deep. The burial ground should be on sandy loam soil, not too close to houses. There should be a wall around, and trees planted.</p>
<p>b. Cremation or burning. Hindus and Buddhists usually cremate their dead on the open pyre. Less land is required for this method, but fuel is needed. The cremation ground should be well away from any houses.</p>
<p>The modern method of cremation by the use of a furnace is quicker and uses less space.</p>
<p><strong>Excreta</strong>: The problem of diseases spread from faeces to mouth is very great in India. In rural areas it is common for people to pass motion on the ground and leave it uncovered.</p>
<p>Improper disposal of human exreta lead to the spread of disease in the following ways:</p>
<ol>
<li>Flies can convey germs and worm ova from faeces to food.</li>
<li>Drinking water may be contaminated by infected faeces.</li>
<li>Food may be contaminated by inadequate hand-washing after defaecation.</li>
<li>Vegetables and fruits may be contaminated with worm ova in</li>
</ol>
<p>141 Community Health Nursing - 1</p>
<p>soil or manure, and eaten raw without being washed or cooked.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Wet ground may be heavily infected with tetanus from the faeces of man or animals in soil.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Wounds or cracks in the skin may get infected with tetanus from the faeces of man or animals in soil.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cattle or pits may swallow tapeworm ova passed in human faeces, and later when the met is eaten after insufficient cooking, a tapeworm begins to grow in a new host.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Thus in numerous ways, by improper disposal of excreta, the following diseases are spread:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Bacteria diseases: Cholera, typhoid and paratyphoid fevers, bacillary dysentery.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Parasitic diseases: amoebiasis, intestinal worms such as hookworm, foundworm and tapeworm.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Virus diseases: poliomyelitis, and infectious hepatitis.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-disposal-of-dry-refuse">METHODS OF DISPOSAL OF DRY REFUSE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-disposal-of-dry-refuse" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Refuse should never be thrown on the ground nor swept into a corner. If it cannot be properly disposed of immediately, it must be put into a bin. Anything wet or moist should first be wrapped in paper.</p>
<p>The refuse bin should</p>
<p>a. have a well fitting lid to protect refuse from flies and other insects, crows, rats and dogs.</p>
<p>b. Be made of plastic or metal which is easy to wash.</p>
<p>c. be emptied daily and disposed of by a safe method.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-refuse-disposal">Methods of Refuse Disposal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-refuse-disposal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Feeding to animals: Left over food and vegetables waste may be fed to animals such as pigs. A separate bin may be kept for this purpose.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Burning: By this method bacteria will be killed and refuse reduced to a small amount of ash. Burning should be carried out well away from houses to avoid smell and smoke, preferably in an incinerator.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Burying: In a pit or trench 3 feet deep, to prevent dogs or rats from getting at the refuse. Each time refuse is dumped it must</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Hygiene
142</p>
<p>be covered with some soil. When done on a large scale this is called 'controlled tipping' method. Refuse is broken down by bacteria into manure which may be used at the end of 3-6 months, and the pits used again for fresh refuse.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="methods-of-disposal-of-wet-refuse-and-excreta">METHODS OF DISPOSAL OF WET REFUSE AND EXCRETA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#methods-of-disposal-of-wet-refuse-and-excreta" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="disposal-of-sullage-water">Disposal of Sullage water:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#disposal-of-sullage-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>If waste water collects, it has to be drained away to a safe place. Wherever water is scarce, the sullage water should not be wasted but made use of in such a way that there is no health hazard.</p>
<p>Drains should be well planned for free flow of water, and checked frequently for any blockage. The water must not be allowed to flow into a clean source of waster. It may flow into a kitchen garden or cultivated field, where it is used to help in growing food.</p>
<p>Papaya and banana trees are good for using up waste water and good food for the family.</p>
<p>If a kitchen garden is not possible, the drain should pass to a soakage pit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="soakage-pit-this-is-made-as-follows">Soakage pit: This is made as follows:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#soakage-pit-this-is-made-as-follows" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Select a place near the house where waste water runs out of the house.</li>
<li>Dig a pit 2 metres deep and 11/2 metres in diameter.</li>
<li>Fill the lowest 1/3 of the pit with stones and bricks of 3/4 size.</li>
<li>Fill the middle 1/3 of the pit with stones or bricks of 1/2 size.</li>
<li>Fill the upper 1/3 of the pit with stones or bricks of 1/4 size.</li>
<li>The waste water should flow into the soakage pit through a pipe. The pipe should be empty into a basket filled with straw and leaves which is placed in the middle of the upper part of the pit, and which serves as a filter. This basket should be removed and cleaned or replaced every 2-3 months.</li>
<li>Cover the top layer of the pit with a layer of earth to above ground level. Build a parapet 10 cm. high round the top of</li>
</ol>
<p>143 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>the pit to protect it from rain water.</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>
<p>The soakage pit should not be used in the rainy season (block off the drain).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the pit starts overflowing, it must be emptied, and the stones or bricks washed, dried and replaced.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Sullage from cattle sheds:</strong> Cattle shed floors should be washed daily and the waster drained away into a soakage pit.</p>
<p><strong>Disposal of Excreta:</strong> In urban areas there is water carriage system. Large pipes called sewers collect from house drains and carry away for treatment the excreta together with sullage water and rain water, called 'sewage'.</p>
<p>In rural areas, usually there is no public system of sewage disposal. Village people need to be shown a safe and practical method of excreta disposal.</p>
<p>It has been found that privately owned latrines are best, as they are most likely to be kept clean. Types of latrines are:</p>
<p>a. Service type.</p>
<p>b. Sanitary latrines.</p>
<p>c. Simple latrines.</p>
<p><strong>Service type Latrine:</strong> This type needs someone to collect and empty the buckets of nightsoil (excreta). It is not recommended except in case of sickness, when a commode or bedpan is needed.</p>
<p><strong>Sanitary Latrine:</strong> This is one which does not cause nuisance due to sight or smell, the excreta is not left exposed, and it does not pollute the soil nor any water source. The best type of sanitary latrine is the water seal pit latrine. This should be situated conveniently near to the house, but 15 metres from any water source. There should be space for a second pit which is due when the first pit is full. This latrine consists of:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Squatting plate made of cement concrete 3 feet square and 2 inches thick, with raised foot plates.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pan: This must have a smooth surface to prevent excreta sticking to the sides. It slopes from front to back.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Trap: This is a bent pipe 3" diameter, connected to the pan. It holds water and therefore acts as a water seal. The</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Hygiene
144</p>
<p>water seal (a) prevents smell from the excreta in the pit, and (b) prevents flies.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>
<p>Connecting Pipe: This is a 3" diameter pipe about 3 feet long. It connects to the trap and slopes down to the pit.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pit or Dug Well: This is 1 metre square or 1 metre diameter and 21/2 metres deep. It must be provided with a strong cover below ground level, which is covered with earth. Inside the pit, the excret is made harmless by anarobic bacteria.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Superstructure: This is for privacy and can be made of any material according to the means of the family.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Maintenance of the Latrine</strong> If carefully used and maintained, the latrine can last a family of five for 3 to 4 years.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Each time it is used for defaecation, the latrine must be flushed with 1 litre water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The squaring place should be washed frequently and kept dry and clean. Disinfectants should not be used as this would destroy the action of bacteria.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When the pit is full, the latrine cannot be flushed. A fresh pits should be dug, connected to the latrine structure and covered with the old pit cover. The old pit should be filled up with easrth, left for atleast six months, then the contents can be dug up and used as manure.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Simple Latrine</strong> for a camp, especially where there is shortage of water, or for a family where a sanitary latrine cannot be constructed, this type of latrine is suitable.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Dig a pit about 1/2 metre wide and 1-2 metres deep. It can be of any length. It should be atleast 20 metres from buildings and water source.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Make a platform of wood or cement, with a hole in the centre, to place over the pit. Make a wooden cover with handle.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Erect screens of local materials to surround the latrine. The screen can be moved along the trench as it is filled up. The used end of the trench provides good soil for plants.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Each time after use, throw in a little lime, ashes or soil, to reduce smell and keep flies away.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The latrine should be kept clean by careful use and</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>washing down when necessary.</p>
<p><strong>Bio-gas plant</strong> In India the use of biogas plant is being promoted. The plant is expensive to install, but once installed is of great benefit to the family or community using it. The principle is that night soil passes from latrine to a large covered container where decomposition takes place. Animal waste such as cowdung is added and the resulting gas can be piped into the building for use with a gas cooking plate.</p>
<p><strong>Sewage Purification</strong> Large quantities of sewage from a total community is offensive in smell and contains millions of bacteria. It has to be purified to protect the health of the community.</p>
<p>Two types of bacteria are involved in the purification of sewage:</p>
<p>The stages of sewage purification are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Screening</strong>: A metal screen strins out floating refuse such as bits of wood and rags. This refuse is disposed of by burying.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Grit changer</strong>: This is a long narrow trench where heavier solids such as sand and gravel will settle, to be removed later and used for roads or land fillings.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Primary Sedimentation Tank</strong>: The sewage flows through slowly for 6-8 hours while other solids settle and form a black mud called 'sludge'. The sludge is pumped out into another tank, while the upper liquid part called 'effluent' passes on to be further purified. Sludge is dried to make manure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Biological Treatment</strong> One of the following two types of treatment is used.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>a. <strong>Trickling filter</strong>: This is a round bed of stones. A pipe with a row of holes rotates at the top of the filter. The effluent flows through the pipe on to the filter bed. As it passes through, it gets oxidised by aerobic bacteria and is purified.</p>
<p>b. <strong>Activated Sludge Process</strong>: The effluent is kept in a tank for about 6 hours together with a dose of activated sludge. This sludge contains plenty of aerobic bacteria. By pumping air into the bottom of the tank, the mixture is agitated and oxidised. Harmful organisms such as cholera and typhoid germs are</p>
<p>Hygiene
146</p>
<p>distroyed by this process.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Final Sedimentation: The purified effluent is kept in a tank for 21/2 hours. The sludge that collects is rich in aerobic bacteria and some is used for the activated sludge process.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chlorination: Effluent from the Final sedimentation tank is chlorinated and is then safely allowed to flow into fields for irrigation or into rivers or streams.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Other methods of sewage disposal:</p>
<ol>
<li>Oxidation pond: This is a cheap and suitable method for a small community. It is an open pool 3-5 feet deep with an inlet and an outlet.</li>
</ol>
<p>The organic matter in sewage is oxidised, because of the presence of :</p>
<p>a) Sunlight In India this is usually in plentiful supply.
b) Bacteria which feed on the organic matter and produce carbon dioxide.
c) Algae in the pond. Algae uses up carbon dioxide and produces oxygen with the help of sunlight.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Land Treatment of sewage: This method is used in some towns. After screening, grit removal and primary sidementation, the effluent is used for cultivation certain food crops such as plantains and other fruits trees, and of some vegetables (not to be eaten raw).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sea Outfall sewage gets diluted and gradually oxidised in the sea, but there is a chance of solid matter getting washed back. If this method is used, the sewage should be carried well out into deep water.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>COMMUNITY EDCATION AND JOINT PLANNING FOR REFUSE AND SEWAGE DISPOSAL:</p>
<p>The health Worker in community should use every opportunity to educate people about the diseases spread by the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>Dry refuse left on the ground or in a heap, or thrown into water drains.</li>
<li>Water collections near houses and wells.</li>
</ol>
<p>147 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>
<p>Defaecating on the ground. Until they have built latrines, people should be taught to at least dig a hole for passing motion and to cover it with earth, as cats do.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Fly breeding and how flies go from excreta to food.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Spread of hookworm by walking barefoot on soil where faeces lie.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Next, plan and work together with the community to improve the environmental sanitation.</p>
<ol>
<li>Discuss with the community leaders and show the community how to:</li>
</ol>
<p>a. Keep streets and public places clean and free from refuse and flies.</p>
<p>b. Construct drains and dispose of sullage water in a safe manner.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Discuss with householders any plans they may have for disposal of refuse and excreta. Assists in shooting the site, obtaining materials, constructions and maintenance of units such as the following:</li>
</ol>
<p>a. Compost pit, especially when cattle are kept.</p>
<p>b. Kitchen garden.</p>
<p>c. Sanitary latrine.</p>
<p>d. Soakage pit.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Use acceptors in the community to demonstrate to others the successful use of these methods.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>SAFE WATER SUPPLY</strong></p>
<p>Wate is a basic human need. No-one can live without water. Water forms over half (57%) of the body weight, and without a supply of water a person will die within three days. A village or community cannot survive without water supply. Water is needed for:</p>
<p>Drinking and cooking.</p>
<p>Cleanliness - washing the body, clothes, house and utensils.</p>
<p>Food growing and for animals</p>
<p>Fire-fighting, industries, and for generating electricity.</p>
<p>Hygiene
148</p>
<p>Safe water supply is a basic health need. It is estimated that 50% of illness in India could be prevented by provision of safe and adequate supply of water.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-water-in-the-community">SOURCES OF WATER IN THE COMMUNITY :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-water-in-the-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Rain - may be collected and stored. It is very soft water and more suitable for washing than for drinking purposes.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Surface water:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Lakes, tanks and reservoirs.:</p>
<p>Town and cities often depend on water stored in reservoirs. Water from the 'catchment area' around is collected and sent to the water works for treatment/</p>
<p>In rural areas rain water may be collected in a large tank by means of a bund. Lakes are natural collections of water.</p>
<p>This water is usually contaminated by humans and animals and is unsafe for drinking purposes.</p>
<p>b) Streams, rivers and canals.</p>
<p>Rivers collect water from streams on their way to the sea. Some rivers are important for water supply, but it is always polluted and must be treated in the water works.</p>
<p>Canals are artificial water ways, made mainly for transport.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Ground Water:-</li>
</ol>
<p>Some rain sinks into the ground until it reaches an impervious layer such as rock or clay, where it forms sub soil water, or even deeper underground lakes and streams.</p>
<p>Ground water is safer than surface water and may require no treatment.</p>
<p>The supply is usually constant. Even in summer.</p>
<p>Disadvantages of ground water are:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>The water is hard because it has absorbed salts from rock and soil. Hard water means that more soap is needed, and that boilers and water pipes get clogged up or eroded.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It usually requires pumping.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-ground-water-are">Sources of ground water are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-ground-water-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Springs - Where ground water finds its way to the surface.</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Wells, which are of three kinds:</li>
</ol>
<p>a. Shallow wells: These contain sub soil water which may easily be polluted by sewage water.
b. Deep wells: These collect water from below the first impervious layer (of rock or clay) They can supply safe waster if proper precautions are taken.
c. Tube wells: These are usually very deep. Water is tapped by boring a tube into the ground, and a pump is attached.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260121-a53c9bb7.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg">
An unsafe Well</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-problems-of-impure-water">THE PROBLEMS OF IMPURE WATER:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-problems-of-impure-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A great deal of unnecessary disease and death in India is caused by contamination of drinking water.</p>
<p>Sources of contamination are:</p>
<ol>
<li>People defaecate on the banks of rivers and tanks.</li>
<li>People bathe, wash clothes and vessels, animals in or near the water source.</li>
<li>Bird droppings and leaves fall into the water.</li>
<li>Well water is contaminated by underground seepage from latrines, soakage pits etc.</li>
<li>Dirty vessels are used to collect water.</li>
<li>Dirty containers are used to store water.</li>
<li>Containers are uncovered and drinking water is exposed to dust, flies, rats ad birds.</li>
<li>Hands or unclean containers are put into the water to draw.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diseases-conveyed-by-water-water-borne-diseases-are">Diseases conveyed by water (water-borne diseases) are:-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diseases-conveyed-by-water-water-borne-diseases-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Bacterial Chelora, typhoid, and para typhoid, fevers, bacillary dysentery and diarrhoea.</li>
<li>Parasitic roundworms, guinea worms and amoebic dysentery.</li>
<li>Caused by virus is poliomyelitis, infectious hepatitis.</li>
</ol>
<p>Hygiene
150</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="safe-drinking-water-is">Safe Drinking water is :-<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safe-drinking-water-is" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Free from pathogenic organisms. Water should be tested for presence of faecal bacteria.</li>
<li>Free from harmful chemicals such as nitrates, lead or arsenic.</li>
<li>Potalbe, or fit for use in the home. It should be clear and colourless and have no smell. It should be neutral or slightly alkaline but not acid in reaction.</li>
<li>Pleasant to taste, and acceptable regarding amount of salts in the water.</li>
</ol>
<p>bicarbonates, chlorides and sulphates.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="protection-of-water-supply-and-purification-methods">PROTECTION OF WATER SUPPLY AND PURIFICATION METHODS:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protection-of-water-supply-and-purification-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is duty of Health workers to ensure that the water used by the community is safe for drinking. Duties of the MHW in rural areas include:</p>
<ol>
<li>Surveying the water sources in the community - samples should be collected in sterilised bottles and sent for analysis.</li>
<li>Chlorinating public water supply sources.</li>
<li>Seeing that pumps are in working order, and reporting those that are out of order to concerned authorities.</li>
<li>Educating the people about the importance of drinking only safe drinking water.</li>
<li>Advising on proper methods of storing drinking water.</li>
<li>Advising on methods of purifying water.</li>
<li>Taking steps to protect the people in case of an epidemic caused by contaminated water supply.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="protection-of-wells-a-safe-well-is-one-which">Protection of Wells: A safe well is one which:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protection-of-wells-a-safe-well-is-one-which" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Is on high ground and at least 15 metres away from any source of pollution such as latrines, refuse or soakage pit.</li>
<li>is a deep well or tube well, below the first impervious layer.</li>
<li>is lines with bricks and cement to a depth of at least 6 metres to prevent contamination by sub-soil water.</li>
<li>has a parapet wall of brick and cement of at least 70 cm from ground level, and a sloping cement platform with channel for carrying away the waste water (preferably to a vegetables garden or fruit trees).</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>has a cover, and no trees with overhanding branches nearby.</li>
<li>has a pump, or a special bucket with rope, kept free from contamination.</li>
<li>is never used for pot cleaning, clothes washing etc.</li>
<li>has a separate place nearby for washing clothes etc.</li>
<li>is cleaned out once a year, and disinfected regularly.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="chlorination">Chlorination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chlorination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By adding sufficient bleaching powder to water, it is disinfected and made safe to drink. This is called chlorination.</p>
<p>Wells should be chlorinated weekly, and other water sources whenever there is an epidemic of water-borne diseases.</p>
<p>The principle of chlorination is to add sufficient bleaching powder to ensure that the water contains 0.5 parts of chlorine per million parts of water, after 30 minutes of contact. 0.1 ml. of orthotoludine reagent is added to 1 ml. of the water in a test tube, and they yellow colour matched to find out the amount of chlorine. (O-T test)</p>
<p>To chlorinate a well you will need:</p>
<ol>
<li>a bucket with rope or chain.</li>
<li>bleaching powder in an air tight container.</li>
<li>container for measuring.</li>
<li>particulars about diameter of the well, depth of water and chlorine content of the bleaching powder you have.</li>
<li>notebook for recording.</li>
</ol>
<p>To calculate, for example in a well 4 feet diameter and water 10 feet deep, when chlorine content is 20 %, calculate as follows:</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>4</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>4</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>10</mn><mo>×</mo><mn>5</mn><mtext>&nbsp;(constant&nbsp;figure)</mtext><mo>=</mo><mn>800</mn><mtext>&nbsp;gallons&nbsp;of&nbsp;water&nbsp;in&nbsp;well.</mtext></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">4 \times 4 \times 10 \times 5 \text{ (constant figure)} = 800 \text{ gallons of water in well.}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">4</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">4</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">10</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">×</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">&nbsp;(constant&nbsp;figure)</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span><span class="mrel">=</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">800</span><span class="mord text"><span class="mord">&nbsp;gallons&nbsp;of&nbsp;water&nbsp;in&nbsp;well.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p>
<p>14 (cont.fig)</p>
<p><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex-error" title="ParseError: KaTeX parse error: Unexpected end of input in a macro argument, expected '}' at end of input: …aching powder.}" style="color: rgb(204, 0, 0);">800 \times 20 \text{ (% of chlorine)} = 50 \text{ gr. or } 37 \text{ grams of bleaching powder.}</span></span></p>
<p>20 (% of chlorine)</p>
<p>needed.</p>
<p>Next, fix the rope or chain to the bucket. Mix the calculated amount of bleaching powder in the bucket three - fourths full</p>
<p>Hygiene
152</p>
<p>of water. Then lower the bucket into the well and shake it about in the water. Take care not to disturb the bottom of the well.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="water-purification-in-the-home">Water Purification in the Home<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water-purification-in-the-home" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If water is obtained from a doubtful source, it should be purified in one of the following ways:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>By boiling</strong>: The waster should be kept boiling for 5 minutes. All water given to babies and young children must be boiled to prevent risk of disease.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>By chemical disinfection</strong>:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>a). Iodine 2 drops of 2% tincture per litre of clear water. Allow 20-30 minutes before drinking.</p>
<p>b) Potassium permanganate enough to make the water a good pink colour. This is not so reliable as the Iodine treatment, but is useful in the case of a cholera epidemic.</p>
<p>c). Bleaching powder: Make a bottle of strong solution by adding 25 gm in 1 litre of water. Keep the bottle top tightly screwed down. Use in the strength of 1 ml. to 5 litres of water, and let it stand for half an hour before using.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li><strong>Filtration</strong></li>
</ol>
<p>There are various types of domestic filters, but they do not remove the viruses of poliomyelitis and infectious hepatitis. Filters are expensive and require regular cleaning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="safety-in-storing-and-drawing-water">Safety in Storing and Drawing Water<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#safety-in-storing-and-drawing-water" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>The container must be clean and supplied with a suitable cover to prevent dust, flies and other insects, rats or birds from polluting the water.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Water should be poured out if the container is small enough. If not, the container should have a tap for drawing or dipper with long handle should be kept inside the container.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="water-purification-for-towns">Water Purification for Towns:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#water-purification-for-towns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The methods used are:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Storage and sedimentation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Filtration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chlorination.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Storage</strong>: This takes place either in the reservoir, or in storage tanks at the water works. Chemicals may be added to aid in</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>the coagulating and settling of solid materials, which sink to the bottom of the tank.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Filtration:- Large cement tanks are prepared, with collecting pipes at the bottom. The tanks are filled up in layers with large stones, then small stones and gravel, then sand about two feet deep on the top. Inlet pipes let in the water which floods over the filter and passes through, becoming clean in the process. when filtration becomes too slow, another filter bed is used while the first is cleaned.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Chlorination: Chlorine gas, a powerful disinfectant, is injected in to the water in measured doses. By this means any remaining bacteria are killed. Ammonia may be injected also, to remove the taste of chlorine and yet prolong its action.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Distribution of Water:</strong></p>
<p>From the water works, the purified water is pumped into protected storage tanks underground, or straight to overhead water towers. From the tower the water flows in water mains made of iron with well-sealed joints, and branches from these mains, called service pipes, go to the houses.</p>
<p>If the water supply is constant and plentiful, water can be taken directly from the tap at any time. If however, the supply is intermittent, then storage tanks are needed in houses, and these must be kept very clean and free from contamination.</p>
<p><strong>USE OF WATER IN PREVENTION AND TREATMENT OF ILLNESS:</strong></p>
<p>In David Werner's book 'Where there is no Doctor', many suggestions are given for ways of healing without the use of medicine, but by the use of water. Refer to that book for full details. Here is a brief summary.</p>
<ol>
<li>Drin Plenty of water.</li>
</ol>
<p>To treat diarrhoea and dehydration</p>
<p>For fever.</p>
<p>For minor urinary infections.</p>
<p>For Constipation.</p>
<p>For cough, bronchitis, asthma, whooping cough.</p>
<p>Hygiene
154</p>
<p>In summer, to prevent heat stroke and heat exhaustion, drink plenty of water with salt added.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Breathe hot water vapour to ease cough (inhalation)</li>
<li>Sniff salt water for stuffed up nose.</li>
<li>Gargle with hot salt water for sore throat and tonsillitis.</li>
<li>Wash hands and boil drinking water to prevent diarrhoea, worms and gut infections.</li>
<li>Wash wounds well with soap and water to prevent infection including tatanus.</li>
<li>Bathe often to prevent skin infections. In summer bathe many times a day in cold water to avoid heat stroke.</li>
<li>Scrub with soap and water for pimples, sores, impetigo, ringworm..</li>
<li>Hot soak or hot compresses for infected wounds, abscesses, boils, piles or anal fissure. Hot compresses also for stiff, sore muscles and joints.</li>
<li>Soak hand or foot in cold water in the case of minor burns.</li>
<li>Soak body with cool water for very high fever or heat stroke.</li>
<li>Cold compresses to forehead for fever, and for irritation of the skin.</li>
<li>Flood eye with cool water at once in case of strong chemical or foreign body in the eye.</li>
</ol>
<p>SUMMARY</p>
<ul>
<li>The Health worker should understand the importance of periodical health examination.</li>
<li>She assist while doing physical examination.</li>
<li>She should arranged the equipment ready for the Health examination.</li>
<li>Immunizations are used to prevent the dreadful diseases like, TB, Dyptheria, partusis, tetanus, measles, hepatitis, polio.</li>
<li>Vaccines must be stored in very low degree of temperatures.</li>
<li>The immunization schedule should be applied strictly to 0-1 year children will call protected child.</li>
<li>A house is not only gives shelter but also provides health.</li>
<li>The standards must be followed to construct home towards site, walls, windows, doors etc.</li>
</ul>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ul>
<li>There are various hazards due to improper housing eg. respiratory diseases, skin diseases etc.</li>
<li>A house must has good lighting and ventilation.</li>
<li>There is 2 type of water</li>
</ul>
<p>Refuse and excreta. These should be disposed in different methods to prevent communicable diseases and maintain good health.</p>
<ul>
<li>The animal sheds, insect and pets are properly cared.</li>
<li>The community is supplied by safe drinking water to maintain proper environmental sanitation. Every house has sanitary latrine.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mental-hygiene">MENTAL HYGIENE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mental-hygiene" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Def:- Mental Hygiene is mental health care from birth to death in sickness and in health. The aim of mental hygiene is to ensure mental health at all stages of life and to prevent mal adjustment and mental illness.</p>
<p><strong>Introduction:</strong> Mental Health is a component of total health. It is concerned not only with early diagnosis and treatment of mental disorders but also with the preservation and promotion of good mental health and prevention of mental illness. Mental Health and physical health are interrelated. A sound mind in a sound body is an ancient saying. Health is defined by the WHO, includes both physical and mental health and social well being. This is the modern concept of optimum health which mental health is an important component.</p>
<p><strong>Factors contributing to mentally healthy person:</strong></p>
<p>The foundations of mental health are laid in early childhood. The various factors which contribute to mental health may be stated as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p><strong>Good physical Health:</strong> Good physical health is the basis of the mental health. Proper functioning of all the systems of the body i.e., respiratory, cardio-vascular, digestive, nervous and endocrine is essential. Individuals who suffer from deformities, disabilities and chronic incurable diseases fall into mental illness very easily. Good physical health is therefore the first stepping stone to mental health.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Basic needs:</strong> The individuals cannot maintain proper mental health unless certain basic needs are met. These needs are explained as follows:</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>a. <strong>Physical needs:</strong> These are food, shelter, clothing, rest, recreation, sleep etc. which promote physical health. These are basic elementary needs of every person.</p>
<p>b. <strong>Psychological needs:</strong> The need for independence, affection, achievement and recognition are among the importance psychological needs which every individual craves for</p>
<p>Hygiene
157</p>
<p>c. Social needs:- These are needs for security, social status, praise etc. It cannot be possible to meet all the basic needs of given individuals. These are useful for the promotion of mental health.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Habits :- Certain habits contribute to good mental health. They are habits of work, study, play, rest and sleep. Control of onces emotions both in the home and outside the home learning to adjust to environment; showing appreciation for others and respecting the rights of others, cultivation of self confidence, setting reasonable goals for one self are some of the attitudes which one should habituated.</li>
</ol>
<p>Characteristics of a mentally healthy person:-</p>
<p>In order to know the mentally abnormal person in the community, the Health worker should know the mentally healthy person characters. They are listed below</p>
<ol>
<li>A mentally healthy person has good self control and not easily upset. Control of emotions like fear, anger, and love, expressing these in an acceptable manner and has learned to tolerate frustrations and disappointments.</li>
<li>He face problems and treis to solve then intelligently.</li>
<li>He adjusted to the environment well and able to get along well with others.</li>
<li>He feels to be satisfied with himself.</li>
<li>He does not pity himself.</li>
<li>He feels happy, calm and cheerful.</li>
<li>There are no conflicts and frustrations with in himself.</li>
<li>He accepted criticism and is not easily upset.</li>
<li>He understand emotional needs of others and tries to be considerable and courteous in his dealings with others.</li>
<li>He fuls secure in a group.</li>
<li>Able to think for one self, make ones own decisions, set reasonable goals, and face up to life's problems.</li>
<li>Appricate the others achievements and wins.</li>
<li>Able to develop friend ships, and be sensitive to their emotional needs and problems.</li>
</ol>
<p>158
Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ol start="14">
<li>Have meaning and purpose ones own life and work, develop talets and use time well. Responsible and dependable in duties.</li>
</ol>
<p>Mental health development or mental hygiene at different stages i.e. in infancy, early childhood late childhood, adolescence and adult hood and old are discussed in psychology chapters in III unit.</p>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="psychology">PSYCHOLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#psychology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Psychology is the basis of good nursing because the nurse comes in contact with patients, relatives, visitors, and colleagues in her daily work. She come and contact with people of all ages in the community. A knowledge of Psychology is essential for a nurse to know her self and others to differentiate between the normal and abnormal and to help promote mental behavior and to help promote mental health in individual &amp; families.</p>
<p>Psychology is defined as "The scientific study of behavior &amp; experience".</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-influencing-human-behavior">Factors influencing Human Behavior<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-influencing-human-behavior" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The main factors influencing human behavior are knowledge, beliefs, values, attitudes, skills, finance, and materials.</p>
<p>Time and the influence of family members, friends &amp; coworkers, opinion leaders and even health workers themselves. Some of the other factors influencing human behavior are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Environmental stimuli: sight, smell, stumuli etc.</li>
<li>Needs: Behavior influenced by his needs, wants</li>
<li>Emotions Feelings: These arises from with in the body Eg: Anger, joy, hunger. Behavior is also dependent on our feelings and emotions</li>
<li>Motivation: Without Motivation behavioral changes commit take place. Motivation is an force which achieves an individual to a contain action.</li>
<li>Intellectual Perception: A persons intellectual Perception thinking and reasoning can influence his behavior in a given stimulation that is why each individual behavior in ways which make sense to him</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="heredity-and-environment">Heredity and Environment:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#heredity-and-environment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Heredity seems to contribute to behavior development. Heredity always contribute to behavior with in context of particular Environment circumstances monozygotic twins are more similar to dizotic twins.</p>
<p>Environmental is also seems to contribute the behavioral development when identical twins that is same heredity and the same environmental reared together possess same Intelligent Quotient. The fraternal twins that is dissimilar heredity the same environment will shows the different twins dissimilar degree of Intelligent</p>
<p>Psychology
160</p>
<p>Quotient.</p>
<p>Characteristics like short temper ness, musical and artistic skills are passed genetically passed. Then parents provide the Environment for department in the early years.</p>
<p>Any behavioral Characteristics is determined by genetic factors Eg; Intelligence, perception, evaluation, reasoning etc other factors like blood group is totally determined by the genes.</p>
<p>Any amount of environmental modification cannot change such Characteristics. Some of the genetically determined Characteristics which are modified by Environment are phencyeketonuria which leads to MR. The dietary and other treatment procedures the disease can be treated. The factors like intelligence, stress tolerance are not traceable to any genes but indirectly affected by heredity. These factors are highly modifiable by Environmental influences.</p>
<p>The modern science has advanced that inherited characters like facial features can be changed by plastic surgery. A person who is undergone such change would naturally develop positive self image and his behavior will be different. This illustrate that the deliberate influence of Environment and more recent research shows that neither is heredity inflexible nor in Environment, all that effective.</p>
<p>Basic Needs or drives or Urges: These are divided into 3 types</p>
<ol>
<li>Biological Needs: Such as temperature, regulation, pain, sleep, hunger, thirst, sex drive and maternal drives, food water, oxygen, sexual.</li>
</ol>
<p>(i) Temperature regulation: An individual is active in maintain a comfortable state of warm and cold. A man may pull on a blanket if he feels cold or wear a sweater. He may open windows and switches on the fan if he feels hot.</p>
<p>(ii) Pains: The individual tries to achieve comfort by avoiding all sorts of painful stimuli. According to that the sense organs are activated</p>
<p>(iii) Sleep: It is one more physical drive for sleep is regulated by certain centers in the brain</p>
<p>(iv) Hunger: The motive of hunger gives rise to hunger, pangs. It coincides with stomach contractions and which depend upon blood chemistry. As the glucose level in blood raises the stomach contractions increases.</p>
<p>(v) Thirst: When deprived of water for a long time become ex-</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>cessively restless and needs intake of water and dryness of mouth and throat. so intake of water is essential for the individual.</p>
<p>Sex -drive: This drive dominate during childhood with the onset of puberty the sex glands are functioning. As a result the sex drive is stimulated</p>
<p>Maternal drive: Prolactin a hormone form anterior pituitary gland plays an important role in motivating maternal behavior</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Psychological Drives are curiosity and fear</li>
</ol>
<p>(a) Curiosity: It is close to drive exploration. Exploration is a drive that aids satisfaction of curiosity.</p>
<p>(b) Fear: It is learned drive. It motivate the individual to escape from fear producing situation.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Social Drives:- Some of social needs are common to all human beings some others are limited. These are well expresses in all our competitive activity. Social drives result from the specific environment of a individual. Some important social archives are as follows</li>
</ol>
<p>(a) Affiliation: Our need for affiliation is well expressed through our affiliation with associations, clubs and other institutions. Though marriage is partly a mean of satisfying sex drive also helps to satisfy many other needs including need for affiliation.</p>
<p>(b) Social Approval: We often show an almost compulsive tendency to conform to norms set by our social group. This may be result of constant parental directions in childhood as to what is right and what is wrong for child to do.</p>
<p>© The Power Drive: Desire to be in a position of control to be boss to give orders to command, respect and obedience is called the power motive. The power drive directs the behavior of dictators, and leaders, and the financial empires</p>
<p>(d) Dependency Motive: It develops from our baby hood. Baby is completely dependent upon their parents they gave us food, drink, warmth, comfort and relief from pain.</p>
<p>(e) Achievement Drive: Its powerful Drive in some societies. We are taught the value of working hard to achieve several social goals. Success is highly prized. The importance is varies from culture to culture. It seems to be especially among the middle groups. It is a healthy tendency for progress.</p>
<p>Psychology
162</p>
<p>Personality: Personality is a dynamic organization with in individual of those physiological system that determine his unique adjustments to his environment.</p>
<p>Personality is total pattern of characteristic ways of thinking, feeling and behaving that constitute the individual relating to this environment.</p>
<p>Personality implied certain physical and mental traits, which are characteristic of a given individual. The individual's behavior on adjustment to his surroundings.</p>
<p>Personality and self-concept:</p>
<p>Personality means being a person, unique and different from every other person. Personality is related to</p>
<ol>
<li>Goals and desires</li>
<li>Values, attitudes and interests.</li>
<li>Habits of thinking</li>
<li>Feelings and beliefs</li>
</ol>
<p>As the infant grows and learns to distinguish between himself and other people and things and understand the concept or meaning of the word me or self-structure develops, it becomes the important meaning of personality. In this the individual experiences and coping patterns are organized. We may consider the self as the third and final determinant of personality.</p>
<p>A child at an early age begins to be aware of himself as a person. His personality develops by social interaction. Thus every person in some respects is like all other human beings, like some human beings and like no other human beings. Personality is not the experiences of life.</p>
<p>Some of the experiences may harm the personality. They are fears, doubts, guilt feelings that may have started in childhood makes us afraid to show our real selves. The act of role-plays 'games' and hide behind different masks in our relations with other.</p>
<p>Perhaps we can become free from our fears and negative attitudes and begin to grow into what we can become.</p>
<p>Thus each person evaluate himself and develop adopting system in his or her own right way of life and may consider the self as the third and final determinant of personality.</p>
<p>Self - awareness and acceptance:</p>
<p>In order to function well in the community the health worker needs to develop personally and be able to help others grow.</p>

<p>Here are some suggestions for personal growing:</p>
<ul>
