<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="negative-and-positive-emotions">Negative and Positive emotions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#negative-and-positive-emotions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Negative emotions</strong> Negative emotions are those that give us an unpleasant feeling positive emotions are give pleasant feeling to the individual.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="anger">Anger<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#anger" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Its Negative emotions most often caused by some kind of frustrations. It is a reaction of offensive type. It is a destructive force. If it is not controlled it may impulse a person even to communicate murder or there is a quarrel, which may result in violence.</p>
<p>For peace &amp; harmony in relation with others we need to use self-control &amp; find acceptable ways of solving inter personal problems.</p>
<p>The emotion of anger is accepted by society when it is raised &amp; expressed against normal wrongs. If you see a child being cruelly treated it would be natural &amp; socially accepted for you to be raised &amp; to express your anger. Besides the feelings &amp; changes in body already mentioned your face will flush with anger &amp; eyes flash. Unless you can control yourself you may strike in your part would be going too far &amp; you may find you self in trouble.</p>
<p>Some times feeling of anger remains after it has been expressed in a mood of resentment or of self-pity. The face expressions mood. Any one aware of this behavior habit needs to face it &amp; overcome it with more positive attitudes &amp; pleasant feelings in order to help in developing a good personality.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="fear">Fear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#fear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Its common Negative emotions of a can help harm. When there is a danger, such as a building about to fall on us, fear is a raised. It may produce excitement or depression, fright. Our face becomes pale, eyes wide often. Internal changes prepare us to run &amp; get out of building fast so from this we can see how to emotion of fear can help to protect us from harm.</p>
<p>Some of common fears of man are fear of dark, fear of dogs, fears of snakes, fears of ghosts, fears of sickness, fears of death etc. when the fear becomes exaggerated or unnecessary its</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>called phobia. Such fears are common in points with mental disorders.</p>
<p>On the other hand if we are to be able to give first to injured people its necessary to control our own fear</p>
<p>A healthy fear is fear of God &amp; of people of authority a feeling of self worth and knowing your basic rights as an individual should balance this. The emotion of fear is regard to authority should be well under control in a mature person. In many of life's situations we need to use intelligence &amp; good judgment in place of fear.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="c-sorrow">(c) Sorrow<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-sorrow" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is an unpleasant emotion. This feeling shows in face, the eyes &amp; mouth turn down at corners. A tremor or a break comes in voice &amp; very often tears will flow when the reason for sorrows is void such as a hearing of the death of someone you know its is good to let tears flow for a while release the emotion. To control the tears in this case may lead to personality problems.</p>
<p>The emotion of sorrow may rise for yourself EG when scolded or punished for some error you should learn to control yourself accept your fault, ask excuse, &amp; resolve to do better never give away to self pity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="d-anxiety">(d) Anxiety<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#d-anxiety" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this a rapid pulse &amp; breathing, flushing, sweating, dry mouth, nausea, diarrhea, raised B.P etc. Patients admitted to hospitals are anxious. Anxiety leads to tension to pain the doctor must understand the patient's anxiety &amp; give him reassurance.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="e-jealousy">(e) Jealousy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#e-jealousy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a negative emotion, which may be a problem of yours if person is Jealousy</p>
<p>He may not happy with himself &amp; feels dissatisfied with life &amp; resents success &amp; happiness in others. You are Jealousy of a classmate who has better cloths or who gets a higher mark in tests than you such feelings need to be controlled because strong feeling or emotion of Jealousy should be raised in you It may result in you doing some harm to other person with out a good reason</p>
<p>A Jealousy person gradually losses self respect her own personality is poisoned by his emotions. Be aware of where it will lead</p>
<p>Psychology
184</p>
<p>you * change your attitude before such feelings become a habit.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="positive-emotions">Positive Emotions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#positive-emotions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are emotions that give us a pleasant feeling. These emotions are expressed freely in a happy young child. We adults also, whatever our age, need occasionally to act and feel as we did in childhood- to be free to laugh, play and have fun, to love and to show tenderness and affection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="joy">Joy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#joy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The emotion of joy is aroused when you receive good news, such as a pass in the examination. Your face lights up with an expression of pleasure. Your voice reveals excitement, and for a while you may laugh happily, and perhaps hug your classmates. However, if one or more of your classmates have failed, you will need to control your emotion of joy, and express sympathy.</p>
<p>As a child delights in simple pleasure such as a plucked flower, we all need to aware of things in nature or created art or in our religion, which can arouse within us joy. There is so much sorrow in the world - let us express joy and share it with others.</p>
<p><strong>Love</strong>: It is a feeling of attachment to some person. It is a basic emotion of man.</p>
<p>Love is more important than anything else in the world. Infants will not grow and may even die if love is not given to them. Everyone needs to love and be loved.</p>
<p>The emotion of love brings with it a feeling of affection. For good mental health of individuals and families, love needs to be kept alive by thoughtful acts of kindness, by understanding and trust. Selfishness, jealousy and suspicion can spoil the love between people.</p>
<p>Love of the highest kind is sacrificial, a giving of oneself without expecting reward. We see this in the work of Mother Theresa of Calcutta, who is filled with the love of God and expresses it in tender care of destitute and dying people.</p>
<p>The best health workers will be those who can offer this kind of loving, caring service to the community.</p>
<ol>
<li><strong>Emotion and health</strong>: Emotional status determines human behavior. Anger can cause a person to be rude and sarcastic. Disorders of emotion interfere with human efficiency. Lack of concentration, lack of appetite, increased risk of accidents, lack of sleep, palpitation etc. emotional disorders in children</li>
</ol>
<p>185
Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>appear in the form of temper tantrums, abdominal pain, spasms, tics and antisocial behavior such as aggressiveness.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>These are a group diseases called as psychological diseases that is mind acting on body e.g. essential HTN, peptic ulcer, asthma, ulcerative colitis which are attributed to disturbed emotional status.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="frustrations-and-conflicts">Frustrations and Conflicts<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#frustrations-and-conflicts" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Frustration is a condition of tension, because of something that stops us from satisfying our needs or desires.</p>
<p>Causes of frustration include the following</p>
<ol>
<li>Annoying things in daily life, such as electricity failure when we are reading or writing at night.</li>
<li>When plans cannot be carried out because of heavy rain, or being let down by someone.</li>
<li>When our income is not enough to meet our needs.</li>
<li>When family or social customs prevent us from doing something we had set our heart on doing.</li>
<li>When physical weakness or handicap hinders a person’s desire and ambitions.</li>
</ol>
<p>Frustrations are a necessary part of growing up. They should not be in excess and we should gradually learn to tolerate them, with the help of feelings of security and personal worth.</p>
<p>Frustration tolerance means being able to meet frustrating situation without being too upset. Continual frustrations of basic needs may lead to adjustment problems and mental illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="conflicts-are-related-to-frustration-types-of-conflicts-are">Conflicts are related to frustration. Types of conflicts are:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conflicts-are-related-to-frustration-types-of-conflicts-are" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Conflict with another person of group. The reason may be different ideals, attitudes, loyalties or standards of conduct, or it may be a clash of temperament.</li>
<li>Conflict with the environment, as when disaster such as fire affects someone personally.</li>
</ol>
<p>Psychology
186</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Conflict inside a person. For example you have a question you would like to ask the tutor, but are afraid of being thought foolish and ignorant. Or it may be you hate to do some assignment but you are afraid of being punished if you fail to do it. Or you would like to go to see picture but you know your parents would not approve.</li>
</ol>
<p>Conflicts may be conscious or unconscious. There are times when we are not aware of the real motives causing the conflict, but we feel some anxiety.</p>
<p>Conflicts cause tension, and should be ended as soon as possible, for which the help of a mature person may be needed. If conflicts continue, they are repressed or pushed down into the unconscious part of the mind, when they remain active.</p>
<p>Internal conflict is dangerous. It can cause emotional disorder and mental illness.</p>
<p><strong>Defense mechanism and behavior:</strong></p>
<p>Defense mechanism is different ways in which people may adjust to emotional conflicts and frustrations. The person using the defense mechanism may not be aware of them as they usually come from the unconscious part of the mind. We like to think we are in complete control of our behavior, but this is not so.</p>
<p>Defense mechanism are affected by experience and feelings of long ago in our childhood, and forgotten.</p>
<p><strong>Purpose of defense mechanism:</strong></p>
<p>When germs attack our bodies, there are several lines of defense to fight the germs and protect us from infection.</p>
<p>In a similar way, defense mechanism are deices of the mind for protecting us against frustration or stress situation we feel unable to cope with.</p>
<p>The main purpose, then, of defense mechanism is to protect our ego. Other purposes are to relive tension, to overcome feelings of failure, and to maintain inner harmony.</p>
<p><strong>Common defense mechanism:</strong></p>
<p>The stresses and strain caused by frustration and conflicts are uncomfortable, even painful. The following are common defense mechanisms used whether consciously or un-</p>
<p>187 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>consciously to get relief.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Compensation
When in spite of all efforts, a person fails in something and the ego is threatened, the person may look for some other area in which to succeed. If a health worker student feels frustrated by her tutor but cannot say anything, she may compensate by an out burst among classmates.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Negativism
A person, who has been used to having his/her own way, may react to frustration by defiance, doing the opposite of what is expected. By resisting other suggestion the person keeps up his own ego.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sympathism
Instead of facing a problem, we may turn to others for sympathy. A health worker student who is not doing well in studies, instead of seeking the cause and trying harder, may get sympathy by telling of various personal difficulties or by suggesting she is just unlucky.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Projection
We all tend to blame others or circumstances instead of admitting our own failure. It is common for people to criticize others and not see those same faults in themselves.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Identification
If you cannot achieve some goal, you may identify yourself with those who have achieved it. This may help at the time, but if this defense mechanism becomes a habit, you may be continued to feel satisfied with achievement of the group, and make no effort on your own.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Sublimation
Great works of art, music, or science are often due to sublimation because of frustrated love.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>An unmarried woman can sublimate her material urge by finding some job of working with children.</p>
<p>If you should feel angry and want to attack someone, but you know this would be wrong, it is good if you can play some vigorous game to work off the tension.</p>
<ol start="7">
<li>Rationalization is a popular mechanism. We excuse our failings by giving several other</li>
</ol>
<p>Psychology 188</p>
<p>reasons, which seem to justify our action. We hide the real and true reasons. We may not realize that we are twisting truth and deceiving ourselves. If we use this mechanism often, we may lose all sense of what is true.</p>
<ol start="8">
<li>
<p>Regression is returning to a childish level of behavior instead of facing up to problems. A student who is not making progress may cry or sulk, or plead that she has a headache, when told to do an assignment.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Withdrawal</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Failure and criticism cause some people to become timid and withdrawn. They fear failure so much that they refuse to face problems and bear responsibilities.</p>
<ol start="10">
<li>Repression</li>
</ol>
<p>This is an unconscious way of forgetting. Emotions, which do not fit in with social values and norms, such as hatred for parents, are dealt with by our ego forcing them down in to the unconscious mind. Many unpleasant experiences of early childhood are repressed. We are not aware of these, but repressed emotions may come to the surface in the form of antisocial behavior.</p>
<p>ADJUSTMENT:</p>
<p>By means of defense mechanism, we are able to make adjustment to stresses and strains and keep mentally healthy. Many of our adjustments make use of several of these mechanisms at one time. We are usually not aware of how our ego is making adjustment, as these go on in our unconscious minds. We only realize that we feel more comfortable with ourselves as a result.</p>
<p>When there is steady development from infancy, adjustments are made in a simple way and the ego does not need to depend much on defense mechanisms.</p>
<p>On the other hand, a maladjusted person uses them a great deal and may develop mental illness in which such defense mechanisms are constantly being used.</p>
<p>189
Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stress-illness-and-behavior">Stress, illness and behavior:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stress-illness-and-behavior" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Stress includes anything, which produces alarm reactions in our bodies, to give energy for fight or flight. Adrenaline is released and in small doses this is helpful. It gives energy for activities, also helps to train us in facing frustration and in solving problem. Stress in too large a dose, or in continuous small doses is harmful and result in physical and mental illness.</p>
<p>Stress comes to everyone, but affects people in different ways. Our mental and physical health depends on how we react to the stress. In a busy life we need to take time off for relaxation, and time to be alone, to pray and meditate, so as to be renewed with strength and power to overcome, to react in a positive way to the stresses and strains of life.</p>
<p>Illness is very often caused or made worse by stress. Illness upsets a person in every way. Besides changes in the body, illness affects mind and emotions, producing changes in behavior.</p>
<p>Behavior in illness varies a great deal, according to the patient’s personality and previous experience of illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-the-complaining-patient">1. The complaining patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-the-complaining-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Illness causes a person to feel inadequate and that he has lost his self-esteem. He may react by finding fault, blaming others, resenting hospital restrictions. He may lose his usual emotional control and be very difficult. You will need to have much patience with this type of patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-the-dependent-childish-patient">2. The dependent, childish patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-the-dependent-childish-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Some patients react to illness with dependence like a child, demanding a lot of attention and sympathy. Without getting irritate, the health worker will need to combine patience, tact and firmness in dealing with this type of patient. Avoid creating him/her as a child. By maintaining an attitude of respect for the patient as a person, the patient may be gradually helped to give up the childish behavior and move on to independence as he/she recovers from the illness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-the-silent-patient">3. The silent patient<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-the-silent-patient" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Another patient may react to illness by being withdrawn and silent, asking no questions and making no demands. Inside, the patient may be full of fears and worries. There may be a sense of guilt. The health worker needs to show affection, sympathy, kindness and interest, which will help to give confidence to the patient to respond and get release by talking about his feelings.</p>
<p>Psychology
190</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="recovery">RECOVERY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recovery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Stress may also prevent a patient from recovering.</p>
<p>The health worker should prove a restful environment and try to help the patient to understand and resolved both health and emotional problems, and start life a fresh.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Emotions are mental forces, which rise up suddenly inside us.</li>
<li>An emotion is a strong feeling of the individual.</li>
<li>Emotions can cause internal and external changes to the individual.</li>
<li>The emotions are important and have great value in life.</li>
<li>Emotions are major barriers of communication.</li>
<li>Vocal qualities, body movements and facial expressions can express emotions.</li>
<li>A well-adjusted and mentally healthy person is one who is able to keep his emotions under his control.</li>
<li>For adult happy family life is basic for emotional adjustment.</li>
<li>There are positive and negative emotions.</li>
<li>Positive emotions are love and joy.</li>
<li>Negative emotions are fear, anger, anxiety, jealousy and sorrow.</li>
<li>Due to long effect of motions can cause bodily diseases such as essential hypertension, peptic ulcer and asthma.</li>
<li>Frustration and conflicts cause stress and tension.</li>
<li>Stress causes illness to the individual and the individual shows or exhibit some signs of behavior.</li>
<li>Stress and illness may cop up by means of self defense mechanism, which protects us from diseases.</li>
<li>Ego defense mechanism is to protect our ego and relive the tension and over come the failure feelings and maintain inner harmony.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="questions">Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<li>What is the importance of emotions?</li>
<li>How the individual can express the emotions and it can be controlled?</li>

<p>191 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-iv">UNIT - IV<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-iv" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="groups-teams-and-leadership">GROUPS TEAMS AND LEADERSHIP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#groups-teams-and-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Duties of the health worker include working individual, families and various groups in the community, and working with others in the health team. For this work she needs the following skills.</p>
<ol>
<li>Inter-personal skills</li>
<li>Team work, and leadership.</li>
<li>Obtaining information.</li>
<li>Motivating the community for change.</li>
<li>Group dynamics.</li>
<li>Promoting leadership.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="inter-personal-skills">Inter personal skills :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inter-personal-skills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When you have started understanding yourself (self- awareness) and when you feel ok, comfortable with your self, accepting your self, then you are ready to develop good relations with others. This is most important for the health worker who needs to work with people, each of them a person with thoughts, feelings and potential to grow.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="1-appreciation">(1) Appreciation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-appreciation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is a basic need, a hunger of every person. When someone makes a remark to you of appreciation or praise, such as "You spoke so well at the meeting", how could you feel! when you stroke a pet cat it will purr with pleasure. In psychology we use the word 'stroking' to mean taking notice of another person. You should practice giving strokes to other people and see the effect on them. Don't flatter and overdo it however. Be sincere when you praise.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="2-recognition">(2) Recognition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-recognition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is another hunger. Speaking to a person, looking into his/her face, and listening to what is said all help a person to feel important, a person of worth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="3-approval">(3) Approval<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-approval" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You can 'stroke' a person by your facial or other expression showing your approval. When behavior is approved, a person gains more confidence. He /she is encouraged to develop talents, or is motivated to greater effort. When you disapprove, you need to be aware that what you say or do may bring harm to that persons ego if it is not done with care. Before you criticize, always give a positive stroke</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="4-receiving-negative-strokes">(4) Receiving Negative strokes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-receiving-negative-strokes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Psychology 192</p>
<p>To be ignored, ridiculed or criticized, is usually painful. Emotions of anger or shame may arise in you. What should you do?</p>
<p>When you receive a negative stroke, be aware of how you feel, but take control of yourself. If you know the person well, you may express your feelings of hurt without emotion and without blaming the other persons. The person then might say ‘I’m sorry’, and you both grow as persons and in relating to one another. If there is no good response from the other person, you could keep quiet and later find outlet for your feelings by some vigorous exercise, or by praying about it.</p>
<p>(5) <strong>Acceptance</strong></p>
<p>Just as we have seen the importance of self acceptance. we need to accept other also as individuals in this world for a purpose. Acceptance means that we do not judge their behavior or appearance. we have no prejudice on account of caste, class, or where they come from. Acceptance means we allow other people to be themselves, and respect each as an individual with right and freedom.</p>
<p>(6) <strong>Under standing</strong></p>
<p>For good understanding, we need to get to know people. We need to be interested in them and sensitive to their attitudes, values, aspirations and needs. We should observe and listen carefully, then respond in a helpful way.</p>
<p><strong>Teamwork and leadership</strong></p>
<p>A team is a group with a certain task, which requires that members of the group help, support and understand each other. A team can be permanent e.g. the health team, in which the health worker function as a member, or it may be a temporary group set up for a special purpose or project.</p>
<p>For good teamwork the members need to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Feel they each belong to team spirit.</li>
<li>Grow in understanding of each other, and knowledge of each person’s role.</li>
<li>Be able to contribute to the achieving of common goals.</li>
<li>Participate freely and openly in face-to-face discussion.</li>
<li>Co-operate and co-ordinate activities.</li>
<li>Accept one another, support one another, and trust one another.</li>
</ol>
<p>193 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>The basic tasks of a team are to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Decide on policy, set goals, and plan.</li>
<li>Solve problems.</li>
<li>Evaluate progress and goal achievements.</li>
<li>Resolve conflicts among themselves. Conflicts of ideas and views can be used for better results if all have the will to work together. The health worker should be able to manage, or lead a team such as the VHGs, Dais, Depot holders and other volunteers in a village or group of villages.</li>
</ol>
<p>The leader of a team should try to:</p>
<ol>
<li>Make sure the goals are clear to everyone.</li>
<li>Make sure that each one knows what others are doing.</li>
<li>Find out the talents of members.</li>
<li>Promote a good team spirit. Avoid domination by one person. The leader should set an example in listening and working together step by step. Everyone should contribute.</li>
<li>Be sensitive to tension, and encourage members to share feelings and to accept one another even if opinions differ.</li>
<li>Be sensitive to time, and see that useful work is done.</li>
<li>Be prepared to accept mistakes, learn from them, and try again.</li>
<li>Be flexible, prepared to make changes, but keeping the goals in mind.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="obtaining-information">OBTAINING INFORMATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#obtaining-information" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The health worker works with the community with the goal of promoting health and wholeness. She needs to be well informed, and aware of various ways of obtaining information. Here are some guides - lines:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Take note of instruction from your authorities.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Keep up to date with trends and new discoveries.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Add to your knowledge and experience by meeting and mixing with people, by attending conferences, seminars and workshops, by listening to radio etc.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Get to know your community. Student health workers may discover a great deal about the community by making weekly visits to 8 or 10 families in different locations and getting to know these families. Observe, listen and try to find out the following:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>What groups and social activities are there? Who are leaders? Who has power, and why?</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Psychology
194</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>
<p>Altitudes of people towards other groups. How far do different groups understand each other / Are they prepared to work together for the benefit of the whole community?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Resources of the community; land (whose is it?) and food sources, animals and poultry, water supply, buildings, schools, roads, and transport, people with skills, health care resources, work opportunities, and earnings in relation to cost of living. What rate of interest to poor people have to give for loans?</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Family nutrition and health, beliefs, customs and habits related to health and family welfare.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>What do people feel are their priority needs?</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="motivating-the-community-for-change">MOTIVATING THE COMMUNITY FOR CHANGE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#motivating-the-community-for-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The health worker will find that differences of caste, education customs, values and attitudes cause conflicts so that people will not work together easily. The main causes of conflict may be identified as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Power, control and Attitudes of the Rich</li>
</ol>
<p>The rich own the land, decide how much (or how little) wages will be paid, control the water supply (often denying use of wells by Harijans). They may not realize how the poor are suffering, why they get more and more into debt and into a worse state of poverty and poor health.</p>
<p>The motives of the rich are usually related to looking after their own interests, and so it is best to keep things as they are and not to bring changes.</p>
<p>A few of the rich do care about the poor. They are fair, generous and sympathetic. The health worker should stimulate such persons to find out causes of poverty and poor health, and raise questions to motivate others too in this interest and concern.</p>
<p>Rich people too, should be made aware that for better health and well being of the whole community, the poor need to be well represented in committees and encouragement to participate fully.</p>
<p>They should realize the right to dignity and self-respect of poor people, and that they need encouragement to find the way to freedom and self-reliance. Then their children will become well-adjusted and useful members of the society.</p>
<p>195
Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>The Condition and Attitudes of the Poor</li>
</ol>
<p>Poor people are used to hunger, sickness, and deaths in their families. They struggle to survive, and become more and more dependent on aid such as free food supplies. The women work hard in the fields for much less than men receive. For months there may be no work. Loans are taken at a high rate of interest, which they can never repay, so they lose their property.</p>
<p>The poor usually have a low self-image. Their attitude may be one of apathy or despair. They have no hope that things will improve for them. Some may become angry and join a political party, or become delinquent.</p>
<p>Role of the Health Worker</p>
<p>The health worker must try by all means, to motivate individuals (especially community leaders), families and groups, to change unhelpful attitudes and habits, also to work together for the health and well-being of all. The basic need is to work towards social equality, and unity.</p>
<p>The health workers main goal should be to enable people to self-reliant and have control over their health and their lives.</p>
<p>Motivation may be by means of -</p>
<ol>
<li>Good communications, using all different methods</li>
<li>Example, e.g. a community near by where changes are seen.</li>
<li>Rewards and incentives. These give pleasure and encouragement.</li>
<li>Aspiration and goal achievement.</li>
<li>Satisfactory results.</li>
</ol>
<p>The community should never feel entirely satisfied however, but go on changing and moving on to achieve new goals.</p>
<p>GROUP DYNAMICS</p>
<p>When people come together for a meeting or group discussion, it can be very helpful or not, depending on how the group functions. It is helpful when it functions as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>The group is not too large and everyone sits in a circle including the leader.</li>
<li>Everyone is welcomed and introduced.</li>
<li>The group elects a leader or chairman. Also if required a recorder.</li>
<li>The leader introduces the subject with few words and starts the discussion, then lets others talk.</li>
</ol>
<p>Psychology 196</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Every one is encouraged to ask questions, share thoughts and experiences, and make suggestions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>No one dominates the discussion. The leader controls those who talk too much and encourages the silent ones to contribute.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The leader tries to keep a calm and friendly atmosphere, using interpersonal skills and humor if this will help (but never laugh at people, only with them).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If visual aids are used this often helps to make the issues clear, e.g. ideas can be noted down on a blackboard.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When there has been enough discussion, the leader asks the group to drop conclusion or to make a discussion on the action to me taken—what action by whom, where, and how.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After the meeting, what has been decided on is carried out and reported on at the next meeting of the group.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The health worker should try to sensitive to the needs of each member of the group. If there are some who seem afraid to speak, it may be better to divide up into smaller groups, then come together again to share in the big group.</p>
<p>Whatever activities have been decided upon, the health worker should try to see that facilities are provided for carrying them out, and that group members take up their responsibilities.</p>
<p><strong>PROMOTING LEADERSHIP:</strong></p>
<p>There are three kinds of leadership:</p>
<ol>
<li>When the leader is boss?</li>
</ol>
<p>The leader plans, decides, direct and controls the program of action. The group submits and carries out order but with not much interest. The work output is very low. The program is only supporting the leader’s ego.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>When the leader is guide?</li>
</ol>
<p>The leader asks the group question, and may accept some of their suggestion. The group has some influence and makes minor decisions, but is up to the level of the leader’s ability.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>When the leader is stimulator?</li>
</ol>
<p>The leader educates the group for active participation and control. The role of leader rotates as members of the group show ability. The group controls and evaluates the program, and becomes responsible. The work output is well</p>
<p>197 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>above what the leader expected.</p>
<p>If the health worker has a superior attitude and is always telling people what to do, no leadership will be developed. The health worker should not always lead. She should be prepared to follow the lead of others. The aim of good leader is to promote leadership qualities so that the program will be carried on when she is not there, and the community becomes self-reliant.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="helping-in-times-of-stress">Helping in Times of Stress<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#helping-in-times-of-stress" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The health worker may frequently be required to help an individual or a family in coping with stress. This too is a health care activity for which the health worker student needs to acquire qualities and skills, which she can use herself and develop in other in the community. It can be called psychological support, emotional support, a helping relationship, or counseling.</p>
<p>The health worker needs to realize that 'being a helper in times of stress' is not the same as psychotherapy. Psychotherapy is long-term treatment of those with severe emotional problems or mental illness, by a psychotherapist. Counseling is also not giving guidance, but is helping normal people to adjust better to stress, in a shorter times than psychotherapy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="identifying-stress-situations">IDENTIFYING STRESS SITUATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#identifying-stress-situations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The health worker should visit as early as possible any family in her area in which there is a stress or crisis situation. Do not wait to be called, as these families are at high risk for mental health.</p>
<p>Examples of stress situation are as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Where a person is dying or has died, especially if the person is father or mother of young children, or a previous baby.</li>
<li>Suicide or attempted suicide.</li>
<li>Where a newborn baby has some abnormality or a girl when a boy was wanted.</li>
<li>Wife or husband had deserted the family, or a girl has eloped (run away with her lover).</li>
<li>A person has had an accident or operation involving loss of a limb, breast or genital organs.</li>
<li>A person has been diagnosed as having disease such as leprosy, or cancer.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="basic-approaches">BASIC APPROACHES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#basic-approaches" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fr. Joe Currie in the barefoot counselor describes two</p>
<p>Psychology 198</p>
<p>different approaches of the helper.</p>
<ol>
<li>Dispensary (directive) Approach</li>
</ol>
<p>This kind of helper feels he knows what the problem is and know how to deal with it. He dispenses what he thinks is the cure, but those with emotional hurts are not cured in the way that those with physical ailments may be .he will find that it is not so easy, and that different skills are needed in order to help the person with mental stress.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Non-directive Approach</li>
</ol>
<p>This kind of helper knows that he should be a listener. The one in need of help is relieved that someone is willing to listen while he tells of his difficulties. This helper is trying to really understand the person and to know how he feels. He accepts him and cares about him. He does not counsel nor offer a solution. He may come to accept himself and gain confidence to go on and find his way through his difficulty.</p>
<p>It has been found that counseling helps some people, and some are harmed. Success seems to depend on the qualities and behavior of consoler (helper).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="conditions-for-a-helping-realtionship">CONDITIONS FOR A HELPING REALTIONSHIP<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conditions-for-a-helping-realtionship" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Person to person deep relationship, and sharing of feelings is necessary between helper and helper (the one needing help). They are two people at work. They should meet each other at eye level, linked by the fact that both are persons. Status in life does not matter at this time. It is essential that what be said is kept confidential.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Lack of integration of the helpee</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The helpee is unhappy, defensive, anxious and confused. He is not able to accept himself, not accepting others, and not accepting his present situation. He feels uncomfortable, not ok. He finds it difficult to think of other things and to make decisions.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Better integrations of the helper</li>
</ol>
<p>The helper feels OK, and in better. Control of his feelings than the helpee. He is aware of his feelings, accepts them, and can reveal them to other if and when it is appropriate.</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Listening and Responding</li>
</ol>
<p>199 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>These are the two most basic skills required by the helper. It is not easy to listen with full attention and awareness. Not only that, but the helper should take note of how it is said -what feelings go with what is said? Watch for non-verbal message - facial expression and gestures, and tone of voice.</p>
<p>Responding should relate to the full message given by the helper, both the words and the mood or emotions. The helper's listen and respond to each understanding.</p>
<p>Further the helper has empathy. He is willing to set aside his own self temporarily to enter into the experience of the helper. This does not mean that the helper has to feel the same way as the helper, but he should understand how the helper is feeling. An important question to keep to the present is How do feel now?</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Acceptance</li>
</ol>
<p>The helper has deep respect for the helper as a person of value, without regard to his behavior, thoughts and feelings. Acceptance does not mean agreement. The helper does not ask the helper to be like him, but to be his own true self. With this kind of acceptance, personal growth of the helper can be expected.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Communicating</li>
</ol>
<p>The helper communicates to the helper his warmth and concern, by means of his attitude, concentration and verbal responses. The message he conveys is I am with you -may be I can help you.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-helping-process">THE HELPING PROCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-helping-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The helper needs to be able to change in two directions.</p>
<ol>
<li>To wards Greater Confidence</li>
</ol>
<p>He should move from negative to positive feelings. He needs to re-discover himself as a person of worth and of abilities, even with his limitations. He needs to regain self-acceptance, tolerance or others, and hope that something can be done.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Towards seeing a way forward, from a position of conflict and confusion to insight and decision.</li>
</ol>
<p>The first direction is concerned with his feelings, and the second with his understanding. The directions the helper takes during the interview will depend much on the helper's sensitivity to his needs.</p>
<p>Psychology
200</p>
<p>The helper may feel as though he is in a dark tunnel with no way out. His negative feelings, of being 'not ok' are a block to his understanding.</p>
<p>The helper should try to communicate to the helper that he accepts him, to go along with him to find that way.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="stages-of-the-helping-process">Stages of the Helping Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-the-helping-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>(1) Rapport - forming a close relationship by means of recognition, acceptance and warmth on the part of the helper. The helper should put aside his own problems and needs for this time, and concentrate on the other's needs in a relaxed way.</p>
<p>(2) Un folding of the Problem</p>
<p>The helper, knowing he has the full attention of the helper, feels secure ding, the helper concentrates on the person, as being more important than the problem. As the helper tries to understand his feelings, the helper is encouraged to make efforts to understand him and to get to the root of his problem.</p>
<p>(3) Release of Negative Feelings</p>
<p>At first the helper was full of negative feeling such as inadequacy, anxiety, anger or resentment. The helper respects all of the feelings of the helper and helps him to express them. The helper accepts the helper as he is with all his negative feelings. As he beings to accept him, the helper loses most if not all of those feelings.</p>
<p>(4) Encouragement of Positive Feelings</p>
<p>The helper begins to see a more positive self, reflected in the helper's respect for him. Having regained his self - esteem, he feels more comfortable with himself and with the helper.</p>
<p>(5) Growing Confidence to Explore New Ways</p>
<p>The helper, by now feeling in a closer relationship with the helper develops hope that may be there is a way forward. They now work together on a search for root causes and new directions.</p>
<p>(6) Confrontation and Sorting out</p>
<p>At this stage, when the helper has full confidence in his genuine concern, the helper may point out something he seems to be hiding or avoiding. He asks the helper to explore this, and together they sort it out.</p>
<p>(7) Insight and Decision</p>
<p>Gradually new insight and possibilities emerge as the helper</p>
<p>201 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>and helper work together. The helper may by now have a clear idea of what action he can take, and confidence to carry out the plan. He knows too, that he can come again to the helper for evaluation and if necessary to renew their search for a better way.</p>
<p><strong>THE HELPER’S CODE – WHAT TO AVOID AND WHAT TO DO?</strong></p>
<p>What the Helper should avoid?</p>
<ol>
<li>A quick solution</li>
<li>Probing the problem</li>
<li>Long narratives, and past history</li>
<li>Complaints against another (for this, joint counseling is needed)</li>
<li>Advising, judging and moralizing</li>
<li>Over reassuring, supporting, or protecting</li>
<li>Over identifying, feeling with the helper</li>
<li>Talking too much yourself</li>
<li>Trying to impress</li>
<li>Continuing counseling when there is no progress</li>
<li>Being bored, irritable, impatient or hostile</li>
<li>Breaking confidence</li>
</ol>
<p>What the Helper should try to do?</p>
<ol>
<li>Be yourself, and be relaxed</li>
<li>Concentrate and listen to full message (non-verbal also)</li>
<li>Respond in a way that will best help</li>
<li>Communicate interest, warmth and understanding</li>
<li>Accept, and appreciate the other</li>
<li>Confront if and when necessary with sensitivity</li>
<li>Help to sort out and clarify the problem</li>
<li>Help the other to be responsible and independent</li>
</ol>
<p>Psychology
202</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The health worker who needs to work efficiently, she should know about the appreciation, recognition, approval in social relations, acceptance of the individual etc.</li>
<li>When she has to work with team, she should maintain good relation with the team.</li>
<li>The team and the team leader should maintain the group dynamics.</li>
<li>The leader must act as boss, a guide and a stimulated to the group</li>
<li>Health worker should identify the stress situation.</li>
<li>Prepare a role-play on power in the community, in order to experience the feeling of different groups.</li>
<li>The various conditions for helping relationships one person to person. Better integration of helper, acceptance, listening and responding and communicating.</li>
</ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-v">UNIT -V<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-v" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-motivation-and-change-in-behavior">Learning Motivation and change in Behavior :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-motivation-and-change-in-behavior" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Motivation is a keyword in psychology. It is an inner force which drives an individual to a certain action. It also determines human behavior motivation may be positive (carrot) or negative (stick). Without motivation behavioral changes cannot be expected to take place. Positive motivation, is often more successful than negative motivation. Motivation is not manipulation. A motivated person acts willingly and knowingly. The terms motives, needs, wants, desires and wages are all used synonymously. These terms are inter related and inter dependent.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="kinds-of-needs-and">Kinds of Needs and<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kinds-of-needs-and" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is difficult to define human needs. There are many kinds of needs and</p>
<p>(1) Biological Needs :</p>
<p>These are biological needs. A hungry man needs food, a thirsty man water, a sick man medicine. There are also physiological needs such as the need for sleep, rest, recreation and fresh air. The nurse should be aware of these needs in the day - to - day care of the points.</p>
<p>(2) Social Needs :</p>
<p>The need for company, the need for love and affection, the need for recognition, the need for education, the need for social states are social needs.</p>
<p>(3) Economic Needs :</p>
<p>Economic security, that is security from want is one which every one desires.</p>
<p>(4) Ego - integrative Needs :</p>
<p>The desire for prestige, power and self - respect come in this category.</p>
<p>Motivation is contagious, it spreads from one motivated person to another. We make use of motives and in actives in community health work. Motivation of eligible couples for a small family is an important activity in the national family welfare program. Motivation is required to English peoples participation in community health work.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="change-in-behavior">Change in behavior :<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#change-in-behavior" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Human behavior is result of physical and mental factors interacting acts other. They are knowledge, beliefs, values, attitudes, skills, finance, materials, time and the influence of family members, friends, co - workers, opinion leaders and even health worker.</p>
<p>The behavior can be changed by some factors such as follows 13</p>
<p>Psychology</p>
<p>Envtal stimuli like sight, smell, touch reach the cerebral cortex
Through home impulses. The information received is assembled
And evaluated by a set of another impulses the cerebral
Cortex orders the behavior of the individual. This is known as conscious
Behavior. It is the behavior determined by the standards or expectations
Of the society.</p>
<p>Emotions and feelings behavior may be changed by our feelings and emotions. These are arise from with in the body. When we say a person is blind with rage or paralyzed with fear, we mean that he is a victim or captive to his own emotions. Ex. Thus effect behavior the seat of primary emotion.</p>
<p>Eg. Anger, joy, hunger is the thalamus in the brain. It is the under control of cerebral cortex. If the central cortex influence is removed for eg. When an enjoy to cerebral cortex occurs, the persons behavior may be affected</p>
<p><strong>NEEDS:</strong>
The individual behavior can be changed by his needs, wants, driver and urges are used synonymously.
Motivation: Motivation is an inner force with driver and an individual to a certain action with ant motivation, behavior al changes cannot take place</p>
<p><strong>Intellectual perception:</strong>
A person's individual perception, thinking and reasoning can change the behavior of an individual in a given situation. That is why each individual behavior in ways a which makes sense to him.</p>
<p><strong>Incentives and goals</strong>
Goals are the same as aims in life. People who do not have an aim or goal in life do not feel inclined or motivated to do anything. Some people are very ambition provide a strong motive for action. There is a difference between an incentive and motives.</p>
<p>Incentive exists outside the individual e.g. food is an incentive for a hungry man. Prize is an incentive for a scholar. Incentives are among the factors that stimulate motivation and encourage specific behaviors. Incentives are either intrinsic or extensic, material or psychological self determined or selected by others. An intrinsic incentive is the benefit that comes from solving ones</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>own problems. Extensive incentives are rewards that do not relate directly to the goal towards which the desired behavior is aimed, for e.g. financial compensation of individuals undergoing stylization operations for family planning. Material incentives are tangible goods or services, psychological incentives include the satisfaction, self-esteem, or enhanced capabilities gained through a proposed course of action.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aspirations">Aspirations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aspirations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An aspirations is a high aim, longing or ambition. When a person aims to high he may be disappointed and suffer frustration. Our aspirations should be realistic.</p>
<p>Leader may produced due to aspirations. Some who aspire to be great may be come very selfish and hostile to others.</p>
<p>The best kind of aspirations is seen in a person who has no selfish motive but who wants only to serve others to the best of his ability. A health worker student who has this kind of aspiration will be highly motivated to learn, to develop her talents and the skills she will need. In additions in fulfilling the aim of service, she will find an inner peace and satisfaction which is the best reward for such service.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="attitudes">Attitudes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#attitudes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Attitudes are acquired characteristics of an individual, there are more less permanent ways of behaving. An attitudes includes three components</p>
<p>(a) A cognitive or knowledge element
(b) An affective and feeling element
(c) A tendency to action</p>
<p>An attitudes as been defined as a relatively enduring organization of beliefs around an object, subject or concept which pre-dispose one to respond in some preferential manner.</p>
<p>Attitudes are not learnt from text books, they are acquired by social interaction, e.g. attitude towards person, things, situations all issues (e.g. government policies, program all administrative measures). It has been truly said that attitudes are caught, and not taught. Once formed attitudes are difficult to change.</p>
<p>Psychology
206</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="habits">Habits:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#habits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Habits is an accustomed way of doing things, habits are accumulated through generation emerge as customs all custom in turn, exited habits. Habits are formed perfect all influence human behavior habits are said to have 3 characteristics</p>
<ul>
<li>They are acquired through repetition</li>
<li>They are automatic and</li>
<li>They can be performed only under similar circumstances. Habits once formed persist and influence human behavior.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="habit-formation">Habit formation:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#habit-formation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Habits are formed. they are of many kinds e.g. habit relating to food, sleep, work, smoking, intake of drugs and alcohol etc. they are both good and bad habits.</p>
<p>Good habits promote health. Bad habits like drug dependence may ruin health. There fore cultivate of good habits is desirable. The principles involved in habit formation are</p>
<ol>
<li>Habit formation should begin early in childhood, when the child has not yet formed any habit and is receptive to all influences.</li>
<li>Habits are formed by frequent repetition</li>
<li>Time taken to form habits. They can not be formed over night</li>
<li>There should be a strong emotional stimulus to form habits e.g. taking a vow, reward, recognition etc.</li>
<li>Good habits kill bad habits the best way to brake bad habits in to cultivate good habits</li>
</ol>
<p>Habits build up human personality. Man should not become a slave to his habits, he should remain a master. It is the job of the psychological to find out how good habits can be developed and bad one eliminated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning">LEARNING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Learning is necessary for mains survival and for human progress.</p>
<p>Learning is defined as any relative permanent change in behavior that occurs as a results of practice or experience. It means acquiring so nothing new knowledge, new techniques, new skills, new fears, new experiences</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>Learning is necessary for man's survival and for human progress. It includes not only acquiring knowledge but also skills and formation of habits and development of perception. Learning depends largely upon intelligence. Learning also depended upon motivation and motivation depends on the need students fear to learn. Learning is a continuous process. It is both conscious and unconscious.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="conditions-affecting-learning">Conditions affecting learning<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#conditions-affecting-learning" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Intelligence: - Learning depends upon the intelligence or mental faculty of an individual. It involves the activity of sensory adjustment all motor mechanisms and the body. The mental faculty is related to heredity, nutrition and IQ. children with low IQ are poor learners, they may not learn at all</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Age :- The curve of learning reaches its peak between 22to25years of age. After the age of 30, there is short delaine. It has been appropriately said one can not teach to an old person with new learning abilities.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Learning situations:- Physical facilities for learning or institutions, teachers, text books, audio visual aids promote learning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Motivation:- In order to learn effectively, there must be adequate motivation. Some of the powerful motives are encouragement, praise, reward and success. These are stimulate learning.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Physical health:- A physically handicapped person e.g. deaf, dumb, chronically sick can not learn properly.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mental health:- Worries, anxieties and fears interfere with learning.</p>
</li>
</ol>
