<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-ix">UNIT-IX<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-ix" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="social-stratification">Social stratification:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#social-stratification" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is the horizontal division of society into higher and lower social units. These divisions called social strata include the caster and class groups. It is the division of society into permanent groups or categories</p>
<p>Linked with each other by the relationship of superiority and subordination. Some individuals and groups are rated higher than other on the basis of opportunities and privileges that they enjoy.</p>
<p>For eg In India doctor and engineers are rated higher than teachers. Status and role, economic and political groups are also factors in social stratification.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="caste">Caste:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#caste" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a collection of families or group of families bearing a common name, membership of which is hereditary, imposing on its members certain restriction in matter of social interaction. It is a hereditary type of social group. The Hindus social order is based on the caste system. Membership is by birth. The group or caste has a common name and traditional occupation. The members have to marry with in their own group, or else be treated as outcaste. The rules about food and drink are very strict.</p>
<p>The society is divided into various caste with a well developed life of their own. The status of a person does not depend on his wealth but on the traditional importance of the caste in which he had born. Status is determined not by vocation but by birth.</p>
<p>There are regular caste councils to regulate and control the conduct of all caste members. Their rules over all caste members work powerfully which keeps the people in their proper places.</p>
<p>In our society, the classes are divided from high, low. Thus Brahmins in India stand at the apex of the social ladder. Because they are produced from the purest pant of the supreme i.e. from the mouth. So a Brahmin is entitled to whatever exists in the world. The whole world is his property. Others live on his charity. The speech uttered by Brahmins never fails to</p>
<p>Sociology</p>
<p>come true. In contrast high position enjoyed by Brahmins the sudras was subject to lowest they are untouchables with they could not use the public roads or public well.</p>
<p>Member of the first these classes must not travel the company of sudras. If sudras violate the rules, they may under in go sever punishments. Ever the well is polluted if a low Carte man draws water from them. The public schools did not admit impure caste. Sudan could not study the scared literature.</p>
<p>A person born in a Caste remains in it for life and dies in it. Members of a particular caste are expected to follow the caste occupation. They can't change to other occupation. Generally the impure castes are made to live on the outskirts of the city.</p>
<p>The lowest and most depressed groups are known as "scheduled castes". To help them up the social ladder, they are given opportunities and reservations in education and jobs. There is an "unsociability offences Act" to control the ill-treatment of untouchables.,</p>
<p><strong>Social class:</strong></p>
<p>It is one or two or more broad groups of individuals who are ranked by the members of the community, in socially, superior an inferno position. The members of the upper class are master and their made of dress typing way of recreation with expenditure are high</p>
<p>Where as the members of lower class are servants and mode of lining is manual labor.</p>
<p>In modern communities wealth is the primary determinant of social stratification there is an intimate relating between the social close and the occupation, which indicates the mode of life and general social standing. The members of class poser's common interests, they're brought into consciousness by the need of defense against the common enemy.</p>
<p>Social class a social class is a section of a community different from other sections because of social status. Social status may be because of birth (e.g. royalty in U.K. or Nepal) or race. In the modern society social status may be related to an of the following: income, occupation, education, political power, economic power, or religious power. Those who share a common status unite in a social class, and they feel belong in that class.</p>
<p>The 'upper class' includes those with greater wealth and prop</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>erty. Besides status, they often have power over the 'lower' class, and power may be mis-used. The poor are exploited and become still poorer. There is a gap between the rich and the poor, which is becoming wider.</p>
<p>The 'middle class' in Indian society is growing in size and strength. This is a strata between the upper and lower classes. It is based on economic factors and includes doctors, college professors, business managers, office workers and factory workers. A middle-class consciousness and culture is developing in modern India.</p>
<p><strong>Mobility:</strong></p>
<p>People in society continue to move up and down the status scale is called social mobility. It is to be distinguished from migration which is movement in geographical space.</p>
<p>Mobility has been classified as Horizontal mobility, Vertical mobility. Horizontal mobility's refers to change of residence or job with out status change. E.g. transfer of teacher from one school to another.</p>
<p>Vertical mobility refers to movement in any or all of the three areas of living class occupation and power. Mobility may be down ward or upward.</p>
<p>This term can mean a change in social status, or a change of place, e.g. from rural to urban area. In India today, large numbers of rural people migrate to the cities. They go in search of work, or to beg in order to live. If an 'untouchable' goes to live in the city, he gets away from the depressed social status he had in the village. If he finds a way to earn money he may move up from 'low class' to 'middle classes.</p>
<p>Suppose a Brahmin moves from his village to the city. He will probably lose the superior social status he had before. In the urban community there is much more social mobility than in the rural community.</p>
<p>Independent India has adopted the principles of equality, freedom and justice. The Government planning and legislation are slowly bringing about social change. Education and the influence of foreign cultures, also politics and inter-group conflicts are other reasons for social change and social mobility.</p>
<p>For example, when a certain social group accepts Family Planning the smaller number of children get a better education, and later some may get top positions in society. In this way a</p>
<p>Sociology</p>
<p>whole group may move up in social status.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="social-status">Social Status:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#social-status" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a social position that determines for its possessor, apart from his personal and social services, a degree of respect, prestige and influence. It refers to individuals. Total standing in society the individuals ones respect by virtue of his social status.</p>
<p>Status means the position of an individual in the group, or community. Status may be because of age, sex, caste, class, occupation, marriage or achievements. For example, the elders in the family and in the community are usually respected. By his own ability and efforts, a person may achieve status and respect.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="patterns-of-leadership">Patterns of leadership<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#patterns-of-leadership" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Leadership is found in every society. The society can be divide into (a) the leaders and (b) the followers.</p>
<p>A leader is one who leads a group of people. The leader has influence or power over the group.</p>
<p>It is said that leaders are "born". Heredity does seem to be one factor, but there are others such as development of character and good personality. Socialization is important in development of leaders.</p>
<p>Effective leadership depends partly on the people who are the followers. Some want strong leaders who dominate (authoritarian type). Others want leaders who allow for independence (democratic type). The Health Worker should realize that the power of leaders may be used for good or for evil. The leader can use power based on love and good relationships, or based on fear.</p>
<p>A really good leader identifies (is one with) the group., and enables them to plan and take group action to bring about change for the better. Thus he heaps to make the followers also into leaders.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="in-a-community-we-find-the-following-kinds-of-leaders">In a community we find the following kinds of leaders:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#in-a-community-we-find-the-following-kinds-of-leaders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Formal Leaders</li>
</ol>
<p>i Official- those employed by Government, including the village Sarpanch, schoolteachers, post-masters, tax-collector etc. Their leadership goes with the post, and may be only temporary (they may be transferred).</p>
<p>239 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>These leaders may or may not enjoy the respect of the community.</p>
<p>i Functional - those elected or appointed to be leaders of non-Governmental organizations such as co-operative societies, Youth Clubs and Mahila Mandals.</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Informal Leaders</li>
</ol>
<p>i Natural leaders - those with influence in the village, who may be housewives, dais, or shop-keepers etc.</p>
<p>i Status leaders - those who are respected and have the confidence of the people because of age, caste, religion, wealth or education.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Opinion leaders</li>
</ol>
<p>Opinion leaders are those who would be able to help in promoting and supporting community health and development programmers. We need leaders who are convinced about the need and the valued of the programmers, and who also have qualities of leadership which can be developed. Some of the formal and informal leaders may have the right qualities and motivation and could be used. Other people too, such as those who have accepted family planning methods and are satisfied, may make good leaders for promoting the F.P. programmed.</p>
<p>The opinion leaders should be identified by health Workers, and training camps arranged for orientation in health and family welfare programmes.</p>
<p>It is important for success of community health and development programmes, for the team (including FHWs and MHWS) to get the confidence of the community leaders from the start. These leaders can help a great deal to bring about the needed changes. On the other hand, if they are not convinced about a programmed they can cause it to fail.</p>
<p>Community leaders should be involved in</p>
<p>Sociology
240</p>
<p>the planning, implementing and evaluating of programmers for health and family welfare in their villages. This is vital for the programmed to be effective, and to be 'of the people, by the people, and for the people'.</p>
<p><strong>Regionalism:</strong></p>
<p>This refers to different areas where the population has a distinct culture, or a common language, or political outlook. For example, within India some neighboring states may join together in presenting their needs and demands to the central government. Countries of South Asia may unite in order to voice the opinion of the region at meetings of the united Nations Organization.</p>
<p>Regionalism can be harmful and lessen unity if the people of one state or language try to control an area and refuse rights to others.</p>
<p>The community feeling with in a region is called regionalism. It gives man a feeling of others with his fellows and with the earth they share. It involves a cultural wholeness. The fundamental aim of regionalism is the closer integration of the rural civilization and urban civilization. It is the development of an integrated large community with in the city and country.</p>
<p><strong>Family:</strong></p>
<p>It is a system of relationships existing between parents and children's. It is a group of persons whose relations to one another's are based upon consanguinity and therefore retrofire relation to another.</p>
<p><strong>Functions of the family:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The regulation of sexual behavior and reproduction.</li>
<li>Care and training of children.</li>
<li>Co-operation and division of labor.</li>
<li>Primary group satisfactions.</li>
<li>It also helpful for socialization, race perpetration.</li>
</ul>
<p>Regulation and satisfaction of sex needs with economic func-</p>
<p>241 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>tions.</p>
<p>The functions of family are affectional, economic, recreational, protective, religious and educational.</p>
<p><strong>The Modern Family:</strong></p>
<p>The Modern family has ‘decreased control of the marriage contract. Women in modern family have attained an increasing degree of economic independence. In modern family the woman is not the devotee of man, but an equal partner in life with equal rights. It is a smaller family. It is no longer a joint family. It is scular in attitudes.</p>
<p><strong>Types of Families:</strong></p>
<p>a. The Nuclear Family, of father, mother and children. By tradition, father is the earning member and mother stays at home to care for the family. In a modern family these roles may change. When mother has a better job and earns more than father, there is often conflict, and children become insecure and may become delinquents.</p>
<p>b. The Joint Family consists of a number of married couples and their children who live together in the same household. If it is a matriarchal family (as in Kerala) the bridegroom comes to the bride’s home and the senior female of the household is the head of the family. In a patriarchal family, the wife has to stay in her husband’s home and her social status is very low. There are often problems related to dowry and property.</p>
<p>c. Three Generation Family, in which young couples continue to live with their parents and have their own children.</p>
<p><strong>Joint Family:</strong></p>
<p>The family has a joint property and every person has his share in it since the time he is born. The earnings of all the members are put in a common fund out of which family expenses are met. The uses of joint family are</p>
<ul>
<li>It sues economic progress.</li>
<li>Division of labor secures the advantages.</li>
<li>It secures economy of expenditure.</li>
<li>It provides opportunity for leisure.</li>
<li>It provides social insurance.</li>
<li>Avoids fragmentation of holdings.</li>
<li>Demerits are finders the development of personality</li>
<li>Leads of quarrels</li>
</ul>
<p>Sociology</p>
<ul>
<li>Encourages litigation</li>
<li>Privacy denied.</li>
<li>Unfavorable accumulation of capital.</li>
<li>The joint families are disintegrated due to industrialization.</li>
<li>Extension of communications with transport.</li>
<li>Decline of agriculture and village trades.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Marriage:</strong></p>
<p>Marriage is an institution which admits adult’s men and women to family life. It is a stable relationship and in which men and women is socially permitted to have children. The right to have children implying the right to several relations.</p>
<p><strong>Types Of Marriages are:</strong></p>
<ol>
<li>Polyandry in which one wife having many husbands.</li>
<li>Fraternal polyandry—One wife is regarded the wife of all brothers who have several relation with her.</li>
<li>Polygon—One husband in having two or many wives at a time.</li>
<li>Monogamy—One man marries are woman at a time.</li>
<li>Experimental marriage: Two people before they settle down to a life of permanent union. A man and woman may be allowed to lead matrimonial life temporarily in order to find out if they can settle down permanently or not.</li>
<li>Companionate marriage: This is the marriage of two persons on the understanding. If there are no children, the marriages may be dissolved by mutual consent.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>THE FAMILY—STRICTIRE AMD ACTIVITIES</strong></p>
<p>The family is not an organized group. Members are joined into a group because of marriage and kinship. They are related to one another, share the family home, and a common kitchen. The family begins with marriage.</p>
<p>In most families there is one man to one woman; this is monogamy type of society. Polygamy (two or more wives) is practiced in some societies, e.g. Muslim.</p>
<p>They way in which man and woman come together (mate) also varies. In India it is usual for the elders or parents to arrange the marriage of their children. Usually the couple must be of the same religion and caste. It is also the tradition in India for elder sisters to be married first, then brothers.</p>
<p>243 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>In Modern society, often there are ‘love marriages’, in which the man and woman marry their own choice of partner. This type may be interacts, even inter-racial marriage.</p>
<p>In some societies, marriage is a social contract, in others a religious sacrament. Registration of the marriage makes it legal. If the marriage breaks up. One or other partner may get a divorce.</p>
<p>Broken marriages have a very bad effect on the children, and are not good for the society. We should do all we can to help in keeping good relationship between husbands and wives. This is most important for the total family and community welfare.</p>
<p>In India the marriages are between any two Hindus. It based on exogamy i.e. consanguinity marriages.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Social stratification is the horizontal division of society into “higher and “lower” social units.</li>
<li>Caste – it is a collection of families or group of families bearing a common name, membership is hereditary.</li>
<li>Class is one or two more broad groups of individuals. Whom do the members of the community in socially superior or inferior position rank.</li>
<li>Mobility is movement of the people continuously from ups and downs</li>
<li>Social status is a social position of the individuals in the group or community.</li>
<li>A good leader identified the group</li>
<li>Regionalism is a common feeling with in a region.</li>
<li>Family is a system of relationship existing between parents and children.</li>
<li>Marriage is an institution which admits men and women to family life.</li>
</ul>

<p>Sociology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="unit-x">UNIT - X<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-x" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The community is a territorial group with shares a common soil as well as shared way of life. People living in the same locality come to have a distinctive community life. The community is more than the locality it occupies. It is also sentiment. The people living at a common place and leading their levies in one another's company come to develop "we - feeling". They share common memories and traditions, customs and institutions. Today none of us belong to one inclusive community. Under modern conditions attachment to local community is decreasing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-community">Types of community:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are two types</p>
<ol>
<li>Rural Community</li>
<li>Urban Community</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="1-rural-community">1. Rural Community:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-rural-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this people living close to and well acquainted with each other. There are immediate contacts between the neighbors in a village.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-village-community">Characteristics of village Community:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-village-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It has several facts: the important ones are the following</p>
<ol>
<li>The village people have a sense of unity. The relationship between people is intimate. They personally know each other structurally and functionally the village is a unit.</li>
<li>In the village, people assist each other and thus they have close neighborhood relations.</li>
<li>In the village still there is joint family system is retains. The agricultural occupation requires the cooperation of all the family members.</li>
<li>The People in the villages have deep faith in religion and duties.</li>
<li>The village people lead a simple life. They are simple plain people believing a god.</li>
<li>Their behavior is natural and not artificial. They live in life. They are free from mental conflicts. They are hard working the level of moralities is high. Social crimes are very rare. Their life is governed by norms.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="changes-in-the-village">Changes in the Village:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#changes-in-the-village" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ancient village community was a very small group of ten or twenty families.</p>
<p>245 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>The feeling of familiarity was so great that if a child wandered of from the home. The parents had nothing to worry because there are numerous relatives in the village. They laid a common property. Due to lack of communication and transport the members of the community were separated due to distance.</p>
<p>In the medieval village community so many changes. The keen ship did not played for a long time to bend people. The land is belongs to king and the slave with masters.</p>
<p>The modern village community, there is a rise of industrialism. Now urban group began to dominate civilization. Urbanization is increased with dominant rural social forms have been changing. Rural people follow the urban forms of life. Kinship bond is broken due to increased size and mobility of population.</p>
<p>Land is no longer cultivated jointly. They continue to work the land but then try to live in the mode of the city. Rural social forms are changed due to urbanization. By the large the rural way of life has been writhing away.</p>
<p><strong>2. Development of Rural community:</strong></p>
<p>The nation’s Five Year Plans for development are mainly for improving life in rural communities. Development of the people themselves is most important for success. There needs to be:</p>
<p>a. Social preparation of the community. The health and development personnel will need to get know, understand, and work with the people. The people need to feel it is their own programme for their own better way of life.</p>
<p>b. Co-operation between B.D.O. staff, the health team, community leaders and the people themselves, to find out the community problems and needs. If possible, community members should be used for data collection (survey).</p>
<p>c. Planning with the community. It is best to select first programme which will cost little and bring quick results, e.g. kitchen gardens for better nutrition, or an anti-fly campaign to lessen the problem of diarrhea and dysentery.</p>
<p>d. On-going Community leaders’ meeting, for further planning, implementing (carrying out the programmers) and evaluating (how useful is the programme?).</p>
<p>For health programmers, the role of the Health Worker is to</p>
<p>Sociology</p>
<p>assist the committee, provide technical information and training, and stimulate to action.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="3-major-rural-problem">3. Major Rural Problem:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-major-rural-problem" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. Health problems, the most common being: Malnutrition, especially in under - five year children. Communicable diseases and infection. Too many child deaths and maternal deaths. A home accident especially burns and scalds.</p>
<p>b. Education - the problems of illiteracy, child labor, school dropouts, too few teachers (one teacher schools), also lack of equipment, buildings too small or in need of repair etc.</p>
<p>c. Transport and communications - lack of good roads, especially in rainy season, causes problems of supplies, marketing and taking the sick to hospital etc. The problem of villages being cut off from other communities and urban facilities, results in slow progress and development.</p>
<p>d. Agriculture - the farmer may have problems such as insufficient water supply, especially in failure of monsoon, electricity cuts, and repair of pump-sets, tractors etc. Delay in getting supplies of seed, fertilizers, especially if he has n capital reserves.</p>
<p>Labor problems - laborers may not be available when needed, or coolly demands are high.</p>
<p>Procurement price given by Government may be too low, or demand for products is low.</p>
<p>Sickness and death of flocks and herds (sheep and cattle).</p>
<p>e. Population and employment - Agriculture can no longer provide enough for the growing population in rural areas. Some rural communities have taken up handloom weaving or other small industries, but these are not without many problems. Young men leave the village for urban areas in search of jobs. Sometimes whole groups of families migrate to a distant place to work for a contractor (building, mining and other project). They get advances from the contractor to buy food, and soon may become 'bonded laborers' and never get bat to their own village.</p>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="urban-community">Urban Community:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#urban-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is indicates fashionable living, wide acquaintance with things and people and political manner of speech. It limited note only to urban, slowly extended to rural people also. Every village possesses some elements of the city while every city carries some features of the village.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="development-of-urban-community">Development of Urban Community:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#development-of-urban-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>City develops according to whatever resources available there. In ancient times these resources were available by the people. Slavery forced labor, taxation by the ruling are main factors for development of urban community. The extension of mans power over nature is a primary condition of the modern growth of cities and city population.</p>
<p>Industrialization and urbanization has also been greatly stimulated by the new techniques of production associated with industrial revolution. The invention of production associated with industrial revolution. The invention of machinery the department of steam power and to work in the factories, many people from village are abandoned to urban. Industrialization has stimulated city development, trade and commerce. Ancient civilizations cities grew wherever goods were good and commercial transactions were carried. Due to development of transport with communications, the facilities can be transported and develop urban community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="economic-pull-of-the-cities">Economic pull of the cities:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#economic-pull-of-the-cities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cities can provide more opportunity for personal advancement than rural areas. Employment opportunism are more in the city. Even businessman comes to the city from the village to avail of better opportunities for making higher profits. Education and recreational facilities and amusement theatres are available in cities which contribute the urban community growth.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="characteristics-of-urban-community">Characteristics of Urban community:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#characteristics-of-urban-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Home lessens are a disturbing feature of city community.</li>
<li>Energy and speed are the traits of a city. The people work at a speed, day and night which stimulate other to work.</li>
<li>People indulge in too many activities. Cities are consumers of population.</li>
<li>Facilities for preserving health such as hospitals and medical specialist are many and excellent.</li>
<li>City has more heterogeneous than the village. It is most</li>
</ul>
<p>Sociology</p>
<p>favorable breeding ground of new biological and cultural hybrids. The personal traits, the occupations, the cultural and the ideas of the members of the urban community vary widely. Class extremes characterize urban community. In a city, the people rolling in luxury and living, in grand mansion as well as people live in pavements. The best forms of ethical behavior and the worst racketeering are both to be bound in cities.</p>
<ul>
<li>Superior creativeness and chronic unemployment are alike the city is the home of opposites.</li>
<li>The home problem in a big city is very acute.</li>
<li>The meddle class have insufficient accommodation the child doesn't get any play space.</li>
<li>The city dwellers treats the strangers he meet as animated machines tater than as human beings.</li>
<li>They meet with speak with out knowing each other's name.</li>
<li>A citizen may live for several years in a city and may not know the names of one-third of the people who live in the same city area.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="2">
<li>Urban Adjustments Life is quite different in towns and cities than in the village. Traditions, customs and modes do not have much influence over those living in urban areas. Family life is less disciplined, and there is no community support. There is much more mixing among people of very different backgrounds. This brings about changes in habits and attitudes. Family conflicts are common.</li>
</ol>
<p>For the individual's, and for families coming to live in the urban area, conscious efforts need to be made to form good friendships and to live in harmony with others. There are many opportunities for joining social groups for various activities.</p>
<p>People need to take up the challenge for forming a new 'community' even in the city, for mutual help and action to solve problems.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Urban Problems The main urban problems may be listed as follows:</li>
</ol>
<p>a. Growth of slums and in the number of pavement dwellers.
b. Lack of employment, leading to poverty, under-nutrition, disease, and anti-social activities.</p>
<p>249 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>c. Failure of people to adjust, causing mental illness or delinquency.</p>
<p>d. Crime and delinquency, begging and prostitution.</p>
<p>e. Overcrowding in dwellings, buses and streets.</p>
<p>f. Failure in administration (e.g. public services such as refuse collection and disposal) to cope with the rapid growth of the population.</p>
<p>g. Road accidents.</p>
<p>h. Health problems due to overcrowding and to stress of urban living.</p>
<p>i. Political and industrial unrest and conflicts.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="social-and-economic-change-in-communities">SOCIAL AND ECONOMIC CHANGE IN COMMUNITIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#social-and-economic-change-in-communities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-influence-change">What influence change?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-influence-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The following are some causes for change in communities:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Industry and technology of modern life. New machines and new methods of doing things are continually being introduced.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Introduction of different cultures and new attitudes and values e.g. because of rural - urban interaction.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Population growth: This brings the need for more food production, schools, houses and jobs, and leads to struggle and corruption in the keen competition.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Inter-group conflicts, e.g. between labor and owner, between the 'haves' and 'have-nots' (class conflicts) between tribal and not-tribal populations, between low castes and upper castes and between youth and the elders of society. Such conflicts sooner or later bring about change.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>women's movements: Greater freedom of women and more equality of sexes, leads to changes in family life and norms of society.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Political forces: The desire of people to share in decision-making is growing. Political power can bring changes in laws.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Government plans and programmers for health and development. Planning is directed towards social change.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="organizing-the-community-for-change">Organizing the Community for Change<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organizing-the-community-for-change" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>An important task of the Health Worker is to assist</p>
<p>Sociology</p>
<p>the community in organizing itself for change.</p>
<p>Inspire of 30 years of planned development, the rural poor are still poor. Most of the babies are born into a world of hunger, illiteracy, disease, oppression injustices and a struggle for existence. This section of the community needs out special attention. They need to be helped:</p>
<ol>
<li>To benefit from employment or to be trained for self-employment in the rural community itself.</li>
<li>To get useful employment or to be trained for self-employment in the rural community itself.</li>
<li>To develop leadership, in order to fight for justice.</li>
</ol>
<p>The section of the community whose needs are less basic, also need to be helped to adjust to the changes of the modern age. This section needs to be made more aware of the injustices and struggles of the poor. Migration to the cities should be stopped, by introducing more variety of occupations in the rural areas. Simple technologies for processing of crops, milk and meat production, and small-scale manufacturing, would provide work for more people. Help is needed to form co-operative.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-change-affects-community-development-and-health">How change affects community development and health?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-change-affects-community-development-and-health" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>a. Political Forces Through political struggles, the oppressed sections of society strive to bring a change in their situation. If these forces become violent, development is hindered. There is much destruction of properties, injuries and perhaps loss of life. Bitter feelings may continue for a long time, and there is suffering for many. Such things are a set-back to health and development programmes.</p>
<p>There needs to be change, but we should strive for peaceful change by democratic means and not by violent revolution.</p>
<p>b. Socio-economic Forces The modern world is full of a variety of material things, and the changing culture has a deep effect on people. There is confusion and conflict. Often there is a break-down of former traditions and values, of family life and caste. Poor health both</p>
<p>251 Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<p>mental and physical, result.</p>
<p>Poor people are tempted to buy things like transistor radio, or</p>
<p>Tinned baby foods, when they do not have enough to eat. They get things on credit and cannot pay back. The little bit of land they may have inherited has to be sold, debs pile up to the pint of despair, and sometimes suicide.</p>
<p>In spite of land reforms and movements, even more land has gone into the hands of the few landlords. Rural development programmers seem to help these landlords more than they help the landless poor. The poorest section seems unable to benefit from schemes such as cottage industries. The free medicines of the health services are not much help to poor people who have no money even for food.</p>
<p>Health workers need to be a bridge to link these helpless poor with sources of development and welfare programmers so that their basic needs can be met. There needs to be much more education of the people in making better use of their resources, e.g. simple nutritious diet, use of simple remedies in sickness, and avoiding debts due to spending on family functions and religious festivals.</p>
<p>Both in the urban and in rural communities, people need help in adjusting to the changes of modern life. People need to understand what will really help to bring to birth a happy, healthy way of life for all. The Health worker in community has a vital role to play in bringing about these changes for the better.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="gathering-information-about-our-communities">Gathering Information About Our Communities<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gathering-information-about-our-communities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="health-statistics">HEALTH STATISTICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-statistics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Health statistics are facts and figures which reveal the state of health of the community. Sickness and death, population, housing, lands, nutrition, social and economic factors, environment etc. are all important in measure g the health of the community.</p>
<p>Health statistics are collected by means of the following:</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Census: Every 10 years this is taken. Each person’s age, sex, marital status, birth place, religion, literacy, occupation and other information are collected on national level.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Registration of births, deaths and marriages. These are called vital statistics, or vital events (see chapter 2).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Notification of communicable diseases (see chapter 8)</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Sociology</p>
<ol start="4">
<li>Records of the Health center ad hospital.</li>
<li>Health survey.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="registration-of-vital-statistics">REGISTRATION OF VITAL STATISTICS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#registration-of-vital-statistics" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The registration of vital statistics is not satisfactory at present. Many births and deaths are not reported, and there are often mistakes in the data. The system of collection of vital statistics needs to be improved.</p>
<p>The Health worker can influence the community to bring about some improvements as follows:</p>
<ol>
<li>Educating the community about the importance of registration and getting correct certificates of births, deaths and marriage.</li>
<li>Parents should produce a certificate of birth before a child is admitted to school.</li>
<li>Appointment of the secretary of the Gram Panchayat as the local Registrar.</li>
<li>The Registrar should send the data on to the proper authority without delay, and records kept up-to-date. A village record should show family wise records of vital evens.</li>
<li>Officers of the Health Department may be encouraged to inspect the records.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A community is a territorial group, which shares a common soil in the same locality.</li>
<li>In rural community the people are living close to and well acquainted with each other.</li>
<li>The main change in rural community is land is not cultivated jointly.</li>
<li>The development of rural community in co-operation with planning of social organizations. Major problems are health, education and agricultural problems.</li>
<li>Urban community is more fashionable, wide range of opportunities and employment and industrialization.</li>
<li>Homelessness is a disturbing facture of city community.</li>
<li>Growth of slum, crime, road accidents and unemployment are major problems.</li>
<li>There is a vast change in socially and economically in urban communities.</li>
</ul>
<p>Community Health Nursing -I</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="questions">Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="glossary">Glossary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glossary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Abdomen - stomach, the part of the body cavity</p>
<p>Abduction - to move a limb a part from the body</p>
<p>Abrasion - a minor wound in which the surface of the skin or mm is worn away</p>
<p>Acute - severe symptoms with brief duration.</p>
<p>Adduction - move a limb towards the body.</p>
<p>Aerobic - requiring free oxygen for life and growth.</p>
<p>Albumin - protein that is soluble in water.</p>
<p>Albuminuria - presence of albumin in urine.</p>
<p>Anaerobic - growth of micro - organism without oxygen</p>
<p>Anesthesia - loss of feeling of sensation.</p>
<p>Antibiotic - the substance that derived from micro - organisms, that destroys or inhabits the growth of micro - organism.</p>
<p>Anticoagulant - an agent that prevents the clotting of blood.</p>
<p>Antipyretic - a chemical that destroys the growth of disease causing bacteria and other micro - organism.</p>
<p>Anuria - absence of urination.</p>
<p>Apnea - absence of respiration.</p>
<p>Arrhythmia - deviation from the normal rhythm of the heart.</p>
<p>Ascites - abnormal accumulation of the fluid in the abdominal cavity.</p>
<p>Auscultation - the process of listening with the aid of stethescope, produced by movement of gas or liquid with in the body.</p>
<p>Aspirate - process of the withdrawal of fluid from the body by means of aspirator.</p>
<p>Bacteria - a group a micro - organism that do not have nucleus</p>
<p>255</p>
<p>and cause diseases.</p>
<p>Brady cardia - slowing the heart rate.</p>
<p>Catheter - a tube for insertion into a narrow opening of the body.</p>
<p>Chronic - prolonged or far a long time.</p>
<p>Colon - large intestine.</p>
<p>Coma - loss of consciousness or state of unconsciousness.</p>
<p>Congestion - an accumulation of blood with in an organ.</p>
<p>Conscious - state of consciousness or arousal.</p>
<p>Constipation - a condition in bowel avaculation occur infrequently.</p>
<p>Contaminate - unhygienic</p>
<p>Crisis - sudden decrease of body temperature or the turning point of a disease.</p>
<p>Cyanosis - change of body into blue due to lack of oxygen.</p>
<p>Debility - Fatigue</p>
<p>Decubitus ulcer - ulcerated area of skin caused by irritation and continues press on part of the body.</p>
<p>Defecation - process of passing bowel or motion.</p>
<p>Deficient - Any disease caused by lack of an essential nutrient in the diet.</p>
<p>Dehydration - loss of water in body tissues.</p>
<p>Depressant - An agent that reduces the normal activity of the body system or function.</p>
<p>256</p>
<p>Dermis - The second layer of the skin, which is under epidemics.</p>
<p>Detoxification - The process where by toxic substance are removed</p>
<p>Diabetes mellitus - Increased blood sugar due to decreased production of insulin in the body.</p>
<p>Diagnosis - The process of determining the nature of the disorders</p>
<p>Diarrhorea - Lose motions.</p>
<p>Distal - A part from the center of the body.</p>
<p>Distention - Accumulation of body due to fluid or gas.</p>
<p>Diuretics - The drug, which increase urination.</p>
<p>Dyspnea - Difficulty in breathing</p>
<p>Edema - Swelling of the body due to increased accumulation of fluid in the tissues.</p>
<p>Electrolytes - The liquid, which contains minerals</p>
<p>Emesis - Expulsion of food or fluid from the stomach by vomit</p>
<p>Epidermis - Upper layer of the skin</p>
<p>Evaporate - Change of fluid into gas</p>
<p>Exhalation - Expelled air from lungs</p>
<p>Feces - Bowel or motion</p>
<p>Flatters - Gas present in the intestine</p>
<p>Flexion - Bending of the body part</p>
<p>Fracture - Discontinuation of the bone</p>
<p>257</p>
<ul>
<li>Gastric - Pertaing to stomach</li>
